Title: Building Safety Act 2022
Date: 2024-11-04
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2022/30

## Building Safety Act 2022

                                                   B e it enacted  by the
Queen’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the advice and consent of the
Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this present Parliament
assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Introduction

#### Overview of Act

1

1.1

This Act has 6 Parts, and contains provisions intended to secure the safety of
people in or about buildings and to improve the standard of buildings.

1.2

Part 2  contains provision about the building safety regulator and its
functions in relation to buildings in England.

1.3

Part 3  amends the Building Act 1984.

1.4

Amendments made by  Part 3 —

1.4.a

provide that the regulator is the building control authority in relation to
higher-risk buildings in England, and

1.4.b

require the regulator (for England) and the Welsh Ministers (for Wales) to
establish and maintain registers of building control approvers and building
inspectors.

1.5

Part 4  is about occupied higher-risk buildings in England, and imposes duties
on accountable persons.

1.6

Part 5  contains further provisions, including—

1.6.a

provisions about remediation and redress;

1.6.b

provision requiring a new homes ombudsman scheme to be established;

1.6.c

powers to make provision about construction products;

1.6.d

further provision about fire safety;

1.6.e

provision about the regulation of architects;

1.6.f

provision about housing complaints.

1.7

Part 6  contains general provisions.

### The regulator and its functions

#### The regulator and its general functions

##### The building safety regulator

2

2.1

In  this Part  “ the regulator ” means the Health and Safety Executive.

2.2

Schedule 1  contains amendments of provisions of the Health and Safety at Work
etc Act 1974 that relate to the regulator.

##### The regulator: objectives and regulatory principles

3

3.1

The regulator must exercise its building functions with a view to—

3.1.a

securing the safety of people in or about buildings in relation to risks
arising from buildings, and

3.1.b

improving the standard of buildings.

3.2

In exercising a building function (other than an excepted function), the
regulator must have regard to the following principles—

3.2.a

regulatory activities should be carried out in a way which is transparent,
accountable, proportionate and consistent, and

3.2.b

regulatory activities should be targeted only at cases in which action is
needed.

3.3

The duty in  subsection (2)  is subject to any other requirement affecting the
exercise of the function.

3.4

In  subsection (2)  “ excepted function ” means—

3.4.a

a function under any of sections 4 to 6, or

3.4.b

a function of the regulator under the Health and Safety at Work etc Act 1974
so far as relating to any such function.

3.5

In  this Part  “ building function ” means—

3.5.a

any function of the regulator under, or under an instrument made under, this
Act or the Building Act 1984;

3.5.b

any prescribed function of the regulator;

3.5.c

any function of the regulator under the Health and Safety at Work etc Act 1974
so far as relating to a function within  paragraph (a)  or  (b) .

##### Duty to facilitate building safety: higher-risk buildings

4

4.1

The regulator must provide such assistance and encouragement to relevant
persons as it considers appropriate with a view to facilitating their securing
the safety of people in or about higher-risk buildings in relation to building
safety risks as regards those buildings.

4.2

The assistance and encouragement that must be provided under subsection  (1)
includes, in particular, assistance and encouragement with a view to
facilitating securing the safety of disabled people in or about higher-risk
buildings in relation to building safety risks as regards those buildings.

4.3

For this purpose “ relevant persons ” means—

4.3.a

residents of higher-risk buildings within the meaning of  Part 4 ,

4.3.b

owners of residential units in such buildings,

4.3.c

persons who are accountable persons within the meaning of  Part 4 , and

4.3.d

persons upon whom duties are imposed by virtue of paragraph 5B of Schedule 1
to the Building Act 1984 (dutyholders).

4.4

In subsections  (1)  and  (2) —

“ building safety risk ” has the meaning given by section 62; “ disabled ”:
see section 30; “ higher-risk building ” means— a higher-risk building within
the meaning of  Part 4  (see section 65), or a higher-risk building within the
meaning of the Building Act 1984.

4.5

Parts 3  and  4  confer further functions on the regulator in relation to
higher-risk buildings.

##### Duty to keep safety and standard of buildings under review

5

The regulator must keep under review—

5.a

the safety of people in or about buildings in relation to risks as regards
buildings, and

5.b

the standard of buildings.

##### Facilitating improvement in competence of industry and building inspectors

6

6.1

The regulator must provide such assistance and encouragement as it considers
appropriate to—

6.1.a

persons in the built environment industry, and

6.1.b

registered building inspectors,

with a view to facilitating their improving the competence of persons in that
industry or members of that profession (as the case may be).

6.2

For the meaning of “the built environment industry” and “registered building
inspector” see section 30.

##### Proposals and consultation relating to regulations

7

7.1

This section applies to regulations under—

7.1.a

this Part , or

7.1.b

any provision of  Part 4  except section 62, 65 or 68.

7.2

The regulator may at any time make proposals to the Secretary of State for the
making of regulations.

7.3

Before making a proposal, the regulator must consult such persons as it
considers appropriate.

7.4

Before making regulations, other than regulations proposed by the regulator,
the Secretary of State must consult—

7.4.a

the regulator, and

7.4.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

##### Duty to establish system for giving of building safety information

8

8.1

The regulator must make arrangements for a person to establish and operate a
voluntary occurrence reporting system.

8.2

A “voluntary occurrence reporting system” is a system to facilitate the
voluntary giving of information about building safety to the person who
operates the system.

#### Committees

##### Building Advisory Committee

9

9.1

The regulator must exercise its powers under section 11A(3) of the Health and
Safety at Work etc Act 1974 to establish and maintain a committee to be known
as the Building Advisory Committee, with the following function.

9.2

That function is to give advice and information to the regulator about matters
connected with any of the regulator’s building functions except its functions
relating to the competence of—

9.2.a

persons in the built environment industry, and

9.2.b

registered building inspectors.

9.3

The Building Regulations Advisory Committee for England, established under
section 14 of the Building Act 1984, is abolished.

##### Committee on industry competence

10

10.1

The regulator must exercise its powers under section 11A(3) of the Health and
Safety at Work etc Act 1974 to establish and maintain a committee concerned
with the competence of persons in the built environment industry (“industry
competence”), with the following functions (and any other function that the
regulator considers appropriate).

10.2

The functions are—

10.2.a

monitoring industry competence;

10.2.b

advising the regulator in relation to industry competence;

10.2.c

advising persons in the built environment industry in relation to industry
competence;

10.2.d

facilitating persons in the built environment industry to improve industry
competence;

10.2.e

providing guidance to the public (or a section of the public) about ways of
assessing the competence of persons in the built environment industry;

10.2.f

carrying out analysis and research in connection with a function mentioned in
any of  paragraphs (a)  to  (e) .

##### Residents’ panel

11

11.1

The regulator must exercise its powers under section 11A(3) of the Health and
Safety at Work etc Act 1974 to establish and maintain a committee with the
functions mentioned in this section (and any other function that the regulator
considers appropriate).

11.2

The committee is to consist of—

11.2.a

such residents of higher-risk buildings as the regulator considers
appropriate, and

11.2.b

such relevant persons (if any) as it considers appropriate.

11.3

The regulator must take all reasonable steps to ensure that the committee
includes—

11.3.a

one or more residents of a higher-risk building who are disabled,

11.3.b

a body that represents, supports or promotes the interests of any description
of disabled people that includes residents of higher-risk buildings, or

11.3.c

a member of a body within paragraph  (b) .

11.4

The committee is to give advice to the regulator about such matters connected
with the regulator’s building functions and relating to higher-risk buildings
as the regulator may specify.

11.5

The regulator must consult the committee before issuing or revising any of the
following—

11.5.a

guidance to residents of higher-risk buildings about any of their rights or
obligations under  Part 4  or regulations made under that Part;

11.5.b

guidance relating to any duty under regulations made under section 89 to give
information or documents to residents of higher-risk buildings or owners of
residential units in such buildings;

11.5.c

guidance relating to any of sections 91 to 93 or 95 or regulations made under
any of those sections (engagement with residents etc, and residents’ duties).

11.6

If the committee has not been established at a time when the regulator has
prepared guidance to which  subsection (5)  applies—

11.6.a

that subsection has effect as if it did not require the committee to be
consulted before the guidance is issued, and

11.6.b

the committee must be consulted in relation to the issued guidance as soon as
reasonably practicable.

11.7

See also—

11.7.a

section 17 (3)  (duty to consult committee about regulator’s strategic plan);

11.7.b

section 94 (2)  (duty to consult committee about regulator’s complaints
system).

11.8

In this section—

                                    “ higher-risk building ” has the same
meaning as in  Part 4  (see section 65);
“ relevant person ” means—
an owner of a residential unit in a higher-risk building,
a body that represents, supports or promotes—
the interests of any description of residents of higher-risk buildings or
owners of residential units in such buildings, or
the interests of any description of persons that includes a description of
such residents or owners, or
a member of a body within paragraph (b).

##### Committees: power to amend or repeal

12

12.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend or repeal any of  sections 9
to 11  (provision about specific committees).

12.2

But regulations repealing section 9, 10 or 11 may be made only if the
regulator has made a proposal to the Secretary of State for the making of such
regulations (as to which see section 7(2)).

12.3

Regulations under this section may make consequential amendments of this Act.

#### Staffing etc

##### Local authorities and fire and rescue authorities: assistance etc to regulator

13

13.1

A relevant authority may at the request of the regulator do anything for the
purpose of—

13.1.a

facilitating the exercise by the regulator of a relevant function, or

13.1.b

enabling the relevant authority to facilitate the exercise by the regulator of
a relevant function.

13.2

The regulator may, for a purpose mentioned in  paragraph (a)  or  (b)  of
subsection (1) , direct a relevant authority to do anything specified in the
direction.

13.3

The direction may specify the way in which, and the time by which, the thing
is to be done.

13.4

A direction—

13.4.a

may be given only if the regulator considers that it is expedient for the
authority to do the specified thing, and

13.4.b

must state how, in the regulator’s opinion, the doing of the thing will
facilitate the exercise of a relevant function or enable the authority to
facilitate that exercise.

13.5

A direction may be given only with the consent of the Secretary of State.

13.6

Before giving a direction, the regulator must—

13.6.a

make a written request under  subsection (1)  for the authority to do the
thing, and

13.6.b

have regard to any written representations made by the authority in the period
specified in the request.

13.7

A request under  subsection (6) (a)  must—

13.7.a

state that the regulator may seek consent to give a direction under this
section if the request is not complied with,

13.7.b

state how, in the regulator’s opinion, the doing of the thing will facilitate
the exercise of a relevant function or enable the authority to facilitate that
exercise, and

13.7.c

specify a reasonable period for the authority to make any representations as
to why it should not do the thing requested.

13.8

In this section—

                                    “ relevant authority ” means a local
authority or fire and rescue authority;
“ relevant function ” means—
a function of the regulator relating to—
the regulation of higher-risk buildings (within the meaning of the Building
Act 1984 or  Part 4  of this Act), or
higher-risk building work (as defined by  section 91ZA  of the Building Act
1984), or
in the case of a local authority, a function of the regulator relating to the
regulation of any work for which the regulator is the building control
authority by virtue of  section 91ZB  of the Building Act 1984.

13.9

A direction or consent under this section must be in writing.

##### FSO authorised persons: assistance etc to regulator

14

14.1

An FSO authorised person may at the request of the regulator do anything for
the purpose of—

14.1.a

facilitating the exercise by the regulator of a relevant function, or

14.1.b

enabling FSO authorised persons to facilitate the exercise by the regulator of
a relevant function.

14.2

In this section—

                                    “ FSO authorised person ” means a person
authorised as mentioned in article 25(1)(e) of the Regulatory Reform (Fire
Safety) Order 2005;
“ relevant function ” means a function of the regulator relating to—
the regulation of higher-risk buildings (within the meaning of the Building
Act 1984 or  Part 4  of this Act), or
higher-risk building work (as defined by  section 91ZA  of the Building Act
1984).

##### Provision of assistance etc: supplementary

15

15.1

This section supplements sections 13 and 14.

15.2

A relevant authority must ensure that any of its staff involved in providing
relevant assistance to the regulator have the appropriate skills, knowledge,
experience and behaviours.

15.3

For this purpose “ relevant assistance ” means anything done by the authority
pursuant to a request or direction, for the purpose of facilitating the
exercise by the regulator of a relevant function.

15.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the
reimbursement by the regulator of expenditure incurred by relevant authorities
in complying with requests or directions.

15.5

The Secretary of State may pay a relevant authority such amount as the
Secretary of State considers appropriate in respect of things done by the
relevant authority in complying with a request or direction.

15.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision in relation
to requests and directions, including in particular provision about—

15.6.a

things done by a relevant authority in connection with a request or direction;

15.6.b

things done by an FSO authorised person in connection with a request.

15.7

In this section—

                                    “ direction ” means a direction given
under section 13;
“ FSO authorised person ” has the meaning given by section 14;
“ relevant authority ” has the meaning given by section 13;
“ relevant function ” has the meaning given by section 13;
“ request ” means a request made under section 13 or 14.

##### Guidance about the provision of assistance

16

16.1

The regulator may issue guidance to—

16.1.a

relevant authorities about their functions under section 13;

16.1.b

FSO authorised persons about their functions under section 14.

16.2

The regulator may revise or withdraw any issued guidance.

16.3

A relevant authority must have regard to any guidance under this section when
exercising its functions under section 13.

16.4

An FSO authorised person must have regard to any guidance under this section
when exercising their functions under section 14.

16.5

Guidance under this section may be issued, revised or withdrawn only with the
consent of the Secretary of State.

16.6

In this section—

                                    “ FSO authorised person ” has the meaning
given by section 14;
“ relevant authority ” has the meaning given by section 13.

#### Plans and reports

##### Strategic plan

17

17.1

The regulator must—

17.1.a

prepare a strategic plan, and

17.1.b

submit it to the Secretary of State for approval.

17.2

A “strategic plan” is a plan setting out how the regulator proposes to carry
out its building functions in the period to which the plan relates.

17.3

Before submitting it, the regulator must consult—

17.3.a

the committee mentioned in section 11 (residents’ panel), and

17.3.b

such other persons as the regulator considers appropriate.

17.4

The Secretary of State may approve the plan, with or without modifications.

17.5

Before approving the plan with modifications, the Secretary of State must
consult the regulator.

17.6

The regulator must publish the approved plan, and act in accordance with it.

17.7

The first plan—

17.7.a

must be submitted as soon as reasonably practicable after this section comes
into force, and

17.7.b

must relate to a period ending with the third 31 March to occur after the day
on which it is submitted.

17.8

If the committee mentioned in section 11 has not been established at the time
the first plan is prepared—

17.8.a

subsection (3)  has effect as if it did not require the committee to be
consulted before the plan is submitted, and

17.8.b

the committee must be consulted in relation to the first approved plan as soon
as reasonably practicable.

17.9

Any other plan—

17.9.a

must be submitted before the end of the period to which the most recent
approved plan relates (“ the current period ”), and

17.9.b

must relate to the period of three years, or such other period as the
Secretary of State and the regulator may agree, beginning immediately after
the end of the current period.

##### Revised strategic plans

18

18.1

This section supplements section 17.

18.2

The regulator may at any time in the period to which a plan relates—

18.2.a

prepare a revised plan relating to the remainder of that period (or to such
other period as the Secretary of State and the regulator may agree), and

18.2.b

submit it to the Secretary of State for approval.

18.3

The Secretary of State may at any time during the period to which a plan
relates require the regulator to submit a revised plan for approval.

18.4

Where such a requirement is made, the revised plan—

18.4.a

must be submitted as soon as reasonably practicable, and

18.4.b

must relate to the remainder of the period to which the current plan relates
(or to such other period as the Secretary of State and the regulator may
agree).

18.5

Section 17 (3)  to  (6)  apply in relation to a revised plan.

18.6

If approved, the revised plan replaces the current plan.

18.7

In this section—

“ current plan ” means the first plan mentioned in  subsection (2)  or  (3)
(as the case may be); “ plan ” means a strategic plan as defined by section
17.

##### Annual report about information provided under mandatory reporting requirements

19

19.1

As soon as reasonably practicable after the end of each financial year, the
regulator must prepare and publish a report about the information provided to
it during that year pursuant to the mandatory reporting requirements.

19.2

For this purpose, information is provided pursuant to the “mandatory reporting
requirements” if it is provided under—

19.2.a

section 87 (duty of accountable person to report to regulator), or

19.2.b

any provision of building regulations that is prescribed by the regulations
for the purposes of this section.

19.3

A report under this section must not contain personal data.

##### Statement of regulator’s engagement with residents etc

20

20.1

The regulator must, at least once each financial year, publish a statement
about its engagement with—

20.1.a

the committee mentioned in section 11 (residents’ panel),

20.1.b

residents of higher-risk buildings,

20.1.c

owners of residential units in higher-risk buildings, and

20.1.d

bodies that represent, support or promote—

20.1.d.i

the interests of any description of residents of higher-risk buildings or
owners of residential units in such buildings, or

20.1.d.ii

the interests of persons including any description of such residents or
owners.

20.2

A statement under subsection  (1)  must, in particular, include information
about the regulator’s engagement with residents of higher-risk buildings who
are disabled.

20.3

A statement under  subsection (1)  may be published by including it in the
regulator’s annual report.

20.4

In this section—

“ annual report ” means the report made under paragraph 10(3) of Schedule 2 to
the Health and Safety at Work etc Act 1974; “ higher-risk building ” means— a
higher-risk building within the meaning of Part 4, or a higher-risk building
within the meaning of the Building Act 1984.

##### Report on certain safety-related matters

21

21.1

Before the end of the period of three years beginning when this section comes
into force, the regulator must—

21.1.a

carry out a cost-benefit analysis of making regular inspections of, and
testing and reporting on, the condition of electrical installations in
relevant buildings;

21.1.b

consider what further provision under the Building Act 1984, or in guidance
under that Act, may be made about—

21.1.b.i

stairs and ramps in relevant buildings,

21.1.b.ii

emergency egress of disabled persons from relevant buildings, and

21.1.b.iii

automatic water fire suppression systems in relevant buildings,

with a view to improving the safety of persons in or about relevant buildings,
and carry out a cost-benefit analysis of the making of that provision.

21.2

Before the end of that period, the regulator must—

21.2.a

prepare one or more reports about the analysis mentioned in subsection (1)
(which may also contain recommendations), and

21.2.b

give them to the Secretary of State.

21.3

The Secretary of State must publish any report received under subsection (2).

21.4

In this section “ cost-benefit analysis ” means—

21.4.a

an analysis of the costs together with an analysis of the benefits that will
arise if the things mentioned in subsection (1)(a) are done or the provision
mentioned in subsection (1)(b) is made, and

21.4.b

an estimate of those costs and of those benefits (subject to subsection (5)).

21.5

If, in the opinion of the regulator—

21.5.a

the costs or benefits cannot reasonably be estimated, or

21.5.b

it is not reasonably practicable to produce an estimate,

the cost-benefit analysis need not estimate them, but must include a statement
of the regulator’s opinion and an explanation of it.

21.6

In this section—

“ electrical installation ” means fixed electrical cables or fixed electrical
equipment located on the consumer’s side of the electricity supply meter; “
relevant building ” means a residential building or any other kind of building
that the regulator considers appropriate.

#### Enforcement

##### Authorised officers

22

22.1

The regulator may authorise a person in relation to specified paragraphs of
Schedule 2  (investigatory powers), for the purposes of any specified relevant
building function.

22.2

A person may be authorised in relation to a paragraph of  the Schedule  only
if they appear to the regulator to be suitably qualified to exercise any power
conferred by virtue of that paragraph or do anything else mentioned in that
paragraph.

22.3

An authorisation—

22.3.a

must be in writing;

22.3.b

may be varied or revoked by an instrument in writing.

22.4

When exercising or seeking to exercise a power conferred by virtue of
Schedule 2 , an authorised officer must if asked produce the authorisation
(including any instrument varying it) or a duly authenticated copy.

22.5

In this section—

                                    “ authorised officer ” means a person in
respect of whom an authorisation under this section is in force;
“ relevant building function ” means any function of the regulator under, or
under an instrument made under—
Part 4  of this Act (higher-risk buildings), or
the Building Act 1984;
“ specified ” means specified in the authorisation.

##### Authorised officers: offences

23

23.1

A person who intentionally obstructs a person who is an authorised officer
exercising a relevant building function commits an offence.

23.2

A person who, with intent to deceive, impersonates an authorised officer
commits an offence.

23.3

In this section—

                                    “ authorised officer ” means a person in
respect of whom an authorisation under section 22 is in force;
“ relevant building function ” has the meaning given by that section.

23.4

A person guilty of an offence under  subsection (1)  is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.

23.5

A person guilty of an offence under  subsection (2)  is liable on summary
conviction to a fine.

##### Provision of false or misleading information to regulator

24

24.1

A person commits an offence if they provide false or misleading information to
the regulator—

24.1.a

in purported compliance with a building enactment or a requirement imposed by
virtue of such an enactment,

24.1.b

in connection with an application made to the regulator under a building
enactment, or

24.1.c

for the purpose of avoiding enforcement action being taken or continued,

and the person knows that, or is reckless as to whether, the information is
false or misleading.

24.2

In this section—

                                    “ building enactment ” means any provision
of, or of an instrument made under—
Part 2  or  4  of this Act, or
the Building Act 1984;
“ enforcement action ” means action taken with a view to, or in connection
with—
securing compliance with a building enactment or a requirement imposed by
virtue of such an enactment, or
the imposition of a sanction in respect of a contravention of any such
enactment or requirement.

24.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

24.3.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

24.3.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both).

#### Reviews and appeals

##### Review by regulator of certain decisions made by it

25

25.1

This section applies in relation to a prescribed decision of the regulator.

25.2

A prescribed person may, before the end of a period prescribed for the
purposes of this subsection, give a notice to the regulator requiring it to
carry out a review of the decision in accordance with this section.

25.3

A notice under  subsection (2)  must—

25.3.a

contain prescribed information,

25.3.b

be in the prescribed form, and

25.3.c

be given in the prescribed way.

25.4

The nature and extent of the review are to be such as appear to the regulator
to be appropriate in the circumstances.

25.5

The review must take account of any representations made, or information
given, by the person at a stage which gives the regulator a reasonable
opportunity to consider the representations or information (and may take
account of any other information).

25.6

On the conclusion of the review the regulator must either uphold or vary the
decision.

25.7

The regulator must notify the person of the outcome of the review and its
reasoning before the end of a period prescribed for the purposes of this
subsection or such other period as may be agreed in writing (“ the relevant
period ”).

25.8

Where the regulator is required to undertake a review but does not notify the
person by the end of the relevant period—

25.8.a

the review is treated as having concluded at the end of that period, and the
regulator is treated as having upheld the decision, and

25.8.b

the regulator must, as soon as reasonably practicable after the end of that
period, notify the person of that fact.

25.9

The decisions that may be prescribed under  subsection (1)  are any decisions
of the regulator under, or under an instrument made under, this Act or the
Building Act 1984 except—

25.9.a

a decision made on an appeal to the regulator, or

25.9.b

a decision to do any of the following—

25.9.b.i

give a compliance notice under section 99 of this Act;

25.9.b.ii

give a notice under section 35B, 35C or 36 of the Building Act 1984 (notices
in respect of contraventions of building regulations etc);

25.9.b.iii

make a disciplinary order under  section 58I  or  58U , or an order under
section 58J  or  58V , of that Act (misconduct of registered building
inspector or building control approver);

25.9.b.iv

give a notice under  section 58Z4  or  58Z5 , or act under  section 58Z6  or
58Z7 , of that Act (contravention of operational standards rules).

##### Right of appeal: requirement for review before appeal

26

26.1

This section applies to a right of appeal against a decision of a kind
prescribed under  subsection (1)  of section 25.

26.2

The right of appeal may be exercised only if the decision has been reviewed
under that section.

26.3

If on the conclusion of the review the decision is varied, the right of appeal
is in respect of the decision as varied (and not the original decision).

26.4

For the purpose of any time limit as regards the exercise of the right of
appeal—

26.4.a

the decision is treated as made on the day on which the review concludes, and

26.4.b

a person is treated as notified of the decision on the day on which they are
notified of the outcome of the review.

#### Supplementary and general

##### Cooperation and information sharing

27

27.1

Schedule 3 —

27.1.a

imposes duties of cooperation on the regulator and other persons, and

27.1.b

confers powers to share information on the regulator and other persons.

27.2

Except as provided by  subsection (3) , the disclosure of information under
Schedule 3  does not breach—

27.2.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

27.2.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

27.3

Schedule 3  does not authorise a disclosure of information if the disclosure
would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, take into account the powers conferred by the
Schedule).

##### Fees and charges

28

28.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision authorising the
regulator—

28.1.a

to charge fees, and

28.1.b

to recover charges,

for or in connection with the performance of a relevant function.

28.2

The regulations may—

28.2.a

prescribe a fee or charge, or

28.2.b

provide for the amount of a fee or charge to be determined by the regulator in
accordance with the regulations.

28.3

The regulations may in particular—

28.3.a

provide that the amount of any charge is to be determined by the regulator in
accordance with a scheme made and published by it, and

28.3.b

make provision about such schemes, including the principles to be embodied in
such schemes.

28.4

The regulations may make provision about the effect of failing to pay a fee or
charge in accordance with the regulations.

28.5

In this section “ relevant function ” means —

28.5.a

any function of the regulator under, or under regulations made under,  this
Part  or  Part 4 , or

28.5.b

any function of the regulator under the Health and Safety at Work etc Act 1974
that is a building function.

28.6

The regulator may—

28.6.a

with the consent of the Secretary of State, provide services to a person in
connection with any matter relating to buildings;

28.6.b

charge fees for such services at a rate agreed with the person.

28.7

Nothing in  subsection (6)  limits any other power of the regulator to charge
for a service provided by it.

##### Service of documents

29

29.1

This section applies to a document required or authorised under this Part or
Part 4 , or regulations under either Part, to be given to a person; but this
is subject to  subsection (11) .

29.2

The document may be given by—

29.2.a

delivering it by hand to the person,

29.2.b

leaving it at the person’s proper address,

29.2.c

sending it by post to the person at their proper address, or

29.2.d

sending it by email to an electronic address at which the person has agreed to
receive documents or has agreed to receive the document.

29.3

The document may—

29.3.a

in the case of a body corporate, be given in accordance with  subsection (2)
to an officer of the body;

29.3.b

in the case of a partnership, be given in accordance with  subsection (2)  to
a partner.

29.4

For the purposes of this section, the “proper address” of a person (except an
authorised officer of the regulator) is—

29.4.a

in the case of a document to be given by or on behalf of the regulator to a
person who has provided an address for service to the regulator, that address;

29.4.b

subject to that—

29.4.b.i

in the case of a body corporate (including a document given to an officer of
the body), the address of its registered or principal office;

29.4.b.ii

in the case of a partnership (including a document given to a partner), the
address of its principal office;

29.4.b.iii

in the case of any other person, their last known address.

29.5

For the purposes of this section, the “proper address” of an authorised
officer of the regulator is—

29.5.a

the address specified by the officer, or

29.5.b

if no address is specified, the address of the regulator’s principal office.

29.6

If—

29.6.a

the document is to be given to the person as the owner of any premises, a
resident of any premises, or the accountable person of a higher-risk building,
and

29.6.b

the person’s name and proper address is not known, despite reasonable steps
having been taken to ascertain it,

the document may be given by addressing it to the owner or resident of the
premises (naming the premises) or the accountable person of the building
(naming the building) and fixing it to a conspicuous part of the premises or
building.

29.7

A document left as mentioned in  subsection (2) (b)  is treated as given when
it was left.

29.8

A document sent as mentioned in  subsection (2) (c)  is treated as given 48
hours after it was sent, unless the contrary is proved.

29.9

A document sent as mentioned in  subsection (2) (d)  is treated as given 24
hours after it was sent, unless the contrary is proved.

29.10

A document fixed as mentioned in  subsection (6)  is treated as given 48 hours
after it was fixed.

29.11

This section does not apply to the giving of a document for which other
provision is made by or under this Part or  Part 4 .

29.12

In this section—

                                    “ accountable person ” has the same
meaning as in  Part 4  (see section 72);
“ agreed ” means agreed in writing;
“ authorised officer ” means a person in respect of whom an authorisation
under section 22 is in force;
“ giving ”: references to giving include similar expressions (such as
serving);
“ specified ” means specified in writing.

##### Interpretation of 

30

30.1

In  this Part —

                                    “ building ” (except in section 28 (6) )
means any permanent or temporary building in England except a building of a
prescribed description;
“ building function ” has the meaning given by section 3;
“ the built environment industry ” means—
persons carrying on, for business purposes, activities connected with the
design, construction, management or maintenance of buildings, and
employees of such persons;
and references to a person “in” the industry are to any such person or
employee;
“ contravention ” includes a failure to comply;
“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act);
“ disabled ”: a person is disabled if the person has a physical or mental
impairment which has a substantial and long-term adverse effect on the
person’s ability to carry out normal day-to-day activities;
“ financial year ” means a year ending with 31 March;
“ fire and rescue authority ” means a fire and rescue authority, within the
meaning of Part 1 of the Fire and Rescue Services Act 2004, for an area in
England;
“ local authority ” means—
a district council or relevant unitary authority,
a London borough council,
the Common Council of the City of London,
the Sub-Treasurer of the Inner Temple,
the Under Treasurer of the Middle Temple, or
the Council of the Isles of Scilly;
“ maximum summary term for either-way offences ”, with reference to
imprisonment for an offence, means—
if the offence is committed before the time when paragraph 24(2) of Schedule
22 to the Sentencing Act 2020 comes into force, 6 months;
if the offence is committed after that time, 12 months;
“ owner ” has the meaning given by section 115;
“ personal data ” has the same meaning as in the Data Protection Act 2018;
“ prescribed ” means prescribed by regulations made by the Secretary of State;
“ registered building inspector ” has the meaning given by section 58A of the
Building Act 1984;
“ the regulator ” has the meaning given by section 2;
“ resident ” and “resident of a higher-risk building” have the same meaning as
in Part 4 (see section 71 (3)  and  (4) (c) );
“ residential unit ” means—
a dwelling, or
any other unit of living accommodation;
“ standard ”: any reference to the standard of a building is to its standard
from a technical perspective.

30.2

In  subsection (1) , in the definition of “local authority”, “ relevant
unitary authority ” means a council for a county in England so far as it is
the council for an area for which there are no district councils.

30.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that in any prescribed
provision of  this Part  a reference to a building includes any of the
following—

30.3.a

any other structure or erection of any kind (whether temporary or permanent);

30.3.b

any vehicle, vessel or other movable object of any kind, in such circumstances
as may be prescribed.

### Building Act 1984

#### Building control authorities and building regulations

##### Higher-risk buildings etc

31

In the Building Act 1984 after  section 120C  (inserted by  Schedule 5 )
insert—

######### Higher-risk buildings etc

########## Meaning of “higher-risk building”: England

31.120D

31.120D.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Act as it applies in relation to
England.

31.120D.2

“ Higher-risk building ” means a building in England that—

31.120D.2.a

is at least 18 metres in height or has at least 7 storeys, and

31.120D.2.b

is of a description specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State.

31.120D.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision supplementing this
section.

31.120D.4

The regulations may in particular—

31.120D.4.a

define “building” or “ storey ” for the purposes of this section;

31.120D.4.b

make provision about how the height of a building is to be determined for
those purposes;

31.120D.4.c

provide that “ higher-risk building ” does not include a building of a
specified description.

31.120D.5

Regulations made by virtue of  subsection (4) (a)  may in particular define
“building” so as to provide that it includes—

31.120D.5.a

any other structure or erection of any kind (whether temporary or permanent);

31.120D.5.b

any vehicle, vessel or other movable object of any kind, in such circumstances
as may be specified.

31.120D.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section (other than
subsection (1)  or  (3)  or this subsection).

31.120D.7

For the meaning of “higher-risk building work” see section  91ZA .

########## Regulations under 

31.120E

31.120E.1

Before making regulations under  section 120D , the Secretary of State must
consult—

31.120E.1.a

the regulator, and

31.120E.1.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

31.120E.2

But the regulator need not be consulted if—

31.120E.2.a

the regulations give effect to a recommendation made by the regulator under
section 120G , or

31.120E.2.b

the Secretary of State has under  section 120H  asked the regulator for advice
about the description of building in question.

########## Regulations under 

31.120F

31.120F.1

This section applies if the Secretary of State proposes to make regulations
under  section 120D  that would result in a description of building (including
anything within  subsection (5)  of that section) becoming a higher-risk
building for the purposes of this Act as it applies in relation to England.

31.120F.2

The Secretary of State must ask the regulator under  section 120H (1)  for
advice about the description of building, except where the regulations would
give effect to a recommendation under  section 120G (2) .

31.120F.3

The Secretary of State must carry out a cost-benefit analysis and publish it.

31.120F.4

In this section “ cost-benefit analysis ” means—

31.120F.4.a

an analysis of the costs together with an analysis of the benefits that will
arise if the regulations are made, and

31.120F.4.b

an estimate of those costs and of those benefits (subject to  subsection (5)
).

31.120F.5

If, in the opinion of the Secretary of State—

31.120F.5.a

the costs or benefits cannot reasonably be estimated, or

31.120F.5.b

it is not reasonably practicable to produce an estimate,

the cost-benefit analysis need not estimate them, but must include a statement
of the Secretary of State’s opinion and an explanation for it.

########## Recommendations about regulations under 

31.120G

31.120G.1

Subsection (2)  applies if, in respect of any description of building that is
not a higher-risk building, the regulator considers—

31.120G.1.a

that a building safety risk is greater for that description of buildings than
it is for buildings that are not of that description,

31.120G.1.b

that if the risk materialised as regards a building of that description it
would have the potential to cause a major incident, and

31.120G.1.c

that buildings of that description should be higher-risk buildings for the
purposes of this Act as it applies in relation to England.

31.120G.2

The regulator must—

31.120G.2.a

recommend to the Secretary of State that buildings of that description should
be higher-risk buildings for the purposes of this Act, and

31.120G.2.b

give the Secretary of State a statement of its assessment of the issues it
considered when deciding to make the recommendation.

31.120G.3

If, following a recommendation, the Secretary of State decides not to make
regulations under  section 120D  giving effect to the recommendation, the
Secretary of State must publish a document setting out—

31.120G.3.a

the regulator’s recommendation,

31.120G.3.b

the Secretary of State’s decision not to make the regulations, and

31.120G.3.c

the reasons for that decision.

31.120G.4

If the regulator considers that a particular description of higher-risk
building should cease to be a higher-risk building for the purposes of this
Act as it applies in relation to England, it must make a recommendation to the
Secretary of State to that effect.

31.120G.5

In this section—

“ building safety risk ” means a risk to the safety of people in or about a
building arising from any of the following occurring as regards the building—
the spread of fire; structural failure; any other matter prescribed by
regulations under section 62 of the Building Safety Act 2022 in relation to
all buildings, or in relation to a description of building that includes the
building; “ major incident ” means an incident resulting in— a significant
number of deaths, or serious injury to a significant number of people.

########## Advice about regulations under 

31.120H

31.120H.1

Subsections (2)  to  (5)  apply if the Secretary of State asks the regulator
for advice as to whether a specified description of building should be a
higher-risk building for the purposes of this Act as it applies in relation to
England.

31.120H.2

The regulator must consider whether the following conditions are met—

31.120H.2.a

the first condition is that a building safety risk is greater for that
description of buildings than it is for buildings that are not of that
description;

31.120H.2.b

the second condition is that, if the risk materialised as regards a building
of that description, it would have the potential to cause a major incident;

31.120H.2.c

the third condition is that buildings of that description should be higher-
risk buildings for the purposes of this Act as it applies in relation to
England.

31.120H.3

The regulator must—

31.120H.3.a

if the conditions mentioned in  subsection (2)  are met, recommend to the
Secretary of State that buildings of that description should be higher-risk
buildings for the purposes of this Act as it applies in relation to England;

31.120H.3.b

otherwise, recommend to the Secretary of State that buildings of that
description should not be higher-risk buildings for those purposes.

31.120H.4

The regulator must give the Secretary of State a statement of its assessment
of the issues it considered in relation to the recommendation under
subsection (3) .

31.120H.5

If, following a recommendation under  subsection (3) (a) , the Secretary of
State decides not to make regulations under  section 120D  giving effect to
the recommendation, the Secretary of State must publish a document setting
out—

31.120H.5.a

the regulator’s recommendation,

31.120H.5.b

the Secretary of State’s decision not to make the regulations, and

31.120H.5.c

the reasons for that decision.

31.120H.6

If requested, the regulator must provide advice to the Secretary of State as
to whether a specified description of building should cease to be a higher-
risk building for the purposes of this Act as it applies in relation to
England.

31.120H.7

In this section—

“ building safety risk ” has the meaning given by  section 120G ; “ major
incident ” has the meaning given by that section; “ specified ” means
specified in the request.

########## Higher-risk buildings and higher-risk building work: Wales

31.120I

31.120I.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Act as it applies in relation to
Wales.

31.120I.2

“ Higher-risk building ” means a building of a description specified in
regulations made by the Welsh Ministers.

31.120I.3

“ Higher-risk building work ” means any work relating to a higher-risk
building or a proposed higher-risk building, including—

31.120I.3.a

any work relating to a building that is not a higher-risk building that causes
it to become such a building, and

31.120I.3.b

any work relating to a higher-risk building that causes it to cease to be such
a building.

31.120I.4

The Welsh Ministers may by regulations define “ building ” for the purposes of
this section.

31.120I.5

The regulations may in particular provide that “ building ” includes—

31.120I.5.a

any other structure or erection of any kind (whether temporary or permanent);

31.120I.5.b

any vehicle, vessel or other movable object of any kind, in such circumstances
as may be specified.

##### Building control authorities

32

32.1

The Building Act 1984 is amended as follows.

32.2

In section 91—

32.2.a

in subsection (1) before paragraph (a) insert—

32.2.a.za

subsection (3)  of this section and regulations under  section 91ZD ,

;

32.2.b

in subsection (2) for the words from “sections” to the end substitute

—

32.2.b.a

subsection (3)  of this section,

32.2.b.b

sections 5(3), 48(1) and 53(2), and

32.2.b.c

regulations under section  91ZD .

;

32.2.c

after that subsection insert—

32.2.c.3

In cases where section  91ZA  or  91ZB  provides that the regulator is the
building control authority, it is the duty of the regulator (and not the local
authority in question)—

32.2.c.3.a

to carry Part 1 of this Act into execution, and

32.2.c.3.b

to enforce building regulations.

;

32.2.d

in the heading at the end insert  “and the regulator” .

32.3

After that section insert—

########### The regulator: building control authority for higher-risk buildings in England

32.3.91ZA

32.3.91ZA.1

The regulator is the building control authority in relation to any higher-risk
building in England or any proposed such building.

32.3.91ZA.2

This includes the regulator being the building control authority as regards—

32.3.91ZA.2.a

any work relating to a building in England that is not a higher-risk building
that causes it to become such a building, and

32.3.91ZA.2.b

any work relating to a higher-risk building in England that causes it to cease
to be such a building.

32.3.91ZA.3

In this Act “ higher-risk building work ”, in relation to England, means any
work for which the regulator is the building control authority by virtue of
this section.

32.3.91ZA.4

For the meaning of “higher-risk building” see  section 120D .

########### The regulator: building control authority for other work

32.3.91ZB

32.3.91ZB.1

This section applies in relation to work of a prescribed description (“the
work”) that is to be carried out in England and has a prescribed connection
with any higher-risk building work.

32.3.91ZB.2

Where—

32.3.91ZB.2.a

the regulator and the person intending to carry out the work, acting jointly,
give a notice under this section (a “regulator’s notice”) to the local
authority for the area in which the work is to be carried out, and

32.3.91ZB.2.b

the regulator’s notice is accepted (or treated as accepted) by the local
authority,

the regulator is the building control authority in relation to the work.

32.3.91ZB.3

A regulator’s notice may not be given if any of the following has been given
to the local authority in relation to the work (or any part of it)—

32.3.91ZB.3.a

an application for building control approval;

32.3.91ZB.3.b

an initial notice (within the meaning of section 47);

32.3.91ZB.3.c

a public body’s notice (within the meaning of section 54).

########### Section 

32.3.91ZC

32.3.91ZC.1

This section supplements section  91ZB .

32.3.91ZC.2

A local authority to whom a regulator’s notice is given must reject the notice
if any prescribed ground exists, and must otherwise accept the notice.

32.3.91ZC.3

A notice of rejection must be given within the prescribed period, and must
specify the ground or grounds in question.

32.3.91ZC.4

The person intending to carry out the work may appeal to the tribunal against
a decision of the local authority to reject the regulator’s notice.

32.3.91ZC.5

Where a local authority to whom a regulator’s notice is given does not—

32.3.91ZC.5.a

give a notice of rejection in accordance with  subsection (3) , or

32.3.91ZC.5.b

give a notice of acceptance within the period mentioned in that subsection,

the authority is treated as having accepted the regulator’s notice at the end
of that period.

32.3.91ZC.6

As regards any notice under section  91ZB  or this section, building
regulations may make provision about—

32.3.91ZC.6.a

the form and content of the notice;

32.3.91ZC.6.b

the information and documents that must accompany it;

32.3.91ZC.6.c

the way in which the notice, and anything that is to accompany it, is to be
given.

########### Higher-risk buildings in Wales: local authority work

32.3.91ZD

32.3.91ZD.1

Building regulations may make provision about cases where a local authority
for an area in Wales (“ the relevant local authority ”) proposes to carry out
higher-risk building work in that area.

32.3.91ZD.2

The regulations may in particular—

32.3.91ZD.2.a

restrict (or prevent) the exercise by the relevant local authority of
prescribed functions in relation to the higher-risk building work;

32.3.91ZD.2.b

require the relevant local authority to notify the Welsh Ministers of
prescribed matters;

32.3.91ZD.2.c

confer on the Welsh Ministers a power to designate another local authority as
the building control authority in relation to the higher-risk building work
(instead of the relevant local authority);

32.3.91ZD.2.d

confer on the Welsh Ministers a power to require the relevant local authority
to provide specified information, for the purposes of deciding whether to
exercise the power of designation.

32.3.91ZD.3

The regulations may also provide, in cases where a local authority is
designated as the building control authority in relation to the higher-risk
building work, that the relevant local authority and the designated local
authority may agree that the designated local authority is to be the building
control authority in relation to any work of a prescribed description that has
a prescribed connection with the higher-risk building work.

32.3.91ZD.4

Where, as a result of regulations made by virtue of  subsection (2) (c)  or
(3) , a designated local authority is the building control authority in
relation to any work, as regards that work—

32.3.91ZD.4.a

prescribed functions are functions of the designated local authority (rather
than the relevant local authority);

32.3.91ZD.4.b

the designated local authority (rather than the relevant local authority) must
perform such functions relating to enforcement as may be prescribed.

32.4

After section 121 insert—

########### Meaning of “building control authority”

32.4.121A

32.4.121A.1

In this Act “ building control authority ” means—

32.4.121A.1.a

the regulator, in cases where section  91ZA  or  91ZB  provides that the
regulator is the building control authority;

32.4.121A.1.b

the local authority mentioned in  subsection (2) , in any other case.

32.4.121A.2

That local authority is—

32.4.121A.2.a

if, by virtue of regulations made under  section 91ZD  (higher-risk buildings
in Wales: local authority work), a designated local authority is the building
control authority, that local authority;

32.4.121A.2.b

otherwise, the local authority for the area in which the building is situated
or the proposed building is to be situated.

##### Building regulations

33

In Schedule 1 to the Building Act 1984 (building regulations) after paragraph
1 insert—

######### Procedural requirements etc: general

33.1A

33.1A.1

Building regulations may make provision about the procedure that may or must
be followed in relation to any work.

33.1A.2

The regulations may in particular make provision for and in connection with—

33.1A.2.a

the giving of notices;

33.1A.2.b

the making of applications to building control authorities;

33.1A.2.c

the giving or receipt of certificates;

33.1A.2.d

requiring a prescribed person, in prescribed circumstances, to consult such
other person as may be prescribed.

33.1A.3

The regulations may—

33.1A.3.a

confer on a building control authority a power to require a person to notify
the authority of specified matters by the specified time;

33.1A.3.b

provide that in prescribed circumstances an application is treated as granted
or is treated as refused;

33.1A.3.c

make provision about the effect of the grant of an application;

33.1A.3.d

make provision about the effect of certificates;

33.1A.3.e

require a person consulted to give a substantive response to the consultation
before the end of a prescribed period.

33.1A.4

In  sub-paragraph (3) (a)  “ specified ” means specified by the building
control authority.

######### Applications for building control approval

33.1B

33.1B.1

Building regulations may in particular make provision for and in connection
with applications for building control approval (including approval of changes
to anything that has already been approved).

33.1B.2

“Building control approval”—

33.1B.2.a

in relation to any work, means the approval by the building control authority
of—

33.1B.2.a.i

plans of the work, and

33.1B.2.a.ii

such other documents, relating to compliance with any provision of building
regulations, as may be prescribed (or, in a case within  sub-paragraph (5) ,
as are provided to the authority);

33.1B.2.b

in relation to a change to a relevant document, means the approval by the
authority of the change.

33.1B.3

Building regulations may—

33.1B.3.a

confer on building control authorities a power, with the consent of the
applicant—

33.1B.3.a.i

to impose requirements (including in particular requirements of a kind
mentioned in  sub-paragraph (4) ) when granting an application;

33.1B.3.a.ii

to vary requirements;

33.1B.3.b

make provision about the cases in which an application for approval of a
change must be made (including provision conferring on building control
authorities a power to specify the circumstances in which such an application
must be made).

33.1B.4

The requirements referred to in  sub-paragraph (3) (a)  are—

33.1B.4.a

a requirement relating to the provision of a revised version of a specified
relevant document;

33.1B.4.b

a requirement that the work does not proceed beyond a specified stage unless a
specified relevant document has been given to, and approved by, the building
control authority.

33.1B.5

Building regulations may provide that in prescribed cases—

33.1B.5.a

an application may be made to the authority for approval of the plans and such
other relevant documents as the applicant considers appropriate, and

33.1B.5.b

the authority may refuse the application if the applicant does not, on
request, provide it with a specified relevant document.

33.1B.6

In this paragraph—

33.1B.6.a

“ relevant document ” means—

33.1B.6.a.i

the plans mentioned in  sub-paragraph (2) (a) (i) , or

33.1B.6.a.ii

a document prescribed for the purposes of  sub-paragraph (2) (a) (ii) ;

33.1B.6.b

“ specified ” means specified by the building control authority;

33.1B.6.c

a reference to a change to a document includes the replacement of it.

######### Certificates: approved schemes

33.1C

33.1C.1

Building regulations may in particular make provision for and in connection
with certificates that are given—

33.1C.1.a

by a member of a scheme that is approved,

33.1C.1.b

in accordance with the scheme, and

33.1C.1.c

in accordance with any prescribed requirement relating to the provision of
insurance cover in respect of work to which the certificate relates.

33.1C.2

Building regulations may make provision for and in connection with—

33.1C.2.a

the approval of schemes by the appropriate national authority or a person
designated by that authority;

33.1C.2.b

the suspension or withdrawal of approvals (including provision about appeals
to the appropriate court or tribunal against the suspension or withdrawal of
approvals).

33.1C.3

The regulations may in particular provide that a scheme may be approved (and
may remain approved) only if prescribed requirements relating to the provision
of insurance cover are complied with.

33.1C.4

The regulations may provide—

33.1C.4.a

that an approval has effect for a particular period (including a period
specified in the approval), or

33.1C.4.b

that an approval has effect until it is suspended or withdrawn.

33.1C.5

The requirements relating to insurance cover that may be prescribed include in
particular a requirement that insurance cover is provided through a scheme of
insurance approved by the appropriate national authority or a person
designated by that authority.

######### Obtaining, keeping and giving information and documents

33.1D

33.1D.1

Building regulations may, in relation to any work, make provision about—

33.1D.1.a

obtaining information or documents;

33.1D.1.b

creating documents;

33.1D.1.c

keeping information or documents;

33.1D.1.d

giving information or documents.

33.1D.2

The regulations may in particular—

33.1D.2.a

provide that information or documents must be given or kept in accordance with
prescribed standards;

33.1D.2.b

impose requirements as regards keeping information or documents up to date;

33.1D.2.c

confer on building control authorities or other prescribed persons a power, in
prescribed circumstances, to require a person to give information to them.

33.1D.3

Where building regulations provide that any information or document must be
given, they may make provision about the admissibility in any criminal
proceedings of the information or document.

######### Reporting requirements: duty to establish and operate system

33.1E

33.1E.1

This paragraph applies where building regulations made by virtue of  paragraph
1D  require a person to give information—

33.1E.1.a

in relation to work in England, to the regulator;

33.1E.1.b

in relation to work in Wales, to the building control authority.

33.1E.2

For the purpose of facilitating and securing compliance with any such
requirement, the regulations may—

33.1E.2.a

require a prescribed person to establish and operate a system for the giving
of prescribed information to such person as may be prescribed, and

33.1E.2.b

make provision about such systems.

######### Form and content of documents etc

33.1F

33.1F.1

Where building regulations provide that any document must or may be given,
they may make provision about—

33.1F.1.a

the form and content of the document;

33.1F.1.b

the information and other documents that must accompany it;

33.1F.1.c

the way in which the document, and anything that is to accompany it, is to be
given.

33.1F.2

Where building regulations provide that any information must or may be given,
they may make provision about the way in which it is to be given.

33.1F.3

Building regulations may provide that any of the matters mentioned in
paragraphs  (a)  to  (c)  of  sub-paragraph (1) , or in  sub-paragraph (2) ,
are to be specified in a direction made and published in accordance with the
regulations.

33.1F.4

Building regulations may provide that—

33.1F.4.a

a prescribed application must be accompanied by such prescribed documents as
the applicant considers appropriate, and

33.1F.4.b

the building control authority may refuse the application if the applicant
does not, on request, provide it with a document of a kind prescribed for the
purposes of paragraph  (a)  in relation to the application.

######### Inspection, testing etc

33.1G

33.1G.1

Building regulations may make provision for and in connection with—

33.1G.1.a

the inspection and testing of work;

33.1G.1.b

the inspection and testing of buildings;

33.1G.1.c

the inspection and testing of services, fittings and equipment provided in
connection with buildings;

33.1G.1.d

the taking of samples.

33.1G.2

The regulations may in particular—

33.1G.2.a

prohibit the covering up of any work, for a prescribed period after a
prescribed or specified event;

33.1G.2.b

provide for the cutting into or laying open of any work or building, or the
pulling down of any work.

33.1G.3

In  sub-paragraph (2) (a)  “ specified ” means specified by the building
control authority.

######### Applications to building control authorities: extension of period by agreement

33.1H

Building regulations may provide that any prescribed period for the doing of a
thing by a building control authority in connection with an application made
to it may be extended by agreement between the authority and the applicant.

######### Appeals

33.1I

33.1I.1

Building regulations may make provision for and in connection with appeals
against decisions made under, or under an instrument made under, Part 1, 2 or
2A of this Act.

33.1I.2

The regulations may confer, in respect of a prescribed decision—

33.1I.2.a

in relation to England—

33.1I.2.a.i

a right to appeal to the regulator or the tribunal, and

33.1I.2.a.ii

in the case of an appeal to the regulator, a right of appeal to the tribunal
against the decision of the regulator made on appeal;

33.1I.2.b

in relation to Wales—

33.1I.2.b.i

a right to appeal to the Welsh Ministers or a magistrates’ court, and

33.1I.2.b.ii

in the case of an appeal to the Welsh Ministers, a right of appeal to a
magistrates’ court or a right of appeal to the High Court, against the
decision of the Welsh Ministers made on appeal.

33.1I.3

The provision that may be made in connection with appeals includes provision
about a right of appeal conferred by Part 1, 2 or 2A.

33.1I.4

The regulations may in particular make provision about—

33.1I.4.a

the grounds upon which an appeal may be made;

33.1I.4.b

the period within which an appeal must be made;

33.1I.4.c

the way in which any appeal is to be made;

33.1I.4.d

the powers of the court, tribunal or other person determining the appeal
(including provision conferring a power to give directions and, in the case of
the regulator or Welsh Ministers, powers in respect of costs).

33.1I.5

In respect of appeals to the regulator or the Welsh Ministers, the regulations
may make provision about procedural matters (including provision conferring a
discretion as to the procedure to be adopted).

33.1I.6

In respect of appeals to the Welsh Ministers, the regulations may in
particular make provision for and in connection with the Welsh Ministers
appointing a person to determine the appeal (including provision conferring
functions on that person and providing that their decision is treated as the
decision of the Welsh Ministers).

##### Dutyholders and general duties

34

In Schedule 1 to the Building Act 1984 (building regulations) after paragraph
5 insert—

######### Appointed persons

34.5A

34.5A.1

Building regulations may require prescribed appointments to be made in
relation to any work.

34.5A.2

Building regulations may make provision about appointments, including
provision about—

34.5A.2.a

the persons who are to make appointments;

34.5A.2.b

the persons who may be appointed;

34.5A.2.c

the time by which appointments must be made;

34.5A.2.d

the period for which persons are to be appointed;

34.5A.2.e

the termination of appointments;

34.5A.2.f

the replacement of appointed persons.

34.5A.3

The regulations may provide that in prescribed circumstances an appointment is
treated as made.

34.5A.4

In this Schedule “ appointed person ”, in relation to any work, means a person
appointed in relation to that work under building regulations made by virtue
of this paragraph.

######### General duties

34.5B

34.5B.1

Building regulations may, for the purpose of facilitating compliance with any
requirement of building regulations in relation to any work to which building
regulations are applicable—

34.5B.1.a

impose duties on relevant persons in connection with the planning or
management of the work;

34.5B.1.b

require relevant persons to co-operate with other relevant persons.

34.5B.2

The following are “ relevant persons ” for this purpose—

34.5B.2.a

any appointed person;

34.5B.2.b

any prescribed person.

##### Industry competence

35

In Schedule 1 to the Building Act 1984 (building regulations) after  paragraph
5B  (inserted by section 34) insert—

######### Competence requirements

35.5C

35.5C.1

Building regulations may, in relation to any work, impose competence
requirements on—

35.5C.1.a

any appointed person, or

35.5C.1.b

any prescribed person.

35.5C.2

A “competence requirement” is a requirement relating to—

35.5C.2.a

the skills, knowledge, experience and behaviours of an individual;

35.5C.2.b

the capability of a person other than an individual to perform its functions
under building regulations.

35.5C.3

The regulations may require an appointed person who is not an individual to
give an individual acting under its control who has the appropriate skills,
knowledge, experience and behaviours the task of managing its functions as an
appointed person.

##### Lapse of building control approval etc

36

36.1

The Building Act 1984 is amended as follows.

36.2

For section 32 substitute—

########### Lapse of building control approval

36.2.32

36.2.32.1

This section applies where—

36.2.32.1.a

an application for building control approval in respect of any work is made on
any day (“ the relevant day ”), and

36.2.32.1.b

the application is granted.

36.2.32.2

Where—

36.2.32.2.a

the work relates to one building, and

36.2.32.2.b

the work is not commenced within 3 years from the end of the relevant day,

the relevant provisions have effect as if the application had not been made
(and the approval had not been given).

36.2.32.3

Where—

36.2.32.3.a

the work relates to more than one building, and

36.2.32.3.b

the work relating to one or more of the buildings (“the relevant work”) is not
commenced within 3 years from the end of the relevant day,

the relevant provisions have effect in relation to those buildings and the
relevant work as if the application had not been made (and the approval had
not been given).

36.2.32.4

In  subsection (1)  the reference to an application for building control
approval is to an application for approval of a kind mentioned in  paragraph
1B (2) (a)  of Schedule 1.

36.2.32.5

In this section “ the relevant provisions ” means this Act and regulations
made under it except the following provisions and any regulations made under
them—

36.2.32.5.a

sections 56,  56A ,  56B  and 91A (records and registers etc);

36.2.32.5.b

section 105B  (fees and charges).

36.2.32.6

Building regulations may make provision about when work, or work relating to a
building, is to be regarded as commenced for the purposes of this section.

36.3

36.6.b

36.7

########### Lapse of initial notice

36.7.53A

36.7.53A.1

This section applies where—

36.7.53A.1.a

on any day (“ the relevant day ”) an initial notice is given in respect of any
work, and

36.7.53A.1.b

the initial notice is accepted.

36.7.53A.2

Where the work relates to one building and is not commenced within 3 years
from the end of the relevant day—

36.7.53A.2.a

the initial notice ceases to be in force, and

36.7.53A.2.b

if a plans certificate relating to the work (or any part of it) has been
accepted, the relevant provisions have effect as if the certificate had not
been given (or accepted).

36.7.53A.3

36.7.53A.3.a

the initial notice ceases to be in force so far as it relates to the relevant

36.7.53A.3.b

if a plans certificate relating to the relevant work (or any part of it) has

relevant work, the certificate had not been given (or accepted).

36.7.53A.4

For the purposes of  subsection (3) (b)  it does not matter whether the plans
certificate also relates to work other than the relevant work.

36.7.53A.5

In this section “ the relevant provisions ” has the meaning given by  section
32 .

36.7.53A.6

Building regulations may make provision about when work, or work relating to a
building, is to be regarded as commenced for the purposes of this section.

, and

########### Lapse of public body’s notice

36.13.4A

36.13.4A.1

This paragraph applies where—

36.13.4A.1.a

on any day (“ the relevant day ”) a public body’s notice is given in respect
of any work, and

36.13.4A.1.b

the public body’s notice is accepted.

36.13.4A.2

Where the work relates to one building and is not commenced within 3 years
from the end of the relevant day—

36.13.4A.2.a

the public body’s notice ceases to be in force, and

36.13.4A.2.b

if a public body’s plans certificate relating to the work (or any part of it)

36.13.4A.3

Where the work relates to more than one building, and the work in relation to
one or more of the buildings (“the relevant work”) is not commenced within 3
years from the end of the relevant day—

36.13.4A.3.a

the public body’s notice ceases to be in force so far as it relates to the
relevant work, and

36.13.4A.3.b

if a public body’s plans certificate relating to the relevant work (or any

regards the relevant work, the certificate had not been given (or accepted).

36.13.4A.4

For the purposes of  sub-paragraph (3) (b)  it does not matter whether the
public body’s plans certificate also relates to work other than the relevant
work.

36.13.4A.5

In this paragraph “ the relevant provisions ” has the meaning given by

36.13.4A.6

Building regulations may make provision about when work (or work relating to a
