##### Determination of certain applications by Secretary of State or Welsh Ministers

37

After section 30 of the Building Act 1984 insert—

######### Determination by appropriate national authority

########## Determination of certain applications by appropriate national authority

37.30A

37.30A.1

This section applies where the building control authority fails to determine a
prescribed application relating to higher-risk building work (“ the original
application ”) within the relevant period.

37.30A.2

The applicant may apply to the appropriate national authority for the original
application to be determined by that authority.

37.30A.3

An application under this section may be made only—

37.30A.3.a

before the end of the prescribed period, and 

37.30A.3.b

if the building control authority has not determined the original application.

37.30A.4

The building control authority may not determine the original application at
any time after the making of an application under this section.

37.30A.5

Building regulations may make provision about applications under this section,
including in particular provision—

37.30A.5.a

about the making of such applications;

37.30A.5.b

requiring an applicant to notify the building control authority of the making
of an application;

37.30A.5.c

imposing duties on the building control authority in cases where an
application is made;

37.30A.5.d

for and in connection with the appropriate national authority appointing a
person to determine the original application (including provision conferring
functions on that person and providing that their decision is treated as the
decision of the appropriate national authority);

37.30A.5.e

about the procedure to be adopted in connection with the determination of the
original application.

37.30A.6

The provision that may be made by virtue of  subsection (5) (a)  includes
provision about—

37.30A.6.a

the form and content of applications;

37.30A.6.b

the information and documents that are to accompany an application;

37.30A.6.c

the way in which an application, and anything that is to accompany it, is to
be given.

37.30A.7

For the purposes of determining the original application by virtue of this
section, this Act and building regulations apply in relation to the
appropriate national authority (and any person appointed by virtue of
subsection (5) (d) ) as they apply in relation to the building control
authority.

37.30A.8

The applicant may appeal to—

37.30A.8.a

the tribunal, against a decision of the Secretary of State made under this
section;

37.30A.8.b

a magistrates’ court, against a decision of the Welsh Ministers made under
this section.

37.30A.9

In this section “ the relevant period ” means—

37.30A.9.a

the period provided by building regulations as the period within which the
building control authority is to make the decision, or

37.30A.9.b

if the regulations provide that that period may be extended by agreement
between the applicant and the building control authority and such an agreement
is made, the agreed period.

##### Compliance and stop notices

38

38.1

In the Building Act 1984 before section 36 insert—

########### Notices in respect of contraventions

############ Compliance notices

38.1.35B

38.1.35B.1

The building control authority may give a compliance notice to a person who
appears to the authority to have contravened, be contravening or be likely to
contravene—

38.1.35B.1.a

a relevant provision of building regulations, or

38.1.35B.1.b

a requirement imposed by virtue of such a provision.

38.1.35B.2

A “compliance notice” is—

38.1.35B.2.a

a notice requiring the recipient to take specified steps within a specified
period, or

38.1.35B.2.b

a notice requiring the recipient to remedy the contravention or the matters
giving rise to it within a specified period.

38.1.35B.3

A notice of a kind mentioned in  subsection (2) (a)  may specify any steps
relating to—

38.1.35B.3.a

the remedying of the contravention, or

38.1.35B.3.b

avoiding the contravention occurring.

38.1.35B.4

A person who, without reasonable excuse, contravenes a compliance notice
commits an offence.

38.1.35B.5

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

38.1.35B.5.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

38.1.35B.5.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

and (in either case) is liable on summary conviction to a further fine not
exceeding level 1 on the standard scale for each day on which the default
continues after the initial conviction.

38.1.35B.6

A compliance notice may not be given in respect of a contravention which
occurred more than 12 months before the day on which the notice is given.

38.1.35B.7

In this section—

38.1.35B.7.a

“ relevant provision ” means any provision of building regulations except one
that is prescribed for the purposes of this paragraph;

38.1.35B.7.b

“ specified ” means specified in the notice.

############ Stop notices

38.1.35C

38.1.35C.1

The building control authority may give a stop notice to a person appearing to
the authority to be in control of any work if it appears to the authority
that—

38.1.35C.1.a

the carrying out of the work would contravene a provision of building
regulations prescribed for the purposes of this paragraph,

38.1.35C.1.b

a compliance notice relating to the work has been contravened, or

38.1.35C.1.c

the work contravenes a provision of building regulations or a requirement
imposed by virtue of such a provision, and the risk of serious harm condition
is met.

38.1.35C.2

For the purposes of  subsection (1) (c)  the “risk of serious harm condition”
is that use of the building in question without the contravention having been
remedied would be likely to present a risk of serious harm to people in or
about the building.

38.1.35C.3

A “stop notice” is a notice prohibiting, either immediately or from a
specified time, the carrying out of specified work until the occurrence of
such of the following as may be specified—

38.1.35C.3.a

the taking of specified steps;

38.1.35C.3.b

the occurrence of specified circumstances;

38.1.35C.3.c

the remedying of a specified contravention or the matters giving rise to it.

38.1.35C.4

Where a stop notice is contravened, the person to whom the notice was given
commits an offence.

38.1.35C.5

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

38.1.35C.5.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

38.1.35C.5.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

and (in either case) is liable on summary conviction to a further fine not
exceeding level 1 on the standard scale for each day on which the default
continues after the initial conviction.

38.1.35C.6

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to
prove that the person took all reasonable precautions and exercised all due
diligence to avoid the contravention of the stop notice.

38.1.35C.7

In this section “ specified ” means specified in the notice.

############ Compliance and stop notices: supplementary

38.1.35D

38.1.35D.1

Building regulations may make provision about compliance notices or stop
notices.

38.1.35D.2

The regulations may in particular make provision about—

38.1.35D.2.a

the form and content of notices;

38.1.35D.2.b

the giving of notices;

38.1.35D.2.c

the amendment or withdrawal of notices;

38.1.35D.2.d

the extension of any period specified in a compliance notice for the doing of
a thing.

38.1.35D.3

The regulations may require a building control authority which gives a notice
to a person to take reasonable steps to notify other prescribed persons.

38.1.35D.4

A compliance notice, or a stop notice under  section 35C (1) (a) , may not be
given in respect of a contravention (including a future contravention) where—

38.1.35D.4.a

an application for building control approval was made to a building control
authority in respect of any work that is not higher-risk building work,

38.1.35D.4.b

the application was granted, and

38.1.35D.4.c

the contravention consists (or would consist) of the carrying out of work or
the doing of anything else in accordance with—

38.1.35D.4.c.i

the plans, or any other document, approved by the grant of building control
approval, and

38.1.35D.4.c.ii

any requirement imposed by the building control authority in connection with
the work or other thing.

38.2

After section 39 of that Act insert—

########### Appeals against compliance notices and stop notices etc

38.2.39A

38.2.39A.1

A person to whom a compliance notice has been given may appeal to the
appropriate court or tribunal.

38.2.39A.2

Where an appeal under  subsection (1)  is made—

38.2.39A.2.a

the compliance notice is of no effect pending the final determination or
withdrawal of the appeal, and

38.2.39A.2.b

the specified period mentioned in  section 35B (2)  is treated as extended by
the period—

38.2.39A.2.b.i

beginning with the day on which the appeal is made, and

38.2.39A.2.b.ii

ending with the day on which the appeal is finally determined or withdrawn.

38.2.39A.3

A person to whom a compliance notice has been given may apply to the
appropriate court or tribunal for an extension of the period for the doing of
the thing specified in the notice.

38.2.39A.4

Subsection  (2)  applies in relation to such an application as it applies in
relation to an appeal under  subsection (1) .

38.2.39A.5

A person to whom a stop notice has been given may appeal to the appropriate
court or tribunal.

38.2.39A.6

Where an appeal under  subsection (5)  is made—

38.2.39A.6.a

the appellant may apply to the appropriate court or tribunal for a direction
that the stop notice is of no effect pending the final determination or
withdrawal of the appeal, and

38.2.39A.6.b

unless and until any such direction is given, the stop notice continues to
have effect despite the making of the appeal.

##### Breach of building regulations

39

39.1

The Building Act 1984 is amended as follows.

39.2

For section 35 substitute—

########### Offence of contravening building regulations etc

39.2.35

39.2.35.1

A person who contravenes a provision of building regulations, or a requirement
imposed by virtue of any such provision, commits an offence.

39.2.35.2

Building regulations may provide that  subsection (1)  does not apply in
relation to a prescribed provision of the regulations.

39.2.35.3

Building regulations may provide that, in relation to a prescribed provision
of the regulations, it is a defence for a person charged with an offence under
this section to prove such matters relating to the contravention as may be
prescribed.

39.2.35.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

39.2.35.4.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

39.2.35.4.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

and (in either case) is liable on summary conviction to a further fine not
exceeding level 1 on the standard scale for each day on which the default
continues after the initial conviction.

39.3

In section 36 (4)  (time limit for notices requiring removal or alteration of
non-compliant work) for “12 months” substitute  “10 years” .

##### Liability of officers of body corporate etc

40

In the Building Act 1984 before section 113 insert—

######### Liability of officers of body corporate etc

40.112A

40.112A.1

Where an offence under this Act committed by a body corporate—

40.112A.1.a

is committed with the consent or connivance of any director, manager,
secretary or other similar officer of the body corporate, or any person who
was purporting to act in any such capacity, or

40.112A.1.b

is attributable to any neglect on the part of any such person,

that person as well as the body corporate commits the offence and is liable to
be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

40.112A.2

In  subsection (1)  “ director ”, in relation to a body corporate whose
affairs are managed by its members, means a member of the body corporate.

40.112A.3

Subsection  (1)  also applies in relation to a body that is not a body
corporate, with the substitution for the reference to a director of the body
of a reference—

40.112A.3.a

in the case of a partnership, to a partner;

40.112A.3.b

in the case of an unincorporated body other than a partnership—

40.112A.3.b.i

where the body’s affairs are managed by its members, to a member of the body;

40.112A.3.b.ii

in any other case, to a member of the governing body.

##### Revocation etc of certain provision made under section 2(2) of ECA 1972

41

41.1

In this section “ combined instrument ” means an instrument containing
(whether alone or with other provision)—

41.1.a

provision made under section 1(1) of the Building Act 1984 (building
regulations), and

41.1.b

provision made under section 2(2) of the European Communities Act 1972
(provision implementing EU obligations etc).

41.2

Regulations under section 1(1) of the Building Act 1984 may revoke a combined
instrument so far as it is made under section 2(2) of the European Communities
Act 1972.

41.3

Nothing in paragraph 13 or 14 of Schedule 8 to the European Union (Withdrawal)
Act 2018 (procedure etc for SIs amending or revoking regulations etc made
under section 2(2) of the 1972 Act) is to be read as applying to a statutory
instrument that amends a combined instrument so far as the combined instrument
is made under section 2(2) of the European Communities Act 1972.

#### Building control approvers and building inspectors

##### Regulation of building control profession

42

In the Building Act 1984, after Part 2 insert—

######### REGULATION OF BUILDING CONTROL PROFESSION

########## Interpretation

########### “Regulatory authority”

42.58A

In this Act the “ regulatory authority ” means—

42.58A.a

in relation to England, the regulator;

42.58A.b

in relation to Wales, the Welsh Ministers.

########## Registered building inspectors

########### “Registered building inspector”

42.58B

In this Act “ registered building inspector ” means an individual registered
as a building inspector in accordance with this Part.

########### Register of building inspectors

42.58C

42.58C.1

The regulatory authority must establish and maintain a register of building
inspectors.

42.58C.2

The register may provide for different classes of building inspectors (for
example, according to qualifications or experience).

42.58C.3

The regulatory authority must register an individual as a building inspector,
or a building inspector of a particular class, if—

42.58C.3.a

the individual makes an application for registration in accordance with
section 58D , and

42.58C.3.b

the authority is satisfied that the individual meets such criteria as the
authority may from time to time determine.

42.58C.4

Registration may—

42.58C.4.a

have effect in relation to all work or in relation to work of a particular
description;

42.58C.4.b

be subject to conditions.

42.58C.5

Registration must be for a prescribed period.

42.58C.6

The register must record, in relation to each registered building inspector—

42.58C.6.a

the individual’s name and business address;

42.58C.6.b

if the individual is employed by a building control authority or a registered
building control approver, the name and business address of that person;

42.58C.6.c

whether the individual’s registration has effect in relation to all work or
work of a particular description;

42.58C.6.d

if the individual’s registration has effect in relation to work of a
particular description, that description of work;

42.58C.6.e

any conditions to which the individual’s registration is subject;

42.58C.6.f

the period for which the individual is registered;

42.58C.6.g

if the individual’s registration has been varied by an order under  section
58I (2) (b) , that fact and the effect of the variation;

42.58C.6.h

if the individual’s registration has been suspended by an order under  section
58I (2) (c)  or  58J (2) , that fact and the period of the suspension;

42.58C.6.i

any matters that are prescribed.

42.58C.7

The regulatory authority must make the register available for inspection by
the public in whatever way the authority thinks appropriate.

########### Application for registration as building inspector

42.58D

42.58D.1

An application for registration as a building inspector must—

42.58D.1.a

be made in such form and manner, and

42.58D.1.b

be accompanied by such information and supporting evidence,

as the regulatory authority may from time to time determine.

42.58D.2

The regulatory authority may make different provision about those matters for
different cases.

42.58D.3

When considering an application for registration, the regulatory authority may
require the applicant to provide it with such further information or
supporting evidence as the authority may require.

42.58D.4

The applicant may appeal to the appropriate court or tribunal against any
decision made by the regulatory authority on the application.

########### Variation or cancellation of registration as building inspector

42.58E

42.58E.1

A registered building inspector may apply for the variation or cancellation of
their registration.

42.58E.2

Section  58D  applies to such an application as it applies to an application
for registration.

########### Code of conduct

42.58F

42.58F.1

The regulatory authority must prepare and publish a code of conduct for
registered building inspectors.

42.58F.2

The code must set out standards of professional conduct and practice expected
of registered building inspectors.

42.58F.3

The code may make different provision for different cases (for example, for
different descriptions of work).

42.58F.4

The regulatory authority may revise the code of conduct at any time (and must
publish any revised code).

########### Registered building inspectors: information notices

42.58G

42.58G.1

The regulatory authority may by notice in writing require a registered
building inspector to provide the authority with any documents or information
the authority reasonably requires for the purposes its functions under
sections  58B  to  58M .

42.58G.2

The notice must specify—

42.58G.2.a

the documents or information required,

42.58G.2.b

the date by which they must be provided, and

42.58G.2.c

the form in which they must be provided.

########### Professional misconduct investigations

42.58H

42.58H.1

If it appears to the regulatory authority (on receipt of a complaint or
otherwise) that a registered building inspector may be guilty of professional
misconduct, the authority may investigate the matter.

42.58H.2

In this Part “ professional misconduct ”, in relation to a registered building
inspector, means conduct that—

42.58H.2.a

falls short of the standards of conduct and practice expected of registered
building inspectors, or

42.58H.2.b

is likely to bring the profession of registered building inspectors into
disrepute.

42.58H.3

The regulatory authority must prepare and publish a statement of the procedure
it will follow when investigating a registered building inspector under this
section (which must include an opportunity for the inspector to make
representations).

42.58H.4

The regulatory authority may revise the statement at any time (and must
publish any revised statement).

########### Sanctions for professional misconduct

42.58I

42.58I.1

If following an investigation under  section 58H  the regulatory authority
determines that an individual who is a registered building inspector is guilty
of professional misconduct, the authority may make one or more disciplinary
orders.

42.58I.2

A disciplinary order is an order—

42.58I.2.a

requiring the individual to pay a financial penalty of an amount specified in
the order,

42.58I.2.b

varying the individual’s registration in a way specified in the order,

42.58I.2.c

suspending the individual’s registration for a period specified in the order,
or

42.58I.2.d

cancelling the individual’s registration from a date specified in the order.

42.58I.3

Varying the individual’s registration means varying any of the matters listed
in  section 58C (4)  (limitations and conditions).

42.58I.4

Where the regulatory authority makes a disciplinary order it must give a copy
of the order to the individual concerned as soon as reasonably practicable.

42.58I.5

The individual may appeal to the appropriate court or tribunal against a
disciplinary order under this section.

42.58I.6

A disciplinary order under  subsection (2) (a)  or  (b)  has no effect until—

42.58I.6.a

the end of the period within which an appeal may be brought, or

42.58I.6.b

if an appeal is brought before the end of that period, the determination of
the appeal.

42.58I.7

Where the regulatory authority is the regulator, it must pay into the
Consolidated Fund the amount of any financial penalty paid to it pursuant to a
disciplinary order under  subsection (2) (a) .

########### Interim suspension for suspected serious professional misconduct

42.58J

42.58J.1

This section applies where the regulatory authority considers that—

42.58J.1.a

an individual who is a registered building inspector may be guilty of
professional misconduct, and

42.58J.1.b

the suspected misconduct is so serious that, if the authority determines that
the individual is guilty, it is likely to make an order under  section 58I (2)
(d)  cancelling the individual’s registration.

42.58J.2

The regulatory authority may by order suspend the individual’s registration
for a period specified in the order (which must not exceed 3 months).

42.58J.3

The regulatory authority may revoke the order before the end of that period.

42.58J.4

Where the regulatory authority makes (or revokes) an order under this section
it must give a copy of the order (or notice of the revocation) to the
individual concerned as soon as reasonably practicable.

42.58J.5

The individual may appeal to the appropriate court or tribunal against an
order under this section.

########### Suspension orders: further provision

42.58K

An individual whose registration is suspended under  section 58I (2) (c)  or
58J (2)  is not a registered building inspector for the purposes of section
46A or 54B (restricted activities and functions) (but is a registered building
inspector for the purposes of this Part).

########### Offences relating to registration

42.58L

42.58L.1

A registered building inspector commits an offence if, without reasonable
excuse, they carry out a restricted activity on behalf of a building control
authority or a registered building control approver—

42.58L.1.a

in relation to work which is outside the scope of their registration, or

42.58L.1.b

while their registration is suspended.

42.58L.2

“Restricted activity”—

42.58L.2.a

in relation to a building control authority, has the meaning given by section
46A;

42.58L.2.b

in relation to a registered building control approver, has the meaning given
by section 54B.

42.58L.3

A registered building inspector commits an offence if, without reasonable
excuse—

42.58L.3.a

they give advice to a building control authority or registered building
control approver—

42.58L.3.a.i

in relation to work which is outside the scope of their registration, or

42.58L.3.a.ii

while their registration is suspended, and

42.58L.3.b

they know, or ought to know, that the authority or approver is obtaining that
advice for the purposes of section 46A or 54B (restricted functions).

42.58L.4

A registered building inspector commits an offence if, with intent to deceive,
they do anything which implies that work which is outside the scope of their
registration is within the scope of their registration.

42.58L.5

A registered building inspector whose registration is suspended commits an
offence if, with intent to deceive, they do anything which implies that their
registration is not suspended.

42.58L.6

For the purposes of this section, work is outside the scope of a registered
building inspector’s registration if the inspector’s registration does not
have effect in relation to work of that description.

42.58L.7

An offence under this section is punishable on summary conviction by a fine.

########### Offence of acting as, or pretending to be, a registered building inspector

42.58M

42.58M.1

A person who is not a registered building inspector commits an offence if,
with intent to deceive, the person—

42.58M.1.a

impersonates a registered building inspector, or

42.58M.1.b

does anything (including using any name, title or description) which implies
that the person is a registered building inspector.

42.58M.2

An offence under this section is punishable on summary conviction by a fine.

########## Registered building control approvers 

########### “Registered building control approver”

42.58N

In this Act “ registered building control approver ” means a person registered
as a building control approver in accordance with this Part.

########### Register of building control approvers

42.58O

42.58O.1

The regulatory authority must establish and maintain a register of building
control approvers.

42.58O.2

The regulatory authority must register a person as a building control approver
if—

42.58O.2.a

the person makes an application for registration in accordance with  section
58P , and

42.58O.2.b

the authority is satisfied that the person meets such criteria as the
authority may from time to time determine.

42.58O.3

Registration may—

42.58O.3.a

have effect in relation to all work or in relation to work of a particular
description;

42.58O.3.b

be subject to conditions.

42.58O.4

Registration must be for a prescribed period.

42.58O.5

The register must record, in relation to each registered building control
approver—

42.58O.5.a

the person’s name and business address;

42.58O.5.b

whether the person’s registration has effect in relation to all work or work
of a particular description;

42.58O.5.c

if the person’s registration has effect in relation to work of a particular
description, that description of work;

42.58O.5.d

any conditions to which the person’s registration is subject;

42.58O.5.e

the period for which the person is registered;

42.58O.5.f

if the person’s registration has been varied by an order under section  58U
(2) (b) , that fact and the effect of the variation;

42.58O.5.g

if the person’s registration has been suspended by an order under section  58U
(2) (c)  or  58V (2) , that fact and the period of the suspension;

42.58O.5.h

any matters that are prescribed.

42.58O.6

The regulatory authority must make the register available for inspection by
the public in whatever way the authority thinks appropriate.

########### Application for registration as building control approver

42.58P

42.58P.1

An application for registration as a building control approver must—

42.58P.1.a

be made in such form and manner, and

42.58P.1.b

be accompanied by such information and supporting evidence,

as the regulatory authority may from time to time determine.

42.58P.2

The regulatory authority may make different provision about those matters for
different cases.

42.58P.3

When considering an application for registration, the regulatory authority may
require the applicant to provide it with such further information or
supporting evidence as the authority may require.

42.58P.4

The applicant may appeal to the appropriate court or tribunal against any
decision made by the regulatory authority on the application.

########### Variation or cancellation of registration as building control approver

42.58Q

42.58Q.1

A registered building control approver may apply for the variation or
cancellation of their registration.

42.58Q.2

Section  58P  applies to such an application as it applies to an application
for registration.

########### Professional conduct rules

42.58R

42.58R.1

The regulatory authority must prepare and publish professional conduct rules
applying to registered building control approvers (in addition to operational
standards rules applying to them under section  58Z ).

42.58R.2

Professional conduct rules may in particular make provision about insurance
and financial propriety.

42.58R.3

The rules may make different provision for different cases (for example, for
different descriptions of work).

42.58R.4

The regulatory authority may revise the professional conduct rules at any time
(and must publish any revised rules).

########### Registered building control approvers: information notices

42.58S

42.58S.1

The regulatory authority may by notice in writing require a registered
building control approver to provide the authority with any documents or
information the authority reasonably requires for the purposes of its
functions under sections  58N  to  58X .

42.58S.2

The notice must specify—

42.58S.2.a

the documents or information required,

42.58S.2.b

the date by which they must be provided, and

42.58S.2.c

the form in which they must be provided.

########### Investigations into contraventions of professional conduct rules

42.58T

42.58T.1

If it appears to the regulatory authority (on receipt of a complaint or
otherwise) that a registered building control approver may have contravened
the professional conduct rules, the authority may investigate the matter.

42.58T.2

The regulatory authority must prepare and publish a statement of the procedure
it will follow when investigating a registered building control approver under
this section (which must include an opportunity for the person to make
representations).

42.58T.3

The regulatory authority may revise the statement at any time (and must
publish any revised statement).

########### Sanctions for contravention of professional conduct rules

42.58U

42.58U.1

If following an investigation under section  58T  the regulatory authority
determines that a person who is a registered building control approver has
contravened the professional conduct rules, the authority may make one or more
disciplinary orders.

42.58U.2

A disciplinary order is an order—

42.58U.2.a

requiring the person to pay a financial penalty of an amount specified in the
order,

42.58U.2.b

varying the person’s registration in a way specified in the order,

42.58U.2.c

suspending the person’s registration for a period specified in the order, or

42.58U.2.d

cancelling the person’s registration from a date specified in the order.

42.58U.3

Varying the person’s registration means varying any of the matters listed in
section 58O (3)  (limitations and conditions).

42.58U.4

Where the regulatory authority makes a disciplinary order it must as soon as
reasonably practicable—

42.58U.4.a

give a copy of the order to the person concerned, and

42.58U.4.b

in prescribed cases, give a copy of the order—

42.58U.4.b.i

to each local authority in England, where the regulatory authority is the
regulator, or

42.58U.4.b.ii

to each local authority in Wales, where the regulatory authority is the Welsh
Ministers.

42.58U.5

The person may appeal to the appropriate court or tribunal against a
disciplinary order under this section.

42.58U.6

A disciplinary order under  subsection (2) (a)  or  (b)  has no effect until—

42.58U.6.a

the end of the period within which an appeal may be brought, or

42.58U.6.b

if an appeal is brought before the end of that period, the determination of
the appeal.

42.58U.7

Where the regulatory authority is the regulator, it must pay into the
Consolidated Fund the amount of any financial penalty paid to it pursuant to a
disciplinary order under  subsection (2) (a) .

42.58U.8

A person whose registration is suspended by an order under  subsection (2) (c)
is a registered building control approver for the purposes of this Part.

42.58U.9

See section  58Z6 (2)  for further provision about cancellation of a person’s
registration as a building control approver.

########### Interim suspension for suspected serious contravention

42.58V

42.58V.1

This section applies where the regulatory authority considers that—

42.58V.1.a

a person who is a registered building control approver may have contravened
the professional conduct rules, and

42.58V.1.b

the suspected contravention is so serious that, if the authority determines
that the contravention has occurred, it is likely to make an order under
section 58U (2) (d)  cancelling the person’s registration.

42.58V.2

The regulatory authority may by order suspend the person’s registration for a
period specified in the order (which must not exceed 3 months).

42.58V.3

The regulatory authority may revoke the order before the end of that period.

42.58V.4

Where the regulatory authority makes (or revokes) an order under this section
it must as soon as reasonably practicable—

42.58V.4.a

give a copy of the order (or notice of the revocation) to the person
concerned, and

42.58V.4.b

in prescribed cases, give a copy of the order (or notice of the revocation)—

42.58V.4.b.i

to each local authority in England, where the regulatory authority is the
regulator, or

42.58V.4.b.ii

to each local authority in Wales, where the regulatory authority is the Welsh
Ministers.

42.58V.5

The person may appeal to the appropriate court or tribunal against an order
under this section.

42.58V.6

A person whose registration is suspended by an order under this section is a
registered building control approver for the purposes of this Part.

########### Offence of registered building control approver acting outside scope of registration

42.58W

42.58W.1

A registered building control approver commits an offence if, without
reasonable excuse, they exercise a function under this Act, or regulations
made under this Act—

42.58W.1.a

in relation to work outside the scope of their registration, or

42.58W.1.b

while their registration is suspended.

42.58W.2

A registered building control approver commits an offence if, with intent to
deceive, they do anything which implies that work which is outside the scope
of their registration is within the scope of their registration.

42.58W.3

A registered building control approver whose registration is suspended commits
an offence if, with intent to deceive, they do anything which implies that
their registration is not suspended.

42.58W.4

For the purposes of this section, work is outside the scope of a registered
building control approver’s registration if their registration does not have
effect in relation to work of that description.

42.58W.5

An offence under this section is punishable on summary conviction by a fine.

########### Offence of pretending to be a registered building control approver

42.58X

42.58X.1

A person who is not a registered building control approver commits an offence
if, with intent to deceive, the person—

42.58X.1.a

impersonates a registered building control approver, or

42.58X.1.b

does anything (including using any name, title or description) which implies
that the person is a registered building control approver.

42.58X.2

An offence under this section is punishable on summary conviction by a fine.

########## Delegation of registration functions

########### Delegation of registration functions

42.58Y

42.58Y.1

The regulatory authority may delegate its registration functions to another
person, to such extent and subject to such conditions as it considers
appropriate.

42.58Y.2

The regulatory authority’s registration functions are its functions under
sections  58B  to  58X  (and include the charging of any registration fees or
recovery of any registration charges).

42.58Y.3

“Registration fees” and “registration charges” mean fees and charges in
connection with the regulatory authority’s functions under sections  58B  to
58X  that are—

42.58Y.3.a

prescribed by regulations under section 105B, or

42.58Y.3.b

determined by the regulatory authority in accordance with regulations under
that section.

42.58Y.4

The regulatory authority may vary or revoke a delegation.

42.58Y.5

Where the regulatory authority is the regulator, it—

42.58Y.5.a

may make, vary or revoke a delegation only with the consent of the Secretary
of State;

42.58Y.5.b

must vary or revoke a delegation if directed to do so by the Secretary of
State.

42.58Y.6

Section  58Z9  of this Act (sharing of information between regulatory
authorities) and Schedule  3  to the Building Safety Act 2022 (information
sharing between regulator and other authorities) apply as if references to the
regulator included references to a person to whom the regulator has delegated
functions under this section.

42.58Y.7

The following provisions of this Act apply as if references to the Welsh
Ministers included references to a person to whom the Welsh Ministers have
delegated functions under this section—

42.58Y.7.a

section  58Z9  (sharing of information between regulatory authorities);

42.58Y.7.b

section 91B (cooperation and sharing of information between Welsh Ministers
and other authorities);

42.58Y.7.c

section 131A (application to the Crown).

########## Operational standards rules

########### Operational standards rules

42.58Z

42.58Z.1

The regulatory authority may make rules (“operational standards rules”)
applying to local authorities and registered building control approvers in
relation to their exercise of building control functions.

42.58Z.2

Operational standards rules may in particular make provision about standards
to be met, and practices, procedures or methods to be adopted, in exercising
building control functions.

42.58Z.3

In this Part “ building control functions ”, in relation to a local authority
or registered building control approver, means the functions of the authority
or approver under this Act and regulations made under it.

42.58Z.4

The operational standards rules may make different provision for different
cases (for example, for different descriptions of work).

42.58Z.5

The regulatory authority may revise the operational standards rules at any
time.

42.58Z.6

The regulatory authority must publish the operational standards rules (and any
revised rules).

########### Reporting requirements

42.58Z1

42.58Z1.1

The regulatory authority may direct local authorities and registered building
control approvers to provide it, at specified times or intervals, with
specified reports, returns and other information relating to the exercise of
their building control functions.

42.58Z1.2

“ Specified ” means specified in the direction.

42.58Z1.3

A direction under this section—

42.58Z1.3.a

must be in writing;

42.58Z1.3.b

may be general or specific;

42.58Z1.3.c

may be varied or revoked.

42.58Z1.4

A registered building control approver who, without reasonable excuse, fails
to comply with a direction under this section commits an offence.

42.58Z1.5

An offence under subsection  (4)  is punishable on summary conviction by a
fine.

########### Information: Wales

42.58Z2

42.58Z2.1

This section applies where the Welsh Ministers are the regulatory authority.

42.58Z2.2

The Welsh Ministers may by notice in writing require a local authority or
registered building control approver to provide the Welsh Ministers with any
documents or information relating to the exercise of their building control
functions that the Welsh Ministers reasonably require.

42.58Z2.3

The notice must specify—

42.58Z2.3.a

the documents or information required,

42.58Z2.3.b

the date by which they must be provided, and

42.58Z2.3.c

the form in which they must be provided.

42.58Z2.4

A registered building control approver who, without reasonable excuse, fails
to comply with a notice under this section commits an offence.

42.58Z2.5

An offence under  subsection (4)  is punishable on summary conviction by a
fine.

########### Investigations

42.58Z3

42.58Z3.1

If it appears to the regulatory authority (on receipt of a complaint or
otherwise) that a local authority or registered building control approver may
have contravened the operational standards rules, the regulatory authority may
investigate the matter.

42.58Z3.2

The regulatory authority must prepare and publish a statement of the procedure
it will follow when investigating an authority or approver under this section
(which must include an opportunity for the authority or approver to make
representations).

42.58Z3.3

The regulatory authority may revise the statement at any time (and must
publish any revised statement).

########### Improvement notice

42.58Z4

42.58Z4.1

The regulatory authority may give an improvement notice to a local authority
or a registered building control approver if it appears to the regulatory
authority (following an investigation under section  58Z3  or otherwise) that
the local authority or registered building control approver has contravened
operational standards rules.

42.58Z4.2

An improvement notice is a notice requiring the local authority or registered
building control approver to remedy the contravention by doing, or by
refraining from doing, anything specified in the order.

42.58Z4.3

An improvement notice may have effect—

42.58Z4.3.a

until it is revoked, or

42.58Z4.3.b

for a period specified in the notice.

42.58Z4.4

Where the regulatory authority gives an improvement notice, it must also give
the local authority or registered building control approver a statement of the
reasons for giving the notice.

42.58Z4.5

Where the regulatory authority gives an improvement notice to a registered
building control approver, in prescribed cases it must as soon as reasonably
practicable provide copies of the notice and the statement—

42.58Z4.5.a

to each local authority in England, where the regulatory authority is the
regulator, or

42.58Z4.5.b

to each local authority in Wales, where the regulatory authority is the Welsh
Ministers.

42.58Z4.6

Where the regulatory authority giving an improvement notice is the regulator,
it must as soon as reasonably practicable provide copies of the notice and the
statement of reasons to the Secretary of State.

42.58Z4.7

The local authority or registered building control approver to whom the
improvement notice is given may appeal to the appropriate court or tribunal
against the notice.

########### Serious contravention notices

42.58Z5

42.58Z5.1

The regulatory authority may give a serious contravention notice to a local
authority or a registered building control approver if it appears to the
regulatory authority (following an investigation under section  58Z3  or
otherwise) that the condition in subsection  (2)  or  (3)  is met.

42.58Z5.2

The condition in this subsection is that—

42.58Z5.2.a

the local authority or registered building control approver has contravened
operational standards rules, and

42.58Z5.2.b

as a result of the contravention the safety of persons in or about buildings
has been, or may have been, put at risk.

42.58Z5.3

This condition in this subsection is that the local authority or registered
building control approver—

42.58Z5.3.a

has been given an improvement notice under section  58Z4 , and

42.58Z5.3.b

has failed to remedy the contravention of operational standards rules in
respect of which the notice was given.

42.58Z5.4

A serious contravention notice is a notice requiring the local authority or
registered building control approver to remedy the contravention in question
by doing, or by refraining from doing, anything specified in the order.

42.58Z5.5

A serious contravention notice may have effect—

42.58Z5.5.a

until it is revoked, or

42.58Z5.5.b

for a period specified in the notice.

42.58Z5.6

Where the regulatory authority gives a serious contravention notice, it must
also give the local authority or registered building control approver a
statement of the reasons for giving the notice.

42.58Z5.7

Where the regulatory authority gives a serious contravention notice to a
registered building control approver, in prescribed cases it must as soon as
reasonably practicable provide copies of the notice and the statement—

42.58Z5.7.a

to each local authority in England, where the regulatory authority is the
regulator, or

42.58Z5.7.b

to each local authority in Wales, where the regulatory authority is the Welsh
Ministers.

42.58Z5.8

Where the regulatory authority giving a serious contravention notice is the
regulator, it must as soon as reasonably practicable provide copies of the
notice and the statement of reasons to the Secretary of State.

42.58Z5.9

The local authority or registered building control approver to whom the
serious contravention notice is given may appeal to the appropriate court or
tribunal against the notice.

42.58Z5.10

A person who, without reasonable excuse, contravenes a serious contravention
notice commits an offence and is liable on summary conviction to a fine.

########### Continuing failure to meet standards: registered building control approvers

42.58Z6

42.58Z6.1

This section applies where—

42.58Z6.1.a

the regulatory authority has given a registered building control approver one
or more serious contravention notices under  section 58Z5 , and

42.58Z6.1.b

it appears to the regulatory authority that the way in which the approver
exercises their building control functions—

42.58Z6.1.b.i

falls short of the standards expected, and

42.58Z6.1.b.ii

puts, or may put, the safety of persons in or about buildings at risk,

and is likely to continue to do so.

42.58Z6.2

The regulatory authority may cancel the approver’s registration.

42.58Z6.3

But before cancelling a registered building control approver’s registration
under  subsection (2)  the regulatory authority must—

42.58Z6.3.a

give the approver notice that it is considering its registration under that
subsection, and explain its reasons, and

42.58Z6.3.b

invite the approver to make representations within a period specified in the
notice (which must not be less than 14 days).

42.58Z6.4

Where the regulatory authority cancels a registered building control
approver’s registration under  subsection (2)  it must as soon as reasonably
practicable—

42.58Z6.4.a

notify the approver that it has done so,

42.58Z6.4.b

give the approver a statement of its reasons, and

42.58Z6.4.c

notify—

42.58Z6.4.c.i

each local authority in England, where the regulatory authority is the
regulator, or

42.58Z6.4.c.ii

each local authority in Wales, where the regulatory authority is the Welsh
Ministers.

42.58Z6.5

A registered building control approver may appeal to the appropriate court or
tribunal against the cancellation of its registration under  subsection (2) .

########### Continuing failure to meet standards: local authorities in England

42.58Z7

42.58Z7.1

This section applies where—

42.58Z7.1.a

the regulatory authority is the regulator,

42.58Z7.1.b

the regulatory authority has given a local authority one or more serious
contravention notices under  section 58Z5 , and

42.58Z7.1.c

it appears to the regulatory authority that the way in which the local
authority exercises their building control functions—

42.58Z7.1.c.i

falls short of the standards expected, and

42.58Z7.1.c.ii

puts, or may put, the safety of persons in or about buildings at risk,

and is likely to continue to do so.

42.58Z7.2

The regulatory authority may recommend to the Secretary of State that the
Secretary of State make an order under section 116(4) (transfer of functions
to the Secretary of State or another local authority).

42.58Z7.3

But before making a recommendation under  subsection (2)  the regulatory
authority must—

42.58Z7.3.a

give the local authority notice that it is considering making a recommendation
under that subsection, and explain its reasons, and

42.58Z7.3.b

invite the authority to make representations within a period specified in the
notice (which must not be less than 14 days).

42.58Z7.4

Where the regulatory authority makes a recommendation under  subsection (2)
it must as soon as reasonably practicable—

42.58Z7.4.a

notify the local authority that it has done so, and

42.58Z7.4.b

give the local authority a statement of its reasons.

42.58Z7.5

A local authority may appeal to the tribunal against a recommendation under
subsection (2) .

########## Inspection of local authorities and registered building control approvers

########### Inspections

42.58Z8

42.58Z8.1

The regulatory authority may carry out an inspection of a local authority, or
a registered building control approver, in relation to their exercise of
building control functions.

42.58Z8.2

The purposes for which an inspection may be carried out include—

42.58Z8.2.a

ascertaining the efficiency and effectiveness of the local authority or
registered building control approver in exercising their building control
functions;

42.58Z8.2.b

verifying any information provided by the local authority or registered
building control approver to the regulatory authority, in connection with
their building control functions.

########## Information sharing

########### Sharing of information between regulatory authorities

42.58Z9

42.58Z9.1

The regulator may disclose information held in connection with a function
under this Part to the Welsh Ministers for the purposes of—

42.58Z9.1.a

a function of the regulator under this Part, or

42.58Z9.1.b

a function of the Welsh Ministers under this Part.

42.58Z9.2

The Welsh Ministers may disclose information held in connection with a
function under this Part to the regulator for the purposes of—

42.58Z9.2.a

a function of the Welsh Ministers under this Part, or

42.58Z9.2.b

a function of the regulator under this Part.

42.58Z9.3

Except as provided by subsection (4), the disclosure of information under this
section does not breach—

42.58Z9.3.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

42.58Z9.3.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

42.58Z9.4

This section does not authorise a disclosure of information if the disclosure
would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, take into account the powers conferred by this
section).

########## Appeals

########### Appeal to Crown Court

42.58Z10

An appeal lies to the Crown Court against a decision of a magistrates’ court
under this Part.

##### Transfer of approved inspectors’ functions to registered building control approvers

43

Schedule  4  amends the Building Act 1984 so as to—

43.a

transfer the functions of approved inspectors to registered building control
approvers, and

43.b

make other provision consequential on section 42.

##### Functions exercisable only through, or with advice of, registered building inspectors

44

44.1

The Building Act 1984 is amended as follows.

44.2

After section 46 insert—

########### Building control authorities: restricted activities and functions

############ Building control authorities: restricted activities and functions

44.2.46A

44.2.46A.1

A building control authority may carry out a restricted activity in relation
to any work only through a registered building inspector, acting on the
authority’s behalf, whose registration has effect in relation to work of that
description.

44.2.46A.2

Before each exercise of a restricted function in relation to any work, a
building control authority must obtain and consider the advice of a registered
building inspector whose registration has effect in relation to work of that
description.

44.2.46A.3

The registered building inspector who carries out the restricted activity, or
advises on the exercise of the restricted function, may (but need not) be
employed by the authority.

44.2.46A.4

In this section—

“ restricted activity ” means an activity that is prescribed for the purposes
of this section; “ restricted function ” means a function of a building
control authority under— this Part, Part 3, or regulations made under this
Part or Part 3, that is prescribed for the purposes of this section.

44.3

After  section 54A  (inserted by section 47) insert—

########### Registered building control approvers: restricted activities and functions

############ Registered building control approvers: restricted activities and functions

44.3.54B

44.3.54B.1

This section applies to a registered building control approver who is not a
registered building inspector.

44.3.54B.2

The approver may carry out a restricted activity in relation to any work only
through a registered building inspector, acting on the approver’s behalf,
whose registration has effect in relation to work of that description.

44.3.54B.3

Before each exercise of a restricted function in relation to any work, the
approver must obtain and consider the advice of a registered building
inspector whose registration has effect in relation to work of that
description.

44.3.54B.4

The registered building inspector who carries out the restricted activity, or
advises on the exercise of the restricted function, may (but need not) be
employed by the approver.

44.3.54B.5

In this section—

“ restricted activity ” means an activity that is prescribed for the purposes
of this section; “ restricted function ” means a function of a registered
building control approver under this Part, or regulations made under this
Part, that is prescribed for the purposes of this section.

44.3.54B.6

A registered building control approver who contravenes subsection  (2)  or
(3)  without reasonable excuse commits an offence.

44.3.54B.7

An offence under this section is punishable on summary conviction by a fine.

##### Higher-risk building work: registered building control approvers

46

46.1

In section 47 of the Building Act 1984 (giving and acceptance of initial
notice), in subsection (1)(a)—

46.1.a

after “prescribed form” insert  “relating to work that is not higher-risk
building work” ;

46.1.b

after “carry out” insert  “the” .

46.2

In section 51A of the Building Act 1984 (variation of work to which initial
notice relates), for subsection (1) substitute—

46.2.1

This section applies where—

46.2.1.a

it is proposed that the work to which an initial notice relates should be
varied, and

46.2.1.b

the work as varied is not higher-risk building work.

46.3

After section 52 of the Building Act 1984 insert—

########### Cancellation of initial notice when work becomes higher-risk building work

46.3.52A

46.3.52A.1

If, at a time when an initial notice is in force, it appears to the registered
building control approver that some or all of the work has become higher-risk
building work, the registered building control approver must, as soon as is
reasonably practicable, cancel the relevant part of the initial notice by
notice in the prescribed form given to—

46.3.52A.1.a

the local authority concerned, and

46.3.52A.1.b

the person carrying out or intending to carry out the work.

46.3.52A.2

If, at a time when an initial notice is in force, it appears to the person
carrying out or intending to carry out the work that some or all of the work
has become higher-risk building work, the person must, as soon as is
reasonably practicable, cancel the relevant part of the initial notice by
notice in the prescribed form given to—

46.3.52A.2.a

the local authority concerned, and

46.3.52A.2.b

the registered building control approver.

46.3.52A.3

Where a person is required to give a notice under subsection  (1)  or  (2)  in
relation to higher-risk building work in England, the person must, as soon as
is reasonably practicable, give a copy of that notice to the regulator.

46.3.52A.4

If, at a time when an initial notice is in force, it appears to the local
authority concerned that some or all of the work has become higher-risk
building work, the authority must cancel the relevant part of the initial
notice by notice in the prescribed form given to—

46.3.52A.4.a

the registered building control approver, and

46.3.52A.4.b

the person shown in the initial notice as the person intending to carry out
the work.

46.3.52A.5

Where a local authority is required to give a notice under subsection  (4)  in
relation to higher-risk building work in England, the local authority must
give a copy of that notice to the regulator.

46.3.52A.6

A person commits an offence if they fail without reasonable excuse to—

46.3.52A.6.a

give to a local authority a notice that the person is required to give by
subsection  (1)  or  (2) ;

46.3.52A.6.b

give to the regulator a copy of a notice that the person is required to give
by subsection  (3) .

46.3.52A.7

A person guilty of an offence under  subsection (6)  is liable on summary
conviction to a fine.

46.3.52A.8

Where a notice is given under any of subsections  (1) ,  (2)  and  (4)  (a
“cancellation notice”)—

46.3.52A.8.a

the part of the initial notice to which the cancellation notice relates is
cancelled with effect from the day on which the cancellation notice is given,
and

46.3.52A.8.b

a new initial notice may not be given in relation to any of the work to which
the cancelled part of the initial notice related.

46.3.52A.9

In this section “ the relevant part of the initial notice ” means so much of
the initial notice as relates to work that has become higher-risk building
work.

########### Effect of initial notice ceasing to be in force where work becomes higher-risk building work

46.3.52B

46.3.52B.1

This section applies where an initial notice ceases to be in force, whether in
whole or in part, by virtue of section 47(4)(b) (ia)  (higher-risk building
work).

46.3.52B.2

If, before the day on which the relevant part of the initial notice ceased to
be in force, a final certificate—

46.3.52B.2.a

was given in respect of part of the work to which the relevant part of the
initial notice relates, and

46.3.52B.2.b

was accepted by the local authority,

the fact that the relevant part of the initial notice has ceased to be in
force does not affect the continuing operation of section 51(3) in relation to
that part of the work.

46.3.52B.3

The building control authority in relation to any of the uncertified work is—

46.3.52B.3.a

in England, the regulator, and

46.3.52B.3.b

in Wales, the relevant local authority (within the meaning of section  121A
(2) ).

46.3.52B.4

In subsection  (3) , the “ uncertified work ” means any of the work—

46.3.52B.4.a

to which the relevant part of the initial notice relates, and

46.3.52B.4.b

in respect of which no final certificate has been accepted by the local
authority as mentioned in subsection  (2) .

46.3.52B.5

Sections 91 (3)  (duties of the regulator) and  121A (1)  (meaning of “
building control authority ”) apply as if, in each case, the reference to
section  91ZA  or  91ZB  were a reference to section  52B ,  91ZA  or  91ZB .

46.3.52B.6

In any case where this section applies, the reference in subsection (4) of
section 36 to the date of the completion of the work in question has effect,
in relation to a notice under subsection (1) of that section, as if it were a
reference to the date on which the relevant part of the initial notice ceased
to be in force.

46.3.52B.7

In this section “ the relevant part of the initial notice ” means so much of
the initial notice as was cancelled by a notice under section  52A
(cancellation of initial notice when work becomes higher-risk building work).

46.4

In section 47 of the Building Act 1984 (giving and acceptance of initial
notice), in subsection (4)(b)—

46.4.a

omit the “or” after sub-paragraph (i);

46.4.b

after sub-paragraph (i) insert—

46.4.b.ia

it is cancelled, in whole or in part, by a notice under section  52A ,

.

46.5

In section 55 of the Building Act 1984 (appeals), after subsection (2) insert—

46.5.2A

Where a local authority cancels an initial notice, in whole or in part, by
giving a notice (a “cancellation notice”) under section  52A (4) —

46.5.2A.a

the person shown in the initial notice as the person intending to carry out
the work, or

46.5.2A.b

the registered building control approver,

may appeal to the appropriate court or tribunal.

46.5.2B

On an appeal under subsection  (2A) , the court or tribunal must determine
whether the relevant part of the initial notice was properly cancelled.

46.5.2C

In a case where the court or tribunal determines that the relevant part of the
initial notice was not properly cancelled—

46.5.2C.a

the determination does not have the effect of reinstating the relevant part of
the initial notice;

46.5.2C.b

section  52B (2)  and  (6)  continue to apply in relation to the relevant part
of the initial notice;

46.5.2C.c

a new initial notice relating to any of the work to which the relevant part of
the original initial notice related (the “original work”) may be given only if
the new initial notice—

46.5.2C.c.i

is given before the end of the period of seven days beginning with the day on
which the appeal is determined or such other period as may be prescribed, and

46.5.2C.c.ii

relates to all of the original work, except for any work in respect of which a
final certificate has been accepted by the local authority;

46.5.2C.d

the court or tribunal may give such directions as it considers appropriate in
consequence of the determination (which may include giving directions to the
regulator).

46.5.2D

Where—

46.5.2D.a

a plans certificate has been given in respect of any of the original work,

46.5.2D.b

the conditions in paragraphs (a) and (b) of section 53(2) are fulfilled with
respect to that certificate, and

46.5.2D.c

a new initial notice as referred to in subsection  (2C) (c)  is accepted,

section 50 (1C)  does not apply in relation to so much of the work to which
the new initial notice relates as is work specified in the plans certificate.

46.5.2E

Where—

46.5.2E.a

a new initial notice is given in accordance with subsection  (2C) (c) , and

46.5.2E.b

the registered building control approver shown in the new initial notice is
different to the registered building control approver shown in the original
initial notice,

sections  53B  to  53E  apply as if any reference in those sections to a new
initial notice given in accordance with section 53(7)(a) were a reference to a
new initial notice given in accordance with section 55 (2C) (c) .

46.5.2F

In this section the “ relevant part of the initial notice ” means so much of
the initial notice as was subject to the cancellation notice.

##### Higher-risk building work: public bodies

47

After section 54 of the Building Act 1984 insert—

######### Public bodies and higher-risk building work

47.54A

47.54A.1

The appropriate national authority may by regulations make such amendments of

47.54A.2

47.54A.2.a

47.54A.2.b

47.54A.2.c

Schedule 4.

##### Plans certificates

49

49.1

The Building Act 1984 is amended as follows.

49.2

In section 50 (plans certificates)—

49.2.a

for subsection (1) substitute—

49.2.a.1

In this Part a “ plans certificate ” means a certificate by a registered
building control approver that the relevant conditions are met in relation to
the work specified in the certificate (which must be work in relation to which
the approver has given an initial notice).

49.2.a.1A

The relevant conditions are that the registered building control approver—

49.2.a.1A.a

has inspected—

49.2.a.1A.a.i

full plans of the work, or

49.2.a.1A.a.ii

plans of the work that the approver is satisfied are sufficient for the
purposes of giving a plans certificate in relation to the work,

49.2.a.1A.b

is satisfied that the plans are not defective,

49.2.a.1A.c

is satisfied that work carried out in accordance with the plans would not
contravene any provision of building regulations, and

49.2.a.1A.d

has complied with any prescribed requirements as to consultation or otherwise.

49.2.a.1B

Subsection  (1C)  applies if the person intending to carry out work to which
an initial notice relates asks the registered building control approver who
gave the initial notice to give a plans certificate in respect of the work.

49.2.a.1C

If the relevant conditions are met, the approver must give a plans certificate
to the local authority and the person intending to carry out the work.

49.2.a.1D

A plans certificate must be in the prescribed form.

;

49.2.b

in subsection (4) for “certificate under  subsection (1)  above” substitute
“plans certificate” ;

49.2.c

after subsection (7) insert—

49.2.c.7A

Building regulations may make further provision in connection with plans
certificates, including in particular provision—

49.2.c.7A.a

requiring a plans certificate to be given to the local authority in prescribed
cases;

49.2.c.7A.b

about the consequences of failing to comply with such a requirement (for
example, for an initial notice to cease to have effect in whole or in part);

49.2.c.7A.c

requiring a plans certificate stating that the condition in  subsection (1A)
(a) (ii)  is met to include prescribed information about the further plans
that the registered building control approver considers need to be provided.

49.3

In  paragraph 2  of  Schedule 4  (public body’s plans certificates)—

49.3.a

for sub-paragraph (1) substitute—

49.3.a.1

In this Part a “ public body’s plans certificate ” means a certificate by a
public body that the relevant conditions are met in relation to the work
specified in the certificate (which must be work in relation to which the
public body has given a public body’s notice).

49.3.a.1A

The relevant conditions are that the public body—

49.3.a.1A.a

is satisfied that—

49.3.a.1A.a.i

a competent person has inspected full plans of the work, or

49.3.a.1A.a.ii

a competent person has inspected plans of the work which the public body is
satisfied, in the light of that inspection, are sufficient for the purposes of
giving a public body’s plans certificate in relation to the work,

49.3.a.1A.b

is satisfied in the light of that inspection that the plans are not defective,

49.3.a.1A.c

is satisfied in the light of that inspection that work carried out in
accordance with the plans would not contravene any provision of building
regulations, and

49.3.a.1A.d

has complied with any prescribed requirements as to consultation or otherwise.

49.3.a.1B

“ Competent person ” means a servant or agent of the public body who is
competent to assess the plans.

49.3.a.1C

If the relevant conditions are met, the public body may give a public body’s
plans certificate to the local authority.

49.3.a.1D

A public body’s plans certificate must be in the prescribed form.

;

49.3.b

after sub-paragraph (6) insert—

49.3.b.7

Building regulations may make further provision about public body’s plans
certificates, including in particular provision—

49.3.b.7.a

requiring a public body’s plans certificate to be given to the local authority
in prescribed cases;

49.3.b.7.b

about the consequences of failing to comply with such a requirement (for
example, for a public body’s notice to cease to have effect in whole or in
part);

49.3.b.7.c

requiring a public body’s plans certificate stating that the condition in
sub-paragraph (1A) (a) (ii)  is met to include prescribed information about
the further plans that the public body considers need to be provided.

##### Cancellation of initial notice

50

50.1

Section 52 of the Building Act 1984 (cancellation of initial notice) is
amended in accordance with this section.

50.2

In  subsection (1) —

50.2.a

omit the “or” after  paragraph (b) ;

50.2.b

after  paragraph (c) , insert—

50.2.b.d

the registered building control approver is given a disciplinary order under
section  58U (2) (b)  (variation of registration) such that the registered
building control approver is no longer able to carry out the registered
building control approver’s functions with respect to the work to which the
initial notice relates,

50.2.b.e

the registered building control approver is given a disciplinary order under
section  58U (2) (c)  (suspension of registration) or an order under section
58V  (interim suspension for suspected serious contravention), or

50.2.b.f

it appears to the registered building control approver that a prescribed
circumstance exists,

;

50.2.c

for “approved inspector shall” substitute  “registered building control
approver, or in the case of paragraph (e) the person shown in the initial
notice as the registered building control approver, must” .

50.3

For  subsection (3)  substitute—

50.3.3

If, at a time when an initial notice is in force, it appears to the person
carrying out or intending to carry out the work to which the notice relates
that—

50.3.3.a

the registered building control approver is no longer willing or able to carry
out the registered building control approver’s functions with respect to any
of that work, or

50.3.3.b

a prescribed circumstance exists,

the person must cancel the initial notice by notice in the prescribed form
given to the local authority concerned and, if it is practicable to do so, to
the registered building control approver.

50.4

In  subsection (4) , after “subsection” insert  “(1) or” .

50.5

After  subsection (5)  insert—

50.5.5A

If, at a time when an initial notice is in force, it appears to the local
authority concerned that a condition in subsection  (5B)  is satisfied, the
authority must cancel the initial notice by notice in the prescribed form
given to—

50.5.5A.a

the person shown in the initial notice as the registered building control
approver, and

50.5.5A.b

the person shown in the initial notice as the person intending to carry out
the work.

50.5.5B

The conditions are—

50.5.5B.a

the registered building control approver is given a disciplinary order under
section  58U (2) (b)  (variation of registration) such that the registered
building control approver is no longer able to carry out the registered
building control approver’s functions with respect to the work to which the
initial notice relates;

50.5.5B.b

the registered building control approver is given a disciplinary order under
section  58U (2) (c)  (suspension of registration) or an order under section
58V  (interim suspension for suspected serious contravention);

50.5.5B.c

the registered building control approver is given a disciplinary order under
section  58U (2) (d)  (cancellation of registration);

50.5.5B.d

the registered building control approver has their registration cancelled
under section  58Z6 (2)  (serious contravention notices);

50.5.5B.e

a prescribed circumstance exists.

50.6

After  subsection (6)  insert—

50.6.7

Before cancelling an initial notice under subsection  (5A)  based on a
condition in subsection  (5B) (a) ,  (b)  or  (e) , the local authority must—

50.6.7.a

give the person shown in the initial notice as the registered building control
approver a notice in the prescribed form at least seven days before the day on
which the initial notice is to be cancelled, and

50.6.7.b

have regard to any representations made to the local authority during that
period.

##### New initial notices

51

51.1

In section 53 of the Building Act 1984 (effect of initial notice ceasing to be
in force), for subsection (7) substitute—

51.1.7

A new initial notice relating to any of the work to which the original initial
notice related (the “original work”) may be given only if—

51.1.7.a

in the case of an initial notice that ceases to be in force by virtue of—

51.1.7.a.i

being cancelled under section 52(1)(d) or (e),

51.1.7.a.ii

being cancelled under section 52 (5A)  based on a condition in section 52 (5B)
(a)  to  (d) , or

51.1.7.a.iii

such other provision as may be prescribed,

the conditions in subsection  (8)  are met, or

51.1.7.b

in any other case, the conditions in subsection  (9)  are met.

51.1.8

The conditions referred to in subsection  (7) (a)  are that the new initial
notice—

51.1.8.a

is given before the end of the period of seven days beginning with the day on
which the original initial notice ceased to be in force or such other period
as may be prescribed,

51.1.8.b

relates to all of the original work, except for any work in respect of which a
final certificate has been accepted by the local authority, and

51.1.8.c

is not a combined initial notice and plans certificate given in accordance
with section 50(4).

51.1.9

The conditions referred to in subsection  (7) (b)  are that—

51.1.9.a

before the original initial notice ceases to be in force, the original
registered building control approver has given a final certificate under
section 51 in respect of any part of the work which they are satisfied has
been completed, and

51.1.9.b

the new initial notice relates to all of the original work, except for any
work in respect of which a final certificate has been accepted by the local
authority.

51.1.10

Where—

51.1.10.a

a plans certificate has been given in respect of any of the original work,

51.1.10.b

the conditions in paragraphs (a) and (b) of subsection (2) are fulfilled with
respect to that certificate, and

51.1.10.c

a new initial notice as referred to in subsection  (7)  is accepted,

section 50 (1C)  does not apply in relation to so much of the work to which
the new initial notice relates as is work specified in the plans certificate.

51.1.11

Section 53B applies in relation to a new initial notice given in accordance
with subsection  (7) (a) .

51.1.12

The appropriate national authority may issue guidance about the process for—

51.1.12.a

the giving of a new initial notice under subsection  (7) ;

51.1.12.b

the giving of a transfer certificate and a transfer report under section  53B
;

51.1.12.c

the consideration of a transfer certificate and a transfer report under
section  53C .

51.1.13

The appropriate national authority may revise or withdraw any issued guidance.

51.1.14

The following must have regard to guidance issued under subsection  (12) —

51.1.14.a

a local authority;

51.1.14.b

a registered building control approver;

51.1.14.c

a person carrying out or intending to carry out work to which a new initial
notice given under subsection  (7)  relates.

51.2

After section  53A  of the Building Act 1984 (inserted by section 36) insert—

########### New initial notice: change of registered building control approver

51.2.53B

51.2.53B.1

This section applies where a new initial notice is given in accordance with
section 53 (7) (a)  (change of registered building control approver in certain
cases).

51.2.53B.2

Where the new initial notice is accepted by the local authority the registered
building control approver must take all reasonable steps to determine whether
the unfinished work contravenes any provision of building regulations
(including where necessary by carrying out inspections and laying open any
work).

51.2.53B.3

If the registered building control approver determines that the unfinished
work does not contravene any provision of building regulations, the approver
must give a transfer certificate and a transfer report to the local authority
before the end of the relevant period.

51.2.53B.4

If the registered building control approver is unable to make the
determination referred to in subsection  (3) , the approver must—

51.2.53B.4.a

give the person carrying out or intending to carry out the work a notice
setting out why they were unable to make the determination, and

51.2.53B.4.b

give a copy of that notice to the local authority.

51.2.53B.5

A transfer certificate must—

51.2.53B.5.a

confirm that the registered building control approver has determined that the
unfinished work up to the date of the certificate does not contravene any
provision of building regulations, and

51.2.53B.5.b

contain the prescribed information.

51.2.53B.6

A transfer report must contain any plans, documents or other information
related to the confirmation in subsection  (5) (a) .

51.2.53B.7

In this section the “ relevant period ” means—

51.2.53B.7.a

the period of 21 days beginning with the day on which the new initial notice
is accepted or such other period as may be prescribed, or

51.2.53B.7.b

such longer period as may be agreed by the local authority following a request
from the registered building control approver.

51.2.53B.8

A transfer certificate given by a registered building control approver—

51.2.53B.8.a

does not impose any liability, whether civil or criminal, on the registered
building control approver for any work carried out by the previous registered
building control approver, and

51.2.53B.8.b

does not affect any liability, whether civil or criminal, of the previous
registered building control approver for work carried out by that approver.

51.2.53B.9

In this section “ unfinished work ” means all of the work to which the
original initial notice related, except for any work in respect of which a
final certificate was accepted by the local authority.

########### Consideration of transfer certificate and report

51.2.53C

51.2.53C.1

This section applies where a registered building control approver gives a
transfer certificate and a transfer report to a local authority in accordance
with section  53B (3) .

51.2.53C.2

The local authority must, by notice, accept or reject the certificate and
report before the end of the relevant period.

51.2.53C.3

The local authority may reject the certificate and report only if—

51.2.53C.3.a

any of the prescribed grounds exist, or

51.2.53C.3.b

the registered building control approver fails to comply with a requirement in
subsection  (4)  to give information to the local authority.

51.2.53C.4

During the period of 21 days beginning with the day on which the transfer
certificate and transfer report is given to the local authority or such other
period as may be prescribed, the local authority may, by notice, require the
registered building control approver to give to the local authority such
information as may be specified in the notice.

51.2.53C.5

The registered building control approver must give the information specified
in the notice to the local authority before the end of the period of seven
days beginning with the day on which the notice is given or such other period
as may be prescribed.

51.2.53C.6

In this section the “ relevant period ” means—

51.2.53C.6.a

the period of 21 days beginning with the day on which the transfer certificate
and transfer report is given to the local authority or such other period as
may be prescribed, or

51.2.53C.6.b

such longer period as is determined in accordance with subsection  (7) .

51.2.53C.7

Where—

51.2.53C.7.a

a local authority requires a registered building control approver to give
information to the local authority under subsection  (4) , and

51.2.53C.7.b

the day by which the information is required to be given would (but for this
subsection) fall within the final seven days of the relevant period or would
fall outside the relevant period,

the relevant period is to be extended to the end of the period of seven days
beginning with the day after the day by which the information is required to
be given.

51.2.53C.8

Where a local authority requires a registered building control approver to
give information to the local authority under subsection  (4) , the local
authority must give a copy of the notice to the person shown in the initial
notice as the person intending to carry out the work.

########### Cancellation of initial notice: change of registered building control approver

51.2.53D

51.2.53D.1

This section applies where—

51.2.53D.1.a
