a new initial notice is given in accordance with section 53 (7) (a)  (change
of registered building control approver in certain cases), and

51.2.53D.1.b

the notice is accepted by the local authority.

51.2.53D.2

If, at a time when the initial notice is in force—

51.2.53D.2.a

the registered building control approver does not give the local authority a
transfer certificate and transfer report in accordance with section  53B (3) ,
or

51.2.53D.2.b

the local authority rejects the transfer certificate and transfer report in
accordance with section  53C ,

the local authority must cancel the initial notice by notice in the prescribed
form given to the registered building control approver and the person shown in
the initial notice as the person intending to carry out the work.

51.2.53D.3

The person carrying out or intending to carry out the work to which the
initial notice relates may, at a time—

51.2.53D.3.a

when the initial notice is in force, and

51.2.53D.3.b

before the local authority accepts or rejects the transfer certificate and
report in accordance with section  53C ,

cancel the initial notice by notice in the prescribed form given to the local
authority and, if it is practicable to do so, to the registered building
control approver.

51.2.53D.4

A notice under subsection  (2)  or  (3)  has the effect of cancelling the
initial notice to which it relates with effect from the day on which the
notice is given.

51.2.53D.5

Where an initial notice ceases to be in force by virtue of subsection  (2)  or
(3) , a new initial notice may not, except in prescribed circumstances, be
given in relation to any of the work to which the cancelled notice related.

51.2.53D.6

Where an initial notice ceases to be in force by virtue of subsection  (2)  or
(3) —

51.2.53D.6.a

for the purpose of enabling the local authority to perform the functions
referred to in section 48(1) in relation to any part of the work, building
regulations may require the local authority to be provided with plans that
relate to that part of the work, and

51.2.53D.6.b

section 53(5) applies in relation to the notice as it applies in relation to
an initial notice that ceases to be in force as referred to in section 53(1).

51.2.53D.7

This section is without prejudice to any other provisions of this Part
relating to when an initial notice ceases to be in force.

########### Restriction on functions of registered building control approvers

51.2.53E

51.2.53E.1

This section applies where—

51.2.53E.1.a

a new initial notice is given in accordance with section 53 (7) (a)  (change
of registered building control approver in certain cases), and

51.2.53E.1.b

the notice is accepted by the local authority.

51.2.53E.2

During the period in respect of which—

51.2.53E.2.a

the notice is in force, but

51.2.53E.2.b

a transfer certificate and a transfer report have not been accepted by the
local authority,

the registered building control approver may not exercise the relevant
functions.

51.2.53E.3

In this section the “relevant functions” are the functions of a registered
building control approver under, or under regulations made under—

51.2.53E.3.a

section 50 (plans certificates);

51.2.53E.3.b

section 51 (final certificates);

51.2.53E.3.c

section 51A (amendment notices).

51.3

In section 47 of the Building Act 1984 (giving and acceptance of initial
notice)—

51.3.a

in  subsection (4) (b) , after sub-paragraph  (ia)  (inserted by section 46)
insert—

51.3.a.ib

it is cancelled by a notice under section  53D , or

;

51.3.b

after subsection (7) insert—

51.3.b.8

This section is subject to sections 53 and  53B  (new initial notices).

51.4

In section 55 of the Building Act 1984 (appeals)—

51.4.a

in  subsection (1) —

51.4.a.i

omit the “or” after  paragraph (a) ;

51.4.a.ii

after  paragraph (b)  insert

or

51.4.a.ii.c

a transfer certificate and a transfer report,

;

51.4.b

in  subsection (2) (a), after “notice” insert  “, report” ;

51.4.c

in  subsection (2) (b), after “notice” insert  “, report” .

##### Information gathering

52

52.1

In section 53 of the Building Act 1984 (effect of initial notice ceasing to be
in force), after subsection (4) insert—

52.1.4A

For the purpose of enabling the local authority to perform the functions
referred to in section 48(1), the local authority may by notice require the
person shown in the initial notice as the registered building control approver
to give the local authority—

52.1.4A.a

any information the authority would have obtained if the authority had
performed the function of enforcing building regulations in relation to the
work to which the initial notice relates during the period in which the
initial notice was in force, and

52.1.4A.b

any other information the local authority may reasonably require.

52.1.4B

Where a person is required to give information under subsection  (4A) , the
information must be given before the end of the prescribed period.

52.1.4C

The person shown in the initial notice as the registered building control
approver (the “outgoing approver”) must, before the end of the prescribed
period, give the person carrying out or intending to carry out the work to
which the initial notice relates—

52.1.4C.a

any information given to a local authority under subsection  (4A) ,

52.1.4C.b

any other information that the outgoing approver obtained or created in
relation to the work during the period in which the initial notice was in
force, and

52.1.4C.c

any other information that the person carrying out or intending to carry out
the work may by notice reasonably require for the purpose of enabling a person
other than the outgoing approver to perform the functions referred to in
section 48(1) in relation to the work.

52.1.4D

A notice under subsection  (4C) (c) —

52.1.4D.a

may only require information to be given in relation to work carried out
during the period in which the initial notice was in force;

52.1.4D.b

may require information to be provided in a specified format.

52.2

In section 57 of the Building Act 1984 (offences), in subsection (1)—

52.2.a

omit the “or” after paragraph (a);

52.2.b

after paragraph (a) insert—

52.2.b.aa

fails without reasonable excuse to comply with a requirement under section 53
(4A)  to give information, or

.

##### Information

53

53.1

After section 56 of the Building Act 1984 insert—

########### Giving information by electronic means: England

53.1.56A

53.1.56A.1

The regulator must establish and maintain a facility (the “facility”) to
enable a specified person to give specified relevant information to another
person by electronic communication.

53.1.56A.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations require or authorise a specified
person to use the facility when giving specified relevant information to
another person.

53.1.56A.3

Any information given to a person in accordance with regulations made under
subsection  (2)  is to be treated for the purposes of section  56B
(requirement to keep register) as also having been given to the regulator.

53.1.56A.4

Regulations under this section may require a person who is given specified
relevant information otherwise than through the facility to give that
information to the regulator using the facility.

53.1.56A.5

Regulations under this section may make provision treating specified relevant
information that is given using the facility as having been given in the
prescribed form for the purposes of this Part.

53.1.56A.6

In this section—

“ relevant information ” means information that is required or authorised to
be given by this Part or regulations made under it; “ specified ” means
specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State under this section.

53.1.56A.7

In this section and section  56B —

“ information ” includes documents; “ documents ” includes notices,
certificates, orders, consents, demands and plans.

53.1.56A.8

The Secretary of State may make regulations under this section only in
relation to England.

########### Requirement to keep register: England

53.1.56B

53.1.56B.1

The regulator must keep a register of specified relevant information.

53.1.56B.2

The information that may be specified for the purposes of subsection  (1)
includes in particular information given, or treated as having been given, to
the regulator using the facility established under section  56A (1) .

53.1.56B.3

The regulator—

53.1.56B.3.a

must maintain the register in electronic form;

53.1.56B.3.b

must ensure that any specified parts of the register are available for
inspection by members of the public;

53.1.56B.3.c

must, in specified circumstances, provide to members of the public, on
request, copies of information kept in the register.

53.1.56B.4

In this section—

“ relevant information ” means information that is required or authorised to
be given by this Part or regulations made under it; “ specified ” means
specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State under this section.

53.1.56B.5

The Secretary of State may make regulations under this section only in
relation to England.

########### Delegation of functions

53.1.56C

53.1.56C.1

The regulator may by written notice delegate to a person, to such extent and
subject to such conditions as the regulator considers appropriate, the
functions conferred on the regulator by—

53.1.56C.1.a

section  56A (1) ;

53.1.56C.1.b

section  56B (1)  and  (3)  (including the ability to charge fees in
connection with the exercise of those functions).

53.1.56C.2

In subsection  (1)  “ fees ” means fees that are prescribed by, or determined
by the regulator in accordance with, regulations under section  105B .

53.1.56C.3

The regulator may delegate different functions to different persons under
subsection  (1) .

53.1.56C.4

The regulator may delegate functions under subsection  (1)  only with the
consent of the Secretary of State.

53.1.56C.5

The regulator may revoke a delegation of functions to a person by giving a
written notice to the person.

53.1.56C.6

The regulator may revoke a delegation under subsection  (5)  only with the
consent of the Secretary of State.

53.1.56C.7

Schedule  3  to the Building Safety Act 2022 (information sharing) applies as
if references to the regulator included references to a person to whom the
regulator has delegated functions under subsection  (1) (b) .

53.2

In section 55 of the Building Act 1984 (appeals), after subsection (3) insert—

53.2.4

On an appeal under subsection (1), the local authority must give the specified
information to the regulator.

53.2.5

In this section “ specified ” means specified in regulations made by the
Secretary of State under this section.

53.2.6

The Secretary of State may make regulations under this section only in
relation to England.

53.3

In section 56 of the Building Act 1984 (recording and furnishing of
information)—

53.3.a

in subsection (1)—

53.3.a.i

after “authority” insert  “in Wales” ;

53.3.a.ii

after “public body’s notices” insert  “, transfer reports” ;

53.3.a.iii

after “such notices” insert  “, reports” ;

53.3.b

in subsection (3), after “plans certificates, final certificates” insert  “,
transfer certificates” ;

53.3.c

in subsection (4), after “section” insert  “by a local authority in Wales” .

#### Miscellaneous and general

##### Functions under Part 3 of Building Act 1984

54

In the Building Act 1984 after section 90 insert—

######### Functions under this Part: the regulator etc

54.90A

54.90A.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that in specified cases, a
specified function under this Part of local authorities in England is to be a
function of the regulator instead of, or in addition to, the local authority
in question.

54.90A.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that in specified cases, a
relevant authority proposing to exercise a specified function under this Part
must notify a specified relevant authority of specified matters.

54.90A.3

The notification must be made in the specified way and by the specified time.

54.90A.4

In this section—

“ relevant authority ” means the regulator or a local authority for an area in
England; “ specified ” means specified by regulations under this section.

##### Minor and consequential amendments

55

Schedule 5  contains—

55.a

minor amendments of the Building Act 1984, and

55.b

amendments consequential on provision made by  this Part .

##### Appeals

56

Schedule 6  makes provision about appeals under the Building Act 1984,
including provision providing for—

56.a

certain appeals to be made to the regulator instead of the Secretary of State,

56.b

certain appeals relating to buildings in England to be made to the tribunal
instead of a magistrates’ court, and

56.c

a right of appeal against a decision of a local authority not to consider
certain applications or notices on the ground that they are in respect of
higher-risk building work.

##### Fees and charges

57

In the Building Act 1984 after  section 105A  (inserted by  paragraph 29  of
Schedule 6 ) insert—

######### Fees, charges and levies

########## Fees and charges

57.105B

57.105B.1

The appropriate national authority may by regulations make provision
authorising a relevant authority—

57.105B.1.a

to charge fees, and

57.105B.1.b

to recover charges,

for or in connection with the performance of any of its functions under, or
under an instrument made under, this Act.

57.105B.2

The regulations may—

57.105B.2.a

prescribe a fee or charge, or

57.105B.2.b

provide for the amount of any fee or charge to be determined by the relevant
authority in accordance with the regulations;

and may make provision about the effect of failing to pay a fee or charge in
accordance with the regulations.

57.105B.3

The regulations may in particular—

57.105B.3.a

provide that the amount of any charge is to be determined by the relevant
authority in accordance with a scheme made and published by it, and

57.105B.3.b

make provision about such schemes, including the principles to be embodied in
such schemes.

57.105B.4

In this section “ relevant authority ” means—

57.105B.4.a

in relation to England, the regulator or a local authority for an area in
England;

57.105B.4.b

in relation to Wales, the Welsh Ministers or a local authority for an area in
Wales.

##### Levy on applications for building control approval etc

58

In the Building Act 1984 after  section 105B  (inserted by section 57) insert—

######### Levy on certain applications for building control approval etc

58.105C

58.105C.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for and in connection
with the imposition, in respect of relevant applications or notices or
specified descriptions of relevant applications or notices, of a levy for the
purpose of meeting any building safety expenditure.

58.105C.2

The levy is payable to the Secretary of State or a person designated by the
Secretary of State.

58.105C.3

The regulations may in particular make provision about—

58.105C.3.a

the amount of the levy;

58.105C.3.b

the person by whom it must be paid;

58.105C.3.c

when the levy must be paid;

58.105C.3.d

the provision of information or documents to, or by, the Secretary of State or
designated person;

58.105C.3.e

the consequences of a failure to pay the levy in accordance with the
regulations;

58.105C.3.f

the determination of disputes (including provision conferring a right to
appeal to the tribunal and provision about appeals).

58.105C.4

The different provision that may be made by the regulations by virtue of
section 120A(2)(b) includes in particular different provision in relation to—

58.105C.4.a

persons who are eligible to be members of a building industry scheme and are
not members of that scheme, and

58.105C.4.b

other persons.

58.105C.5

The regulations may contain exemptions, for specified descriptions of person.

58.105C.6

The regulations may provide that, unless the building control authority is
given a notification under subsection  (7)  in relation to a relevant
application or notice (or a relevant application or notice of a specified
description), the authority—

58.105C.6.a

may not take a specified step in relation to the application or notice (for
example, may not grant an application, accept a notice or give a specified
certificate in relation to works connected with the application or notice), or

58.105C.6.b

must take a specified step in relation to the application or notice (for
example, must reject a notice).

58.105C.7

A notification under this section is a notification given by the Secretary of
State or designated person—

58.105C.7.a

that the levy payable in respect of the application or notice has been paid,
or

58.105C.7.b

that no levy is payable in respect of the application or notice.

58.105C.8

The regulations must provide for any amount received by a designated person by
way of a levy to be paid to the Secretary of State, subject to retention of an
amount, determined by or in accordance with the regulations, in respect of the
costs of administering the levy.

58.105C.9

A designation under this section must be published in such way as the
Secretary of State considers appropriate.

58.105C.10

In this section “ relevant application or notice ” means—

58.105C.10.a

an application for building control approval,

58.105C.10.b

an initial notice,

58.105C.10.c

an amendment notice, or

58.105C.10.d

a public body’s notice,

relating to a relevant building or proposed relevant building (including any
such application or notice relating to work that causes a building to become a
relevant building or causes a relevant building to cease to be such a
building).

58.105C.11

In this section—

“ amendment notice, “initial notice” and “public body’s notice ” have the same
meaning as in Part 2 (see section 58); “ building industry scheme ” means a
scheme established under section 126 of the Building Safety Act 2022; “
building safety expenditure ” means expenditure incurred by the Secretary of
State (whether before or after the passing of this Act) in providing financial
assistance to persons (whether by way of grant, loan or otherwise) for the
purposes of enabling them to improve the safety of persons in or about
buildings in England; “ relevant building ” means a building in England
consisting of or containing— one or more dwellings, or other accommodation,
(and “accommodation” here includes temporary accommodation, for example in a
hotel or hospital); “ specified ” means specified in the regulations.

##### Crown application

59

In Part 5 of the Building Act 1984 before section 132 insert—

######### Crown application

59.131A

59.131A.1

The following provisions bind the Crown—

59.131A.1.a

Part 1 except sections 35B to 37, 39A and 40;

59.131A.1.b

Part 2;

59.131A.1.c

Part 2A except sections 58I to 58K, 58U, 58V and 58Z4 to 58Z6;

59.131A.1.d

Part 4 so far as it relates to a provision within any of the preceding
paragraphs.

59.131A.2

No contravention by the Crown of a provision within subsection (1)(a) to (d)
makes the Crown criminally liable.

59.131A.3

Subsection  (2)  does not affect the criminal liability of persons in the
service of the Crown.

59.131A.4

Subsection (5) applies where—

59.131A.4.a

a contravention of a provision within subsection (1)(a) or (b), or of Part 4
so far as it relates to such a provision, occurs in relation to a building or
proposed building for which a local authority is the building control
authority, or

59.131A.4.b

a contravention of a provision within subsection (1)(c), or of Part 4 so far
as it relates to such a provision, occurs in relation to Wales,

and the Crown would, but for subsection (2), be criminally liable under this
Act in respect of the contravention.

59.131A.5

The High Court may, on the application of—

59.131A.5.a

the local authority (in a case within subsection (4)(a)), or

59.131A.5.b

the Welsh Ministers (in a case within subsection (4)(b)),

declare unlawful the act or omission constituting the contravention.

59.131A.6

In this section a reference to a provision includes any instrument made under
it.

59.131A.7

For the application to the Crown of Part 3, and Part 4 so far as it relates to
that Part, see section 87.

##### Application to Parliament

60

60.1

The Building Act 1984 is amended as follows.

60.2

In section 95 (power to enter premises) after subsection (4) insert—

60.2.5

This section does not apply in relation to the Parliamentary Estate (as
defined by section 131B).

60.3

After section 131A (inserted by section 59) insert—

########### Parts 1 and 2 etc: application to Parliament

60.3.131B

60.3.131B.1

In their application in relation to the Parliamentary Estate, Parts 1 and 2,
and Part 4 so far as it relates to those Parts, have effect with the following
modifications—

60.3.131B.1.a

sections 35B to 37, 39A and 40 (enforcement etc) do not apply;

60.3.131B.1.b

any reference to the owner or occupier of a building or of any premises is be
read as a reference to—

60.3.131B.1.b.i

the Corporate Officer of the House of Lords,

60.3.131B.1.b.ii

the Corporate Officer of the House of Commons, or (as the case may be)

60.3.131B.1.b.iii

the Corporate Officers acting jointly.

60.3.131B.2

In the following provisions—

“ Corporate Officer ” means— the Corporate Officer of the House of Lords, the
Corporate Officer of the House of Commons, or the Corporate Officers acting
jointly; “ relevant provision ” means— any provision of, or of an instrument
made under, Part 1 or 2, or any provision of Part 4 or of an instrument made
under Part 4, so far as the provision relates to Part 1 or 2.

60.3.131B.3

No contravention by a Corporate Officer of a relevant provision makes the
Corporate Officer criminally liable.

60.3.131B.4

Subsection (3) does not affect the criminal liability of relevant members of
the House of Lords staff or of the House of Commons staff (as defined by
sections 194 and 195 of the Employment Rights Act 1996).

60.3.131B.5

Where a contravention of a relevant provision occurs which, but for subsection
(3), would result in a Corporate Officer being criminally liable, the High
Court may, on the application of the local authority, declare unlawful the act
or omission constituting the contravention.

60.3.131B.6

In this section “ the Parliamentary Estate ” means any building or other
premises occupied for the purposes of either House of Parliament.

### Higher-risk buildings

#### Introduction

##### Overview of Part

61

61.1

This Part  contains provisions about the management of building safety risks
as regards occupied higher-risk buildings.

61.2

In  this Part —

61.2.a

sections 62 to 64 define “building safety risk” and make related provision;

61.2.b

sections 65 to 70 define “higher-risk building”, make related provision, and
confer power to modify  this Part  as it applies in relation to any
description of higher-risk building;

61.2.c

sections 71 to 75 contain other key definitions, including—

61.2.c.i

when a building is “occupied”;

61.2.c.ii

the definition of “accountable person” and “principal accountable person”;

and provide that the First-tier Tribunal may determine who is an accountable
person or the principal accountable person for a higher-risk building;

61.2.d

sections 76 to 82  make provision about the registration of higher-risk
buildings and about building assessment certificates;

61.2.e

sections 83 to 86 make provision about the assessment and management of
building safety risks, including provision requiring a safety case report to
be prepared and revised;

61.2.f

sections 87 to 90 contain provisions about the keeping and giving of
information and documents to the regulator, other accountable persons,
residents and others;

61.2.g

sections 91 to 94 contain provisions about engagement with residents etc,
including—

61.2.g.i

provision requiring a residents’ engagement strategy to be prepared and
revised;

61.2.g.ii

provision requiring complaints systems to be established and operated;

61.2.h

sections 95 to 97 impose duties on residents and make provision for the
enforcement of those duties;

61.2.i

section 98 to 101 contain provisions about the enforcement of  this Part ;

61.2.j

section 102 and  Schedule 7  provide for the appointment of a special measures
manager, to undertake duties under  this Part  in place of an accountable
person, and make further provision in connection with that appointment;

61.2.k

sections 103 to 107 contain provisions about appeals;

61.2.l

sections 108 to 111 contain miscellaneous provisions, including provision
about cooperation and coordination;

61.2.m

sections 112 to 114 provide for certain terms to be implied into leases, and
contain other provisions affecting the relationship between landlord and
tenant or affecting commonholds;

61.2.n

section 115 contains definitions applying for the purposes of  this Part .

#### Meaning of “building safety risk”

##### Meaning of “building safety risk”

62

62.1

In  this Part  “ building safety risk ” means a risk to the safety of people
in or about a building arising from any of the following occurring as regards
the building—

62.1.a

the spread of fire;

62.1.b

structural failure;

62.1.c

any other prescribed matter.

62.2

Before making regulations under  subsection (1) (c) , the Secretary of State
must consult—

62.2.a

the regulator, and

62.2.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

62.3

But the regulator need not be consulted if—

62.3.a

the regulations give effect to a recommendation made by the regulator under
section 63, or

62.3.b

the Secretary of State has under section 64 asked the regulator for its advice
in relation to a proposal to make the regulations.

##### Recommendations about regulations under section 62

63

63.1

The regulator may recommend that the Secretary of State makes regulations
under section 62.

63.2

The regulator may make a recommendation to prescribe a matter under section 62
(1) (c)  for any higher-risk building only if it considers that if the matter
occurred as regards a higher-risk building it would have the potential to
cause a major incident.

63.3

The regulator may make a recommendation to prescribe a matter under section 62
(1) (c)  for a description of higher-risk building only if it considers that
if the matter occurred as regards a higher-risk building of that description
it would have the potential to cause a major incident.

63.4

The regulator may make a recommendation to prescribe a matter under section 62
(1) (c)  for a description of building that is not a higher-risk building only
if—

63.4.a

it considers that—

63.4.a.i

if the matter occurred as regards a building of that description it would have
the potential to cause a major incident,

63.4.a.ii

the risk of the matter occurring is greater for that description of buildings
than it is for buildings that are not of that description, and

63.4.a.iii

this Part  should apply (with or without modifications) in relation to
buildings of that description, and

63.4.b

it also recommends that buildings of that description should be higher-risk
buildings for the purposes of  this Part  (and, if section 69 (2) (b)
applies, makes a recommendation of the kind mentioned there).

63.5

The regulator may make a recommendation to make regulations that would result
in a matter ceasing to be prescribed under section 62 (1) (c)  only if—

63.5.a

where the matter is prescribed for any higher-risk building, it considers that
if the matter occurred as regards a higher-risk building it would not have the
potential to cause a major incident;

63.5.b

where the matter is prescribed for a description of higher-risk building, it
considers that if the matter occurred as regards a higher-risk building of
that description it would not have the potential to cause a major incident.

63.6

When making a recommendation, the regulator must give the Secretary of State a
statement of its assessment of the issues it considered when deciding to make
the recommendation.

63.7

If following a recommendation the Secretary of State decides not to make the
regulations, the Secretary of State must publish a document setting out—

63.7.a

the regulator’s recommendation,

63.7.b

the Secretary of State’s decision not to make the regulations, and

63.7.c

the reasons for that decision.

63.8

In  this Part  “ major incident ” means an incident resulting in—

63.8.a

a significant number of deaths, or

63.8.b

serious injury to a significant number of people.

##### Advice about regulations under section 62

64

Where the Secretary of State asks the regulator to provide advice about a
proposal to make regulations under section 62, it must provide that advice.

#### Meaning of “higher-risk building”

##### Meaning of “higher-risk building” etc

65

65.1

In  this Part  “ higher-risk building ” means a building in England that—

65.1.a

is at least 18 metres in height or has at least 7 storeys, and

65.1.b

contains at least 2 residential units.

65.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision supplementing this
section.

65.3

The regulations may in particular—

65.3.a

define “building” or “ storey ” for the purposes of this section;

65.3.b

make provision about how the height of a building is to be determined for
those purposes;

65.3.c

provide that “ higher-risk building ” does not include a building of a
prescribed description.

65.4

Regulations made by virtue of  subsection (3) (a)  may in particular define
“building” so as to provide that it includes—

65.4.a

any other structure or erection of any kind (whether temporary or permanent);

65.4.b

any vehicle, vessel or other movable object of any kind, in such circumstances
as may be prescribed.

65.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section (other than
subsection (2)  or  this subsection ).

65.6

For the meaning of “residential unit” see section 115.

##### Regulations under section 65: procedure

66

66.1

Before making regulations under section 65, the Secretary of State must
consult—

66.1.a

the regulator, and

66.1.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

66.2

But the regulator need not be consulted if—

66.2.a

the regulations give effect to a recommendation made by the regulator under
section 63 (4)  or 69, or

66.2.b

the Secretary of State has under section 70 asked the regulator for advice
about the description of building in question.

##### Regulations under section 65: additional procedure in certain cases

67

67.1

This section applies if the Secretary of State proposes to make regulations
under section 65 that would result in a description of building (including
anything within  subsection (4)  of that section) becoming a higher-risk
building for the purposes of  this Part .

67.2

The Secretary of State must ask the regulator under section 70 (1)  for advice
about the description of building, except where the regulations would give
effect to a recommendation under section 69 (2) .

67.3

The Secretary of State must carry out a cost-benefit analysis and publish it.

67.4

In this section “ cost-benefit analysis ” means—

67.4.a

an analysis of the costs together with an analysis of the benefits that will
arise if the regulations are made, and

67.4.b

an estimate of those costs and of those benefits (subject to  subsection (5)
).

67.5

If, in the opinion of the Secretary of State—

67.5.a

the costs or benefits cannot reasonably be estimated, or

67.5.b

it is not reasonably practicable to produce an estimate,

the cost-benefit analysis need not estimate them, but must include a statement
of the Secretary of State’s opinion and an explanation of it.

##### Modification of Part in relation to certain kinds of higher-risk building

68

68.1

The Secretary of State may make regulations modifying  this Part  as it
applies in relation to a prescribed description of higher-risk building.

68.2

Before making the regulations, the Secretary of State must consult—

68.2.a

the regulator, and

68.2.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

68.3

But the regulator need not be consulted if the regulations give effect to a
recommendation under section 63 (4) , 69 or 70.

##### Recommendations about definition of “higher-risk building” etc

69

69.1

Subsection (2)  applies if, in respect of any description of building that is
not a higher-risk building, the regulator considers—

69.1.a

that a building safety risk is greater for that description of buildings than
it is for buildings that are not of that description,

69.1.b

that if the risk materialised as regards a building of that description it
would have the potential to cause a major incident, and

69.1.c

that  this Part  should apply (with or without modifications) in relation to
buildings of that description.

69.2

The regulator must—

69.2.a

recommend to the Secretary of State that buildings of that description should
be higher-risk buildings for the purposes of  this Part ,

69.2.b

if it considers that regulations under section 68 should be made modifying
this Part  as it applies in relation to that description of building, make a
recommendation to the Secretary of State to that effect, and

69.2.c

give the Secretary of State a statement of its assessment of the issues it
considered when deciding to make the recommendation under  paragraph (a)  and
any recommendation under  paragraph (b) .

69.3

Subsection (4)  applies if—

69.3.a

following a recommendation under  subsection (2) (a)  the Secretary of State
decides not to make regulations under section 65 giving effect to the
recommendation, or

69.3.b

following a recommendation under  subsection (2) (b)  the Secretary of State
decides not to make regulations under section 68 giving effect to the
recommendation.

69.4

The Secretary of State must publish a document setting out—

69.4.a

the regulator’s recommendation,

69.4.b

the Secretary of State’s decision not to make the regulations, and

69.4.c

the reasons for that decision.

69.5

If the regulator considers that  this Part  should not apply in relation to a
particular description of higher-risk building, it must recommend to the
Secretary of State that buildings of that description should cease to be
higher-risk buildings for the purposes of  this Part .

69.6

For the meaning of “major incident” see section 63.

##### Advice about definition of “higher-risk building” etc

70

70.1

Subsections (2)  to  (6)  apply if the Secretary of State asks the regulator
for advice as to whether a specified description of building should be a
higher-risk building for the purposes of  this Part .

70.2

The regulator must consider whether the following conditions are met—

70.2.a

the first condition is that a building safety risk is greater for that
description of buildings than it is for buildings that are not of that
description;

70.2.b

the second condition is that, if the risk materialised as regards a building
of that description, it would have the potential to cause a major incident;

70.2.c

the third condition is that buildings of that description should be higher-
risk buildings for the purposes of  this Part .

70.3

The regulator must—

70.3.a

if the conditions mentioned in  subsection (2)  are met, recommend to the
Secretary of State that buildings of that description should be higher-risk
buildings for the purposes of  this Part ;

70.3.b

otherwise, recommend to the Secretary of State that buildings of that
description should not be higher-risk buildings for those purposes.

70.4

Where the regulator—

70.4.a

makes a recommendation under  subsection (3) (a) , and

70.4.b

considers that regulations under section 68 should be made modifying  this
Part  as it applies in relation to buildings of the specified description,

it must make a recommendation to the Secretary of State to that effect.

70.5

The regulator must give the Secretary of State a statement of its assessment
of the issues it considered when deciding to make the recommendation under
subsection (3)  and any recommendation under  subsection (4) .

70.6

If, following a recommendation under  subsection (3) (a) , the Secretary of
State decides not to make regulations under section 65 giving effect to the
recommendation, the Secretary of State must publish a document setting out—

70.6.a

the regulator’s recommendation,

70.6.b

the Secretary of State’s decision not to make the regulations, and

70.6.c

the reasons for that decision.

70.7

If requested, the regulator must provide advice to the Secretary of State as
to whether higher-risk buildings of a specified description should cease to be
higher-risk buildings for the purposes of  this Part .

70.8

In this section “ specified ” means specified by the Secretary of State in the
request.

#### Meaning of “accountable person” and other key definitions

##### Meaning of “occupied” higher-risk building etc

71

71.1

The following provisions apply for the purposes of  this Part .

71.2

A higher-risk building is “occupied” if there are residents of more than one
residential unit in the building.

71.3

A reference to a resident of a higher-risk building is to a resident of a
residential unit in such a building.

71.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

71.4.a

amend the definition of a higher-risk building being “occupied”;

71.4.b

amend the definition of a “resident” of a higher-risk building;

71.4.c

define, for the purposes of  this Part , the meaning of being a “resident” of
a residential unit.

71.5

See—

71.5.a

section 65 for the meaning of “higher-risk building”;

71.5.b

section 115 for the meaning of “residential unit”.

##### Meaning of “accountable person”

72

72.1

In  this Part  an “accountable person” for a higher-risk building is—

72.1.a

a person who holds a legal estate in possession in any part of the common
parts (subject to  subsection (2) ), or

72.1.b

a person who does not hold a legal estate in any part of the building but who
is under a relevant repairing obligation in relation to any part of the common
parts.

This subsection  is subject to  subsection (5)  (special rule for commonhold
land).

72.2

A person (“the estate owner”) who holds a legal estate in possession in the
common parts of a higher-risk building or any part of them (“the relevant
common parts”) is not an accountable person for the building by virtue of
subsection (1) (a)  if—

72.2.a

each long lease of which the estate owner is lessor provides that a particular
person, who does not hold a legal estate in any part of the building, is under
a relevant repairing obligation in relation to all of the relevant common
parts, or

72.2.b

all repairing obligations relating to the relevant common parts which would
otherwise be obligations of the estate owner are functions of an RTM company.

72.3

Subsection (4)  applies where—

72.3.a

under a lease, a person (“the estate owner”) holds a legal estate in
possession in the common parts of a higher-risk building or any part of them
(“the relevant common parts”), and

72.3.b

a landlord under the lease is under a relevant repairing obligation in
relation to any of the relevant common parts.

72.4

For the purposes of this section and section 73—

72.4.a

the legal estate in possession in so much of the relevant common parts as are
within  subsection (3) (b)  is treated as held by the landlord (instead of the
estate owner), and

72.4.b

if (and so far as) the landlord’s actual legal estate in those common parts is
held under a lease, the legal estate in possession mentioned in  paragraph (a)
is treated as held under that lease (and, accordingly,  subsection (3)  and
this subsection  may apply in relation to it).

72.5

Where a higher-risk building is on commonhold land, the commonhold association
is the accountable person for the building for the purposes of  this Part .

72.6

For the purposes of this section—

                                    “ common parts ”, in relation to a
building, means—
the structure and exterior of the building, except so far as included in a
demise of a single dwelling or of premises to be occupied for the purposes of
a business, or
any part of the building provided for the use, benefit and enjoyment of the
residents of more than one residential unit (whether alone or with other
persons);
“ commonhold association ” and “commonhold land” have the same meaning as in
Part 1 of the Commonhold and Leasehold Reform Act 2002 (see sections 34 and 1
respectively);
“ long lease ”: for the meaning of “long lease” see section 115;
“ possession ”: a reference to “ possession ” does not include the receipt of
rents and profits or the right to receive the same;
“ relevant repairing obligation ”: a person is under a relevant repairing
obligation in relation to anything if the person is required, under a lease or
by virtue of an enactment, to repair or maintain that thing;
“ RTM company ” has the same meaning as in Chapter 1 of Part 2 of the
Commonhold and Leasehold Reform Act 2002 (right to manage).

72.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section (other than  this
subsection ).

##### Meaning of “principal accountable person”

73

73.1

In  this Part  the “principal accountable person” for a higher-risk building
is—

73.1.a

in relation to a building with one accountable person, that person;

73.1.b

in relation to a building with more than one accountable person, the
accountable person who—

73.1.b.i

holds a legal estate in possession in the relevant parts of the structure and
exterior of the building, or

73.1.b.ii

is within section 72 (1) (b)  because of a relevant repairing obligation
(within the meaning of that section) in relation to the relevant parts of the
structure and exterior of the building.

73.2

For the purposes of this section—

73.2.a

the reference to “the relevant parts of the structure and exterior” of a
building is to its structure and exterior except so far as included in a
demise of a single dwelling or of premises to be occupied for the purposes of
a business;

73.2.b

the reference to “ possession ” does not include the receipt of rents and
profits or the right to receive the same.

73.3

Subsection (1) (b)  is subject to section 75 (2)  (powers of tribunal where
more than one accountable person is within  subsection (1) (b) ).

##### Part of building for which an accountable person is responsible

74

In  this Part , any reference to the part of a higher-risk building for which
an accountable person is responsible is to such part of the building
(including all of it) as is determined by or in accordance with regulations.

##### Determinations by the tribunal

75

75.1

An interested person may apply to the tribunal for a determination, as regards
a higher-risk building, of any of the following—

75.1.a

the person or persons who are accountable persons for the building;

75.1.b

the person who is the principal accountable person for the building;

75.1.c

the part of the building for which any accountable person for the building is
responsible.

75.2

Where, on an application under  subsection (1) (b) , it appears to the
tribunal that there is more than one accountable person within section 73 (1)
(b) , the principal accountable person is such one of those accountable
persons as the tribunal considers appropriate.

75.3

In this section “ interested person ” means—

75.3.a

the regulator,

75.3.b

a person who holds a legal estate in any part of the common parts (or who
claims to hold such an estate), or

75.3.c

a person who is under a relevant repairing obligation in relation to any part
of the common parts (or who claims to be under such an obligation).

75.4

In  subsection (3)  “ relevant repairing obligation ” and “ common parts ”
have the same meaning as in section 72.

#### Registration and certificates

##### Requirement for completion certificate before occupation

76

76.1

This section applies if any of the following works are carried out—

76.1.a

the construction of a higher-risk building;

76.1.b

the creation of additional residential units in such a building;

76.1.c

works to a building that cause it to become a higher-risk building.

76.2

If a relevant residential unit is occupied before a completion certificate
relating to a relevant part of the building is issued, the relevant
accountable person commits an offence.

76.3

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to
prove that the person had a reasonable excuse for the residential unit being
occupied before such a completion certificate was issued.

76.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

76.4.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

76.4.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both).

76.5

In this section—

                                    “ completion certificate ” means a
certificate of a prescribed description that is issued under regulations made
under section 1(1) of the Building Act 1984 (building regulations);
“ occupied ”: a residential unit is occupied if there is a resident of it;
“ relevant accountable person ”, in relation to a residential unit, means the
accountable person who is responsible for a relevant part of the building;
“ relevant part ” of a building, in relation to a residential unit, means a
part of the building containing the residential unit;
“ relevant residential unit ” means—
in the case of works within  subsection (1) (a) , any residential unit in the
building;
in the case of works within  subsection (1) (b) , any additional residential
unit;
in the case of works within  subsection (1) (c) , any residential unit in the
building except one that existed before the works began.

##### Occupation: registration requirement

77

77.1

The principal accountable person for a higher-risk building commits an offence
if the building is occupied but not registered.

77.2

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to
prove that the person had a reasonable excuse for the building being occupied
but not registered.

77.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

77.3.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

77.3.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

and (in either case) is liable on summary conviction to a further fine not
exceeding level 1 on the standard scale for each day on which the default
continues after the initial conviction.

77.4

In this section “ registered ” means registered under section 78.

##### Registration of higher-risk buildings

78

78.1

On an application by the principal accountable person for a higher-risk
building the regulator may register the building.

78.2

The regulator must publish the register in such way as it considers
appropriate.

78.3

The regulator may remove a building from the register if it appears to the
regulator that—

78.3.a

the building is not occupied, or

78.3.b

the building is not a higher-risk building.

78.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the register,
including in particular provision about—

78.4.a

the information to be contained in the register;

78.4.b

the updating or other revision of information in the register;

78.4.c

the procedure for removing buildings from the register.

78.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision in relation to
applications under this section, including in particular provision about—

78.5.a

the form and content of an application;

78.5.b

the information and documents that must accompany an application;

78.5.c

the way in which an application, and anything that is to accompany it, is to
be given;

78.5.d

the circumstances in which an application may be withdrawn or treated as
withdrawn;

78.5.e

the way in which an application may be withdrawn.

##### Occupied building: duty to apply for building assessment certificate

79

79.1

This section applies where the regulator directs the principal accountable
person for an occupied higher-risk building to apply to the regulator for a
building assessment certificate in relation to the building.

79.2

The principal accountable person for the building must make the application
within the period of 28 days beginning with the day on which the direction is
given.

79.3

A person who, without reasonable excuse, contravenes  subsection (2)  commits
an offence.

79.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

79.4.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

79.4.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

and (in either case) is liable on summary conviction to a further fine not
exceeding level 1 on the standard scale for each day on which the default
continues after the initial conviction.

79.5

In this section “ building assessment certificate ” means a certificate issued
under section 81.

##### Applications for building assessment certificates

80

80.1

An application under section 79 must be accompanied by—

80.1.a

a copy of the most recent safety case report for the building unless a copy of
that report has been provided under section 86 (2) ;

80.1.b

prescribed information about the mandatory occurrence reporting system
operated by the principal accountable person;

80.1.c

prescribed information demonstrating compliance by each accountable person for
the building with their duties under section 89;

80.1.d

a copy of any residents’ engagement strategy.

80.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about
applications under section 79, including in particular provision about—

80.2.a

the form and content of an application;

80.2.b

the way in which an application, and anything which is to accompany it, is to
be given;

80.2.c

the circumstances in which an application may be withdrawn or treated as
withdrawn;

80.2.d

the way in which an application may be withdrawn.

80.3

In this section—

                                    “ mandatory occurrence reporting system ”
has the same meaning as in section 87;
“ residents’ engagement strategy ” has the same meaning as in section 91;
“ safety case report ”  has the same meaning as in section 85.

##### Building assessment certificates

81

81.1

This section applies where—

81.1.a

the principal accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building applies
under section 79 for a certificate in relation to the building (a “building
assessment certificate”),

81.1.b

the application is made pursuant to a direction of the regulator under that
section, and

81.1.c

the building is registered under section 78.

81.2

The regulator must assess whether the relevant duties are being complied with
(and may inspect the building in connection with that assessment).

81.3

The regulator—

81.3.a

must give a building assessment certificate if satisfied that all relevant
duties are being complied with;

81.3.b

if not so satisfied, must (subject to  subsection (4) ) refuse the application
and notify the principal accountable person of the refusal.

81.4

If the regulator considers that a contravention of a relevant duty can be
remedied promptly—

81.4.a

the regulator may give a notice under  this subsection  to the principal
accountable person containing a brief description of the contravention and
specifying a period for remedying the contravention, and

81.4.b

if it does so, and the contravention is remedied within that period, it may
give a building assessment certificate (instead of refusing the application).

81.5

In this section “ relevant duty ” means a duty of an accountable person for
the building under, or under prescribed regulations made under, any of the
following—

81.5.a

section 83 (duty to assess building safety risks);

81.5.b

section 84 (management of building safety risks);

81.5.c

section 85 (duties relating to safety case report);

81.5.d

section 87 (5)  (duties relating to mandatory occurrence reporting system);

81.5.e

section 89 (provision of information to regulator, residents etc);

81.5.f

section 91 (duty to produce a residents’ engagement strategy).

81.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about
building assessment certificates and notices under this section, including in
particular provision about—

81.6.a

the period in relation to which a certificate may be given;

81.6.b

the form and content of a certificate or notice;

81.6.c

the way in which a certificate or notice is to be given.

##### Duty to display building assessment certificate etc

82

82.1

The principal accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building must
ensure that the following are displayed together, in a conspicuous position in
the building—

82.1.a

a notice in the prescribed form containing prescribed information about
accountable persons for the building;

82.1.b

the most recent building assessment certificate relating to the building;

82.1.c

any relevant compliance notice (see  subsection (5) ).

82.2

Where a special measures order is in force in relation to an occupied higher-
risk building—

82.2.a

subsection (1)  has effect as if  paragraph (b)  were omitted, and

82.2.b

the principal accountable person for the building must ensure that no building
assessment certificate relating to the building is displayed in the building.

82.3

A person who, without reasonable excuse, contravenes  subsection (1)  or  (2)
(b)  commits an offence.

82.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

82.4.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

82.4.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

and (in either case) is liable on summary conviction to a further fine not
exceeding level 1 on the standard scale for each day on which the default
continues after the initial conviction.

82.5

In this section—

                                    “ building assessment certificate ” has
the same meaning as in section 81;
“ relevant compliance notice ”: a compliance notice is “relevant” if—
it has been given to an accountable person for the building,
if it was not given to the principal accountable person for the building, the
regulator has given a copy of it to the principal accountable person, and
the regulator has not notified the principal accountable person that the
notice has been withdrawn.

#### Duties relating to building safety risks

##### Assessment of building safety risks

83

83.1

An accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building must as soon as
reasonably practicable after the relevant time assess the building safety
risks as regards the part of the building for which they are responsible.

83.2

Further such assessments must be made—

83.2.a

at regular intervals,

83.2.b

at any time that the accountable person has reason to suspect that the current
assessment is no longer valid, and

83.2.c

at the direction of the regulator, within a period specified in the direction.

83.3

An assessment under  subsection (1)  or  (2)  must be suitable and sufficient
for the purposes of enabling the accountable person to comply with their
duties under section 84.

83.4

In this section “ the relevant time ” means—

83.4.a

the time when the building becomes occupied, or

83.4.b

if later, the time when the person becomes an accountable person for the
building.

##### Management of building safety risks

84

84.1

An accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building must take all
reasonable steps for the following purposes—

84.1.a

preventing a building safety risk materialising as regards the part of the
building for which they are responsible;

84.1.b

reducing the severity of any incident resulting from such a risk
materialising.

84.2

Those steps may in particular involve the accountable person carrying out
works to the part of the building for which they are responsible.

84.3

When taking the steps the accountable person must act in accordance with
prescribed principles.

84.4

The steps must be taken promptly.

84.5

The accountable person must make and give effect to arrangements for the
purpose of ensuring the effective planning, organisation, control, monitoring
and review of steps taken under this section.

##### Safety case report

85

85.1

The principal accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building must as
soon as reasonably practicable after the relevant time prepare a report (a
“safety case report”) containing—

85.1.a

any assessment of the building safety risks made under section 83 by an
accountable person for the building, and

85.1.b

a brief description of any steps taken under section 84 by an accountable
person for the building.

85.2

The principal accountable person must revise a safety case report if they
consider it necessary or appropriate to do so following—

85.2.a

any further assessment under section 83 made by an accountable person for the
building, or

85.2.b

the taking of further steps under section 84 by an accountable person for the
building.

85.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about the
content and form of safety case reports.

85.4

In this section “ the relevant time ” means—

85.4.a

the time when the building becomes occupied, or

85.4.b

if later, the time when the person becomes the principal accountable person
for the building.

##### Notification and provision of report to the regulator

86

86.1

The principal accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building must
notify the regulator as soon as reasonably practicable after preparing or
revising a safety case report.

86.2

Where the regulator asks the principal accountable person to provide it with a
copy of the safety case report, the principal accountable person must give a
copy of it to the regulator as soon as reasonably practicable.

86.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about—

86.3.a

the content and form of notifications under this section;

86.3.b

the way in which a notification or copy of a report must be given.

86.4

In this section “ safety case report ” has the same meaning as in section 85.

#### Duties relating to information and documents

##### Mandatory reporting requirements

87

87.1

An accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building must, in prescribed
circumstances, give prescribed information to the regulator by the prescribed
time and in the specified way.

87.2

The information that may be prescribed is information that relates to a
building safety risk as regards the part of the building for which an
accountable person is responsible.

87.3

In  subsection (1)  “ specified ” means specified in a direction given and
published by the regulator.

87.4

A person who, without reasonable excuse, contravenes  subsection (1)  commits
an offence and is liable on summary conviction to a fine.

87.5

The principal accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building must
establish and operate an effective mandatory occurrence reporting system which
complies with prescribed requirements.

87.6

A “mandatory occurrence reporting system” is a system for the giving of
information to accountable persons for the building for the purpose of
enabling them to comply with  subsection (1) .

87.7

Information provided by a person under  subsection (1)  is not admissible in
evidence against that person in criminal proceedings except—

87.7.a

in proceedings for an offence under section 24 or this section,

87.7.b

in proceedings for an offence of perverting the course of justice, or

87.7.c

if in the proceedings—

87.7.c.i

in giving evidence the person makes a statement inconsistent with the
information, and

87.7.c.ii

evidence as to the information that was provided is adduced, or a question
relating to it is asked, by or on behalf of the person.

##### Keeping information about higher-risk buildings

88

88.1

An accountable person for a higher-risk building must—

88.1.a

keep prescribed information in accordance with prescribed standards, and

88.1.b

so far as possible keep such information up to date.

88.2

An accountable person for a higher-risk building must keep copies of
prescribed documents in accordance with prescribed standards.

88.3

Where an accountable person does not hold prescribed information or a copy of
a prescribed document, they must obtain it except where it is not practicable
to do so.

88.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision as to when the duties
in  subsections (1)  to  (3)  apply.

##### Provision of information etc to the regulator, residents and other persons

89

89.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision requiring an
accountable person for a higher-risk building to give prescribed information
or a copy of a prescribed document to—

89.1.a

the regulator,

89.1.b

another accountable person for the building,

89.1.c

residents of the building,

89.1.d

owners of residential units in the building, or

89.1.e

any other prescribed person.

89.2

The regulations may in particular make provision about—

89.2.a

when information or a copy of a document must be given;

89.2.b

the way in which information or copy of a document must be given;

89.2.c

the form in which information must be given (and may in particular require
that the information is given in an accessible form);

89.2.d

the standards in accordance with which information or a copy of a document
must be given.

89.3

The regulations may make exceptions to any duty imposed under the regulations.

89.4

Subject to  subsection (5) , the regulations may provide that the disclosure
of information under this section does not breach—

89.4.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the accountable person in relation to
that information;

89.4.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

89.5

This section does not authorise a disclosure of information if the disclosure
would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, take into account the powers conferred by this
section).

89.6

Where the regulations provide that any information or document must be given
to the regulator, they may make provision about the admissibility in any
criminal proceedings of the information or document.

##### Provision of information etc on change in accountable person

90

90.1

This section applies where at any time (“ the relevant time ”) an accountable
person for a higher-risk building (the “outgoing person”) ceases to be
responsible for all or any part of the building.

90.2

The outgoing person must give prescribed information and a copy of any
prescribed document to any person who, immediately after the relevant time—

90.2.a

is an accountable person for the building, and

90.2.b

is responsible for a part of the building for which the outgoing person ceased
to be responsible at the relevant time.

90.3

The information and documents must be given—

90.3.a

by the prescribed time,

90.3.b

in the prescribed way, and

90.3.c

in accordance with prescribed standards.

90.4

The outgoing person must give prescribed information to the regulator in the
prescribed way, as soon as reasonably practicable after the relevant time.

90.5

Subject to  subsection (6) , regulations made by the Secretary of State under
this section may provide that the disclosure of information under this section
does not breach—

90.5.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the outgoing person in relation to that
information;

90.5.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

90.6

This section does not authorise a disclosure of information if the disclosure
would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, take into account the powers conferred by this
section).

90.7

A person who, without reasonable excuse, contravenes  subsection (2)  or  (4)
commits an offence and is liable—

90.7.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

90.7.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

and (in either case) is liable on summary conviction to a further fine not
exceeding level 1 on the standard scale for each day on which the default
continues after the initial conviction.

#### Engagement with residents etc

##### Residents’ engagement strategy

91

91.1

The principal accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building must—

91.1.a

as soon as reasonably practicable after the relevant time prepare a strategy
(a “residents’ engagement strategy”) for promoting the participation of
relevant persons in the making of building safety decisions;

91.1.b

review the strategy at prescribed times, and revise it if they consider it
necessary or appropriate to do so;

91.1.c

in prescribed circumstances, consult relevant persons and prescribed persons
on the strategy and take any representations made on the consultation into
account when next reviewing the strategy;

91.1.d

act in accordance with the strategy.

91.2

“ Building safety decision ” means a decision by an accountable person for the
building that—

91.2.a

is about the management of the building, and

91.2.b

is made in connection with the performance of a duty of the accountable person
under, or under regulations made under,  this Part .

91.3

The strategy must include information about—

91.3.a

the information that will be provided to relevant persons about decisions
relating to the management of the building,

91.3.b

the aspects of those decisions that relevant persons will be consulted about,

91.3.c

the arrangements for obtaining and taking account of the views of relevant
persons, and

91.3.d

how the appropriateness of methods for promoting participation will be
measured and kept under review.

91.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after the strategy is prepared or revised,
each accountable person for the building must give a copy of the strategy to—

91.4.a

each resident of the building who—

91.4.a.i

is aged 16 or over, and

91.4.a.ii

resides in a residential unit in the part of the building for which the
accountable person is responsible;

91.4.b

each owner of a residential unit in that part of the building;

91.4.c

any prescribed person.

91.5

The duty under  subsection (4) (a)  does not apply in relation to a resident
if the accountable person—

91.5.a

is not aware of the resident, and

91.5.b

has taken all reasonable steps to make themselves aware of persons who reside
in residential units in the part of the building for which the accountable
person is responsible.

91.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

91.6.a

make further provision about the content of a residents’ engagement strategy;

91.6.b

make provision about the preparation, review or revision of a residents’
engagement strategy, in cases where there is more than one accountable person
for the building;

91.6.c

make provision about the way in which a copy of the strategy is to be given;

91.6.d

make provision about consultations under this section.

91.7

In this section—

                                    “ relevant persons ” are—
residents of the higher-risk building who are aged 16 or over, and
owners of residential units in the building;
“ the relevant time ” has the meaning given by section 85.

##### Requests for further information

92

92.1

This section applies where—

92.1.a

a resident of an occupied higher-risk building who is aged 16 or over, or

92.1.b

an owner of a residential unit in the building,

makes a request to an accountable person for the building to give them
prescribed information or a copy of a prescribed document.

92.2

The accountable person must as soon as reasonably practicable give the
resident or owner the information or document requested.

92.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about— 

92.3.a

the way in which information or a copy of a document must be given under this
section;

92.3.b

the form in which information must be given under this section (and may in
particular require that the information is given in an accessible form).

92.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that in prescribed
circumstances an accountable person is not required by  subsection (2)  to
provide a copy of a document or some or all of the information requested.

92.5

Subject to  subsection (6) , the regulations may provide that the disclosure
of information under this section does not breach—

92.5.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

92.5.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

92.6

This section does not authorise a disclosure of information if the disclosure
would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, take into account the powers conferred by this
section).

##### Complaints procedure operated by principal accountable person

93

93.1

The principal accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building must as
soon as reasonably practicable after the relevant time establish and operate a
system for the investigation of relevant complaints.

93.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the
establishment and operation of complaints systems under this section.

93.3

The regulations may in particular make provision—

93.3.a

about the way in which complaints may be made;

93.3.b

about the period within which a complaint must be considered and dealt with;

93.3.c

requiring the principal accountable person to refer a complaint to the
regulator.

93.4

In this section—

                                    “ relevant complaint ” means a complaint
relating to—
a building safety risk as regards the building, or
the performance by an accountable person for the building of any duty under,
or under regulations made under,  this Part ;
“ the relevant time ” has the meaning given by section 85.

##### Complaints procedure operated by the regulator

94

94.1

The regulator must establish and operate a system for the investigation of
relevant complaints that are made, or referred under section 93, to the
regulator.

94.2

The regulator must consult the committee mentioned in section 11 (residents’
panel)—

94.2.a

before the complaints system is established or, if the committee has not been
established at the time the complaints system is established, as soon as
reasonably practicable after the committee is established, and

94.2.b

before making any significant change to the complaints system.

94.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the
establishment and operation of the complaints system under this section.

94.4

The regulations may in particular make provision about—

94.4.a

the period within which a complaint must be considered and dealt with;

94.4.b

action that the regulator must consider taking in response to a complaint.

94.5

In this section “ relevant complaint ” means a complaint relating to—

94.5.a

a building safety risk as regards an occupied higher-risk building,

94.5.b

the performance by an accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building
of any duty under, or under regulations made under,  this Part , or

94.5.c

the performance by a special measures manager of any function conferred on the
manager by a special measures order.

#### Residents' etc duties

##### Duties on residents and owners

95

95.1

This section applies to—

95.1.a

a resident of a residential unit in an occupied higher-risk building who is
aged 16 or over;

95.1.b

an owner of a residential unit in such a building.

95.2

A person to whom this section applies—

95.2.a

must not act in a way that creates a significant risk of a building safety
risk materialising;

95.2.b

must not interfere with a relevant safety item;

95.2.c

must comply with a request, made by the appropriate accountable person, for
information reasonably required for the purposes of a duty under section 83 or
84.

95.3

For the purposes of  subsection (2) (b)  a person “interferes” with a relevant
safety item if they, without reasonable excuse—

95.3.a

damage it,

95.3.b

remove it, or

95.3.c

do anything to, or in relation to, it that interferes with its intended
function.

95.4

In this section—

                                    “ appropriate accountable person ” means
the accountable person for the building who is responsible for the part of the
building comprising the residential unit;
“ relevant safety item ” means—
anything that—
is in, or forms part of, the common parts (as defined by section 72), and
is intended to improve the safety of people in or about the building in
relation to a building safety risk, or
any other prescribed thing.

##### Contravention notices

96

96.1

This section applies where it appears to the appropriate accountable person
that a relevant person has contravened or is contravening a duty under section
95 (2) .

96.2

The appropriate accountable person may give a contravention notice to the
relevant person.

96.3

A “contravention notice” is a notice that—

96.3.a

specifies the alleged contravention;

96.3.b

specifies any steps that the appropriate accountable person considers the
relevant person should take in order to remedy the contravention, and a
reasonable time for the taking of those steps;

96.3.c

specifies anything that the appropriate accountable person considers the
relevant person should refrain from doing, to avoid further contraventions of
the duty;

96.3.d

contains an explanation of the steps that the appropriate accountable person
may take under this section if the notice is not complied with.

96.4

Where it appears to the appropriate accountable person that the relevant
person has contravened or is contravening the duty under section 95 (2) (b) ,
the contravention notice may require the relevant person to pay to the
appropriate accountable person a sum specified in the notice.

96.5

A sum may be specified in a contravention notice under  subsection (4)  only
if—

96.5.a

it is necessary to repair or replace the relevant safety item as a result of
the contravention, and

96.5.b

the sum specified does not exceed the reasonable cost of repairing or
replacing (as the case may be) that item.

96.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about contravention
notices, including—

96.6.a

provision about the form of a notice and the way a notice is to be given, and

96.6.b

further provision about the content of a notice.

96.7

The county court may, on an application made by the appropriate accountable
person, make an order under this section if satisfied that—

96.7.a

a contravention notice has been given,

96.7.b

the contravention alleged in the notice occurred, and

96.7.c

it is necessary to make the order.

96.8

An order under this section may—

96.8.a

require a relevant person to provide specified information or do a specified
thing, by a specified time;

96.8.b

prohibit a relevant person from doing a specified thing;

96.8.c

where a contravention notice requires a sum to be paid under  subsection (4) ,
require a relevant person to pay to the appropriate accountable person a
specified sum.

“Specified” here means specified in the order.

96.9

A sum specified in an order under  subsection (8) (c)  may not exceed the sum
specified in the contravention notice.

96.10

In this section—

                                    “ appropriate accountable person ” has the
same meaning as in section 95;
“ relevant person ” means a person who is subject to the duties under section
95 (see  subsection (1)  of that section).

##### Access to premises

97

97.1

This section applies where —

97.1.a

an accountable person for an occupied higher-risk building makes a request to
a relevant person to enter relevant premises,

97.1.b

the request is made for the purpose of—

97.1.b.i

facilitating the performance of a duty under section 83 or 84 (assessment of
building safety risk etc), or

97.1.b.ii

determining whether a duty under section 95 (duties on residents and owners)
has been contravened,

97.1.c

the request is within  subsection (2) , and

97.1.d

entry to the premises is not given.

97.2

A request is within  this subsection  if it—

97.2.a

is in writing,

97.2.b

sets out the purpose for which it is made,

97.2.c

contains an explanation of why it is necessary to enter the premises for that
purpose,

97.2.d

requests access to the premises at a reasonable time, and

97.2.e

is made at least 48 hours before the time mentioned in  paragraph (d) .

97.3

The accountable person may apply to the county court for an order—

97.3.a

requiring the relevant person to allow the accountable person, or a person
authorised by the accountable person, to enter the relevant premises at a
reasonable time for the purpose mentioned in the request, and

97.3.b

if necessary for that purpose, authorising the taking of measurements,
photographs, recordings or samples by the accountable person or authorised
person.

97.4

The county court—

97.4.a

may make an order under  subsection (3) (a)  or  (b)  if satisfied that it is
necessary to do so for the purpose mentioned in the request;

97.4.b

must, if it does so, specify a date on which, or in a period within which, the
accountable person or authorised person may enter the relevant premises for
that purpose.

97.5

In this section—

                                    “ relevant person ” in relation to
relevant premises means—
a resident of those premises who is aged 16 or over;
where those premises are controlled but not occupied, a person controlling
those premises;
in any other case, an owner of those premises;
“ relevant premises ” means any premises in the part of the building for which
the accountable person is responsible that are occupied or controlled by—
a resident of a residential unit in the building, or
an owner of a residential unit in the building.

#### Enforcement

##### Duty on regulator to enforce Part

98

The regulator must enforce the provisions of  this Part  and regulations made
under it.

##### Compliance notices

99

99.1

The regulator may give a compliance notice to an accountable person for a
higher-risk building who appears to the regulator to have contravened, be
contravening or be likely to contravene a relevant requirement.

99.2

A “compliance notice” is—

99.2.a

a notice requiring the accountable person to take specified steps within a
specified period, or

99.2.b

a notice requiring the accountable person to remedy the contravention or the
matters giving rise to it within a specified period.

99.3

A notice of a kind mentioned in  subsection (2) (a)  may specify any steps
relating to—

99.3.a

the remedying of the contravention, or

99.3.b

avoiding the contravention occurring.

99.4

Where it appears to the regulator that the contravention has placed or will
place people in or about the building in imminent danger, the regulator may
