specify that the compliance notice is a notice to which  this subsection
applies (an “urgent action notice”).

99.5

A person who, without reasonable excuse, contravenes a compliance notice
commits an offence.

99.6

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

99.6.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

99.6.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

and (in either case) is liable on summary conviction to a further fine not
exceeding level 1 on the standard scale for each day on which the default
continues after the initial conviction.

99.7

In this section—

                                    “ relevant requirement ” means any
requirement on an accountable person under, or under regulations made under,
this Part  except one that is prescribed for the purposes of this section;
“ specified ” means specified in the notice.

##### Compliance notices: supplementary

100

100.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about
compliance notices.

100.2

The regulations may in particular make provision about—

100.2.a

the form and content of notices;

100.2.b

the giving of notices;

100.2.c

the amendment or withdrawal of notices;

100.2.d

the extension of any period specified in a compliance notice for the doing of
a thing.

100.3

Subsection (4)  applies where the regulator has given a compliance notice to
an accountable person for a higher-risk building. 

100.4

The regulator must take reasonable steps to notify—

100.4.a

the local authority for the area in which the building is situated;

100.4.b

the fire and rescue authority for the area in which the building is situated;

100.4.c

where the accountable person for the building is a registered provider of
social housing, the Regulator of Social Housing;

100.4.d

any other prescribed person.

##### Offence: contravention giving rise to risk of death and serious injury

101

101.1

An accountable person for a higher-risk building commits an offence if—

101.1.a

without reasonable excuse, the accountable person contravenes a relevant
requirement, and

101.1.b

the contravention places one or more people in or about the building at
critical risk.

101.2

In  subsection (1) —

                                    “ critical risk ” means a significant risk
of death or serious injury arising from a building safety risk;
“ relevant requirement ” means any requirement on an accountable person under,
or under regulations made under,  this Part  except one that is prescribed for
the purposes of this section.

101.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

101.3.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

101.3.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

and (in either case) is liable on summary conviction to a further fine not
exceeding level 1 on the standard scale for each day on which the default
continues after the initial conviction.

#### Special measures

##### Special measures

102

Schedule 7  provides for the appointment of a special measures manager, to
undertake duties under  this Part  in place of an accountable person, and
makes further provision in connection with that appointment.

#### Appeals etc

##### Appeals against compliance notice etc

103

103.1

A person to whom a compliance notice has been given may appeal to the
tribunal.

103.2

An appeal may be on the grounds—

103.2.a

that the person has not contravened, is not contravening, or is not likely to
contravene, a relevant requirement;

103.2.b

that it is unreasonable to require the person to do any thing specified to be
done in the notice.

103.3

Where an appeal under  subsection (1)  is made and the compliance notice is
not an urgent action notice—

103.3.a

the compliance notice is of no effect pending the final determination or
withdrawal of the appeal, and

103.3.b

the specified period mentioned in section 99 (2) (a)  is treated as extended
by the period—

103.3.b.i

beginning with the day on which the appeal is made, and

103.3.b.ii

ending with the day on which the appeal is finally determined or withdrawn.

103.4

Where an appeal under  subsection (1)  is made and the compliance notice is an
urgent action notice—

103.4.a

the appellant may apply to the tribunal for a direction that the compliance
notice is of no effect pending the final determination or withdrawal of the
appeal, and

103.4.b

unless and until any such direction is given, the compliance notice continues
to have effect despite the making of the appeal.

103.5

A person to whom a compliance notice has been given may apply to the tribunal
for an extension of the period for the doing of any thing specified to be done
in the notice.

103.6

Subsections (3)  and  (4)  apply to such an application as they apply to an
appeal under  subsection (1) .

103.7

In this section “ urgent action notice ” has the meaning given by section 99
(4) .

##### Appeals against decisions of the regulator made under 

104

104.1

This section applies in relation to a decision of the regulator—

104.1.a

not to register a building on an application under section 78 (1) ;

104.1.b

to remove a building from the register under section 78 (3) ;

104.1.c

to refuse an application for a building assessment certificate under section
81 (3) ;

104.1.d

to give a direction under section 83 (2) .

104.2

An affected person may appeal the decision.

104.3

An appeal may be on the grounds—

104.3.a

that the decision was based on an error of fact;

104.3.b

that the decision was wrong in law;

104.3.c

that the decision was unreasonable.

104.4

In this section “ an affected person ” means—

104.4.a

in relation to a decision of the regulator mentioned in  paragraph (a)  or
(b)  of  subsection (1) , an accountable person for the higher-risk building
(or a person who would be an accountable person for the building if the
building were a higher-risk building);

104.4.b

in relation to a decision of the regulator mentioned in  paragraph (c)  of
subsection (1) , an accountable person for the higher-risk building;

104.4.c

in relation to a decision of the regulator mentioned in  paragraph (d)  of
subsection (1) , the accountable person subject to the direction.

##### Appeals against decisions of the regulator made under regulations

105

105.1

This section applies in relation to a prescribed decision of the regulator
made under regulations made under  this Part .

105.2

A prescribed person may appeal to the tribunal against the decision.

105.3

An appeal may be made only on prescribed grounds.

##### Appeals: supplementary

106

106.1

This section applies in relation to an appeal to the tribunal under section
103 (1) , 104 or 105.

106.2

The tribunal—

106.2.a

must consider afresh the decision appealed against, and

106.2.b

may take into account evidence that was not available to the regulator.

106.3

The tribunal may confirm, vary or quash the decision of the regulator.

106.4

The Secretary of State may, by regulations—

106.4.a

provide for the suspension during the appeal period of the effect of a notice
(other than a compliance notice) given or other thing done by the regulator;

106.4.b

make other provision about the effect during the appeal period of an appeal
(including provision conferring powers on the tribunal).

106.5

In  subsection (4)  “ the appeal period ” means the period beginning with the
making of the appeal and ending with the final determination or withdrawal of
the appeal.

##### Enforcement of decisions of the First-tier and Upper Tribunal

107

107.1

A decision of the First-tier Tribunal or Upper Tribunal made under or in
connection with  this Part  is enforceable with the permission of the county
court in the same way as an order of that court.

107.2

Subsection (1)  does not apply to a decision of the First-tier Tribunal or
Upper Tribunal ordering the payment of a sum (as to which see section 28 of
the Tribunals, Courts and Enforcement Act 2007 (enforcement)).

#### Miscellaneous and general

##### Guidance

108

108.1

The regulator may issue guidance about any of the following matters—

108.1.a

the performance of any duties under section 87 (mandatory reporting
requirements);

108.1.b

the performance of any duties under section 88 or 89 (duty to keep or give
information);

108.1.c

the performance of any duties under section 92 (duty to give further
information to residents);

108.1.d

the performance of any duties under section 93 (complaints procedure).

108.2

The regulator may revise or withdraw any issued guidance.

108.3

Where in any proceedings it is alleged that a person has contravened a
provision mentioned in  subsection (1) —

108.3.a

proof of a failure to comply with any applicable guidance may be relied on as
tending to establish that there was such a contravention, and

108.3.b

proof of compliance with any applicable guidance may be relied on as tending
to establish that there was no such contravention.

108.4

In any proceedings, a document purporting to be guidance under this section is
to be taken to be such guidance unless the contrary is proved.

108.5

Guidance under this section may be issued, revised or withdrawn only with the
consent of the Secretary of State.

108.6

In this section any reference to a provision includes regulations made under
the provision.

##### Cooperation and coordination

109

109.1

Subsection (2)  applies if there is more than one accountable person for an
occupied higher-risk building.

109.2

When carrying out their duties under, or under regulations made under,  this
Part , each accountable person must so far as possible—

109.2.a

cooperate with every other accountable person for the building, and

109.2.b

coordinate with every other accountable person for the building.

109.3

Subsection (4)  applies to an accountable person for an occupied higher-risk
building if there are one or more other persons who are responsible persons
within the meaning of article 3 of the Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order
2005 in relation to the building.

109.4

The accountable person must cooperate with each responsible person for the
purpose of each responsible person carrying out their duties under the Order.

##### Managers appointed under Part 2 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1987

110

110.1

Section 24 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1987 (appointment of a manager by a
tribunal) is amended as follows.

110.2

After subsection (2ZA) insert—

110.2.2ZB

Subsection (2)(a) does not apply in respect of a breach of a building safety
obligation by an accountable person for a higher-risk building.

110.2.2ZC

In this section—

                                                               “ accountable
person ” has the meaning given in section 72 of the Building Safety Act 2022;
“ building safety obligation ” means an obligation of an accountable person
under  Part 4  of the Building Safety Act 2022 or regulations made under that
Part;
“ higher-risk building ” has the meaning given in section 65 of the Building
Safety Act 2022.

110.3

After subsection (2D) (inserted by paragraph  8 (3)  of Schedule  7 ) insert—

110.3.2E

An order under this section may not provide for a manager to carry out a
function in relation to a higher-risk building where  Part 4  of the Building
Safety Act 2022 or regulations made under that Part provide for that function
to be carried out by an accountable person for that building.

##### Building safety directors of resident management companies

111

111.1

This section applies in relation to a resident management company that is an
accountable person for a higher-risk building.

111.2

The articles of association of the resident management company have effect as
if they included such provision as may be prescribed relating to—

111.2.a

eligibility for appointment as a director of the company, for a building
safety purpose;

111.2.b

the appointment of a director for such a purpose;

111.2.c

the entitlement to remuneration of a director appointed for such a purpose;

111.2.d

the removal of a director so appointed.

111.3

Subsection (2) has effect—

111.3.a

whether or not the provision is adopted by the company;

111.3.b

whether the company was formed before or after the coming into force of this
section;

111.3.c

notwithstanding anything in the company’s articles of association.

111.4

In this section—

                                    “ building safety purpose ” means the
purpose of supporting the resident management company in complying with its
duties under this Part or under regulations made under this Part;
“ resident management company ” has the meaning given by regulations made by
the Secretary of State.

#### Landlord and tenant etc

##### Implied terms in leases and recovery of safety related costs

112

112.1

The Landlord and Tenant Act 1985 is amended in accordance with subsections
(2)  to  (6) .

112.2

After section 30B insert—

########### Higher-risk buildings in England

############ Implied terms relating to building safety

112.2.30C

112.2.30C.1

This section applies to a lease of premises which consist of or include a
dwelling in a higher-risk building.

112.2.30C.2

In the lease there is implied a covenant by the landlord—

112.2.30C.2.a

where the landlord is an accountable person for the higher-risk building, to
comply with their building safety duties;

112.2.30C.2.b

to cooperate with any person in connection with a relevant person complying
with their building safety duties;

112.2.30C.2.c

where a special measures order in relation to the higher-risk building is in
force, to comply with that order so far as it relates to the landlord.

112.2.30C.3

In the lease there is implied a covenant by the tenant—

112.2.30C.3.a

to allow the landlord, a relevant person or a person authorised in writing by
the landlord or a relevant person to enter the premises for a relevant
building safety purpose;

112.2.30C.3.b

where the tenant is a resident of the higher-risk building, to comply with
their duties under sections 95 and 97 of the Building Safety Act 2022;

112.2.30C.3.c

where a special measures order in relation to the higher-risk building is in
force, to comply with that order so far as it relates to the tenant.

112.2.30C.4

In the covenant implied by subsection  (2) (b) , “ cooperate ”, in relation to
a person, includes—

112.2.30C.4.a

taking any steps which are reasonably required by the person to facilitate
compliance by a relevant person with their building safety duties;

112.2.30C.4.b

where the person is a relevant person (or a person authorised in writing by a
relevant person), providing any information (including names and contact
details of residents and tenants of the premises) to the person which is
reasonably required in connection with the relevant person complying with
their building safety duties.

112.2.30C.5

In the covenant implied by subsection  (3) (a) , a relevant building safety
purpose means—

112.2.30C.5.a

inspecting the premises in connection with a relevant person complying with
their building safety duties;

112.2.30C.5.b

carrying out works to the premises, where such works are required to be
carried out in connection with a relevant person complying with their building
safety duties;

112.2.30C.5.c

accessing a part of the higher-risk building that is not let to the tenant in
order to—

112.2.30C.5.c.i

inspect that part of the building in connection with a relevant person
complying with their building safety duties;

112.2.30C.5.c.ii

carry out works to that part of the building, where such works are required to
be carried out in connection with a relevant person complying with their
building safety duties.

112.2.30C.6

The covenant implied by subsection  (3) (a)  requires entry to the premises to
be allowed—

112.2.30C.6.a

only at reasonable times, and

112.2.30C.6.b

only if the tenant has been given at least 48 hours’ notice in writing.

112.2.30C.7

Except as provided by subsection  (8) , the disclosure of information in
accordance with subsections  (2) (b)  and  (4) (b)  does not breach—

112.2.30C.7.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the landlord in relation to that
information;

112.2.30C.7.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

112.2.30C.8

Subsections  (2) (b)  and  (4) (b)  do not require a disclosure of information
if the disclosure would contravene the data protection legislation (but in
determining whether a disclosure would do so, take into account the duty
imposed by subsections  (2) (b)  and  (4) (b) ).

112.2.30C.9

In this section—

                     “ building safety duties ”—
in relation to an accountable person, means any duties of the accountable
person under  Part 4  of the Building Safety Act 2022, or regulations made
under that Part of that Act;
in relation to a special measures manager, means any duties of the manager
included in the special measures order appointing the manager;
“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act);
“ relevant person ” means—
an accountable person for the higher-risk building;
a special measures manager for the higher-risk building;
“ resident ” and “resident of a higher-risk building” have the same meaning as
in  Part 4  of the Building Safety Act 2022 (see section 71 (3)  and  (4) (c)
of that Act);
“ works ” includes alterations, improvements and installations.

############ Liability for building safety costs

112.2.30D

112.2.30D.1

This section applies to a relevant lease of premises which consist of or
include a dwelling in a higher-risk building.

112.2.30D.2

In this section “relevant lease”—

112.2.30D.2.a

means a lease—

112.2.30D.2.a.i

that is granted for a term certain of 7 years or more, whether or not it is
(or may become) terminable before the end of that term by notice given by the
tenant or by re-entry or forfeiture, and

112.2.30D.2.a.ii

under which the tenant is liable to pay a service charge (within the meaning
of section 18), but

112.2.30D.2.b

does not include a relevant social housing tenancy.

112.2.30D.3

The relevant lease has effect—

112.2.30D.3.a

as if the matters for which the service charge is payable under the lease
included the taking of building safety measures by or on behalf of a relevant
person (insofar as this would not otherwise be the case), and

112.2.30D.3.b

where the lease contains different methods for apportioning different relevant
costs (within the meaning of section 18), as if it provided for any costs for
which the tenant is liable by virtue only of paragraph (a) to be apportioned
in the same way as costs incurred in connection with insuring the building.

112.2.30D.4

“ Building safety measure ” means any of the following—

112.2.30D.4.a

applying for registration of a higher-risk building in accordance with section
78 of the Building Safety Act 2022;

112.2.30D.4.b

applying for a building assessment certificate in accordance with section 79
of that Act;

112.2.30D.4.c

displaying a building assessment certificate in accordance with section 82 of
that Act;

112.2.30D.4.d

assessing building safety risks in accordance with section 83 of that Act;

112.2.30D.4.e

taking reasonable steps in accordance with section 84 of that Act (management
of building safety risks), other than steps involving the carrying out of
works as referred to in section 84 (2) ;

112.2.30D.4.f

preparing and revising a safety case report in accordance with section 85 of
that Act;

112.2.30D.4.g

notifying the regulator of a safety case report, and giving a copy of a safety
case report to the regulator, in accordance with section 86 of that Act;

112.2.30D.4.h

establishing and operating a mandatory occurrence reporting system, and giving
information to the regulator, in accordance with section 87 of that Act;

112.2.30D.4.i

keeping information and documents in accordance with section 88 of that Act;

112.2.30D.4.j

giving information and documents to any person in accordance with section 89,
90 or 92 of that Act;

112.2.30D.4.k

complying with any duty under section 91 of that Act (residents’ engagement
strategy);

112.2.30D.4.l

establishing and operating a system for the investigation of complaints in
accordance with section 93 of that Act;

112.2.30D.4.m

giving a contravention notice to a resident, and making an application to the
county court, in accordance with section 96 of that Act;

112.2.30D.4.n

making a request to enter premises, or making an application to the county
court, in accordance with section 97 of that Act (access to premises).

112.2.30D.5

For the purposes of this section any of the following incurred in connection
with the taking of a building safety measure are to be regarded as incurred in
taking the measure—

112.2.30D.5.a

legal and other professional fees;

112.2.30D.5.b

fees payable to the regulator;

112.2.30D.5.c

management costs.

112.2.30D.6

In this section—

                     “ landlord ” includes any person who has a right under
the lease to enforce payment of a service charge (within the meaning of
section 18);
“ relevant person ” means—
if the landlord is an accountable person for the building, the landlord or a
special measures manager for the building;
otherwise, any superior landlord who is an accountable person for the building
or a special measures manager for the building;
“ relevant social housing tenancy ” has the meaning given in section 132 of
the Land Registration Act 2002;
“ tenant ” includes any person who has an obligation under the lease to pay a
service charge (within the meaning of section 18).

112.2.30D.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument amend
subsection  (4)  so as to add, remove or modify a building safety measure.

112.2.30D.8

The regulations may make incidental, transitional or saving provision.

112.2.30D.9

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (7)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

############ Liability for remuneration of building safety director of resident management company etc

112.2.30E

112.2.30E.1

This section applies to a lease of premises which consist of or include a
dwelling in a higher-risk building if—

112.2.30E.1.a

the landlord is an accountable person for the building,

112.2.30E.1.b

the landlord is—

112.2.30E.1.b.i

a resident management company within the meaning of section 111 of the
Building Safety Act 2022, or

112.2.30E.1.b.ii

an RTM company within the meaning of Chapter 1 of Part 2 of the Commonhold and
Leasehold Reform Act 2002 (right to manage), and

112.2.30E.1.c

the tenant is liable to pay a service charge.

112.2.30E.2

The lease has effect—

112.2.30E.2.a

as if it contained provision authorising the appointment of a person (whether
or not a leaseholder or a resident of the building) as a director of the
landlord for a building safety purpose,

112.2.30E.2.b

as if the matters for which the service charge is payable under the lease
included remunerating any director of the landlord appointed for a building
safety purpose (insofar as this would not otherwise be the case), and

112.2.30E.2.c

where the lease contains different methods for apportioning different relevant
costs (within the meaning of section 18), as if it provided that any costs for
which the tenant is liable by virtue only of paragraph (b) to be apportioned
in the same way as costs incurred in connection with insuring the building.

112.2.30E.3

In this section—

                     “ building safety purpose ” means the purpose of
supporting the landlord in complying with its duties under Part 4 of the
Building Safety Act 2022 or under regulations made under that Part;
“ landlord ” includes any person who has a right under the lease to enforce
payment of a service charge;
“ service charge ” has the meaning given by section 18;
“ tenant ” includes any person who has an obligation under the lease to pay a
service charge.

############ Restrictions on contracting out of sections 

112.2.30F

112.2.30F.1

A covenant or agreement, whether contained in a lease to which section  30C
(implied terms) applies or in an agreement collateral to such a lease, is void
in so far as it purports—

112.2.30F.1.a

to exclude or limit the obligations of the landlord or the tenant under
section  30C , or

112.2.30F.1.b

to authorise any forfeiture or impose on the tenant any penalty, disability or
obligation in the event of the tenant enforcing or relying upon the
obligations of the landlord.

112.2.30F.2

A covenant or agreement, whether contained in a lease to which section  30D
or  30E  applies or in an agreement collateral to such a lease, is void
insofar as it purports to modify the effect of section  30D (3)  or  30E (2) .

############ Jurisdiction of county court

112.2.30G

The county court has jurisdiction to deal with any claim or other proceedings
arising under or in connection with any of sections  30C  to  30E  (implied
terms etc) notwithstanding that by reason of the amount of the claim or
otherwise the case would not, apart from this section, be within the
jurisdiction of the county court.

############ Specific performance of implied terms

112.2.30H

In proceedings relating to a breach of a covenant in section  30C (2)  or  (3)
(implied building safety terms), the court may order specific performance of
the covenant—

112.2.30H.a

notwithstanding any equitable rule restricting the scope of the remedy,
whether on the basis of a lack of mutuality or otherwise, and

112.2.30H.b

in the case of a breach of a covenant in section  30C (2)  or  (3) (b)  or
(c) , whether or not the breach relates to a part of the higher-risk building
let to the tenant.

############ Interpretation of building safety provisions

112.2.30I

In sections  30C  to  30H —

   “ accountable person ” has the meaning given in section 115 of the Building
Safety Act 2022;
“ higher-risk building ” has the meaning given in section 115 of that Act;
“ lease ” does not include a mortgage term;
“ special measures manager ” has the meaning given in paragraph  1  of
Schedule 7  to the Building Safety Act 2022;
“ special measures order ” has the meaning given in paragraph  1  of  Schedule
7  to that Act.

########### Limitation of service charges: excluded costs for higher-risk buildings

112.3.20F

112.3.20F.1

This section applies in relation to a lease to which section 30D (higher-risk
buildings: building safety costs) applies.

112.3.20F.2

Excluded costs are not to be regarded as relevant costs to be taken into
account in determining the amount of service charge payable by a tenant under
the lease.

112.3.20F.3

In this section “ excluded costs ” means any of the following incurred in
connection with Part 4 of the Building Safety Act 2022 or regulations made
under that Part—

112.3.20F.3.a

costs incurred or to be incurred by or on behalf of a relevant person solely
as a result of any penalty imposed or enforcement action taken by the
regulator;

112.3.20F.3.b

legal costs incurred or to be incurred by or on behalf of a relevant person in
connection with special measures order proceedings;

112.3.20F.3.c

costs incurred or to be incurred by or on behalf of a relevant person by
reason of any negligence, breach of contract or unlawful act on the part of
that relevant person or a person acting on their behalf;

112.3.20F.3.d

costs of a description prescribed by regulations made by the Secretary of
State that are incurred or to be incurred by or on behalf of an accountable
person or special measures manager for the building in connection with the
taking of building safety measures.

with—

made under that Part, or

those regulations;

Act 2022;

building;
where the landlord is not such an accountable person, any superior landlord
who is an accountable person for the higher-risk building or a special
measures manager for the higher-risk building;
“ special measures order proceedings ” means any proceedings relating to the
making, variation or discharge of, or the giving of directions in relation to,
a special measures order under Schedule  7  to the Building Safety Act 2022
(including any appeals in relation to such proceedings).

112.3.20F.5

Regulations under this section are to be made by statutory instrument.

112.3.20F.6

A power to make regulations includes power to make—

112.3.20F.6.a

incidental, transitional or saving provision;

112.3.20F.6.b

different provision for different purposes.

112.3.20F.7

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this section is subject to
annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

##### Provision of building safety information

113

113.1

The Landlord and Tenant Act 1987 is amended in accordance with subsections
(2)  to  (4) .

113.2

After section 47 insert—

########### Building safety information to be contained in demands for rent etc: England

113.2.47A

113.2.47A.1

Where premises to which this Part applies are premises in England which
consist of or include a dwelling in a higher-risk building, any written demand
given to a tenant of the premises must contain the relevant building safety
information.

113.2.47A.2

Where—

113.2.47A.2.a

a tenant of such premises is given such a demand, but

113.2.47A.2.b

the demand does not contain the relevant building safety information,

any part of the amount demanded which consists of a service charge or an
administration charge (“ the relevant amount ”) is to be treated for all
purposes as not being due from the tenant to the landlord at any time before
the landlord gives the relevant building safety information to the tenant.

113.2.47A.3

But the relevant amount is not to be so treated in relation to any time when—

113.2.47A.3.a

by virtue of an order of any court or tribunal there is in force an
appointment of a receiver or manager whose functions include the receiving of
service charges or administration charges from the tenant, or

113.2.47A.3.b

a special measures order (within the meaning of Schedule  7  to the Building
Safety Act 2022) is in force.

113.2.47A.4

In this section—

            “ demand ” has the meaning given in section 47;
“ higher-risk building ” has the meaning given in section 115 of the Building
Safety Act 2022;
“ relevant building safety information ” has the meaning given in section  49A
.

113.3

After section 49 insert—

########### Notification by landlord of building safety information: England

113.3.49A

113.3.49A.1

Where premises to which this Part applies are premises in England which
consist of or include a dwelling in a higher-risk building, the landlord must
give the tenant a notice containing the relevant building safety information.

113.3.49A.2

Where a landlord fails to give a notice to a tenant in accordance with
subsection  (1) , any rent, service charge or administration charge otherwise
due from the tenant to the landlord is to be treated for all purposes as not
being due from the tenant to the landlord at any time before the landlord
gives the notice to the tenant.

113.3.49A.3

But any such rent, service charge or administration charge is not to be so
treated in relation to any time when—

113.3.49A.3.a

by virtue of an order of any court or tribunal there is in force an
appointment of a receiver or manager whose functions include the receiving of
rent, service charges or administration charges from the tenant, or

113.3.49A.3.b

a special measures order (within the meaning of Schedule  7  to the Building
Safety Act 2022) is in force.

113.3.49A.4

The requirement to give a notice to a tenant under subsection  (1)  may be
satisfied by giving the notice to them at a time when they are a prospective
tenant.

113.3.49A.5

In this section “ relevant building safety information ” means—

113.3.49A.5.a

the fact that the premises consist of or include a dwelling in a higher-risk
building;

113.3.49A.5.b

the name of each person listed in subsection  (6) ;

113.3.49A.5.c

an email address and telephone number through which each person listed in
subsection (6) may be contacted;

113.3.49A.5.d

a postal address in England and Wales at which notices (including notices in
proceedings) may be served by the tenant on the principal accountable person
for the higher-risk building;

113.3.49A.5.e

a postal address for the regulator;

113.3.49A.5.f

such other information as may be prescribed in regulations made by the
Secretary of State.

113.3.49A.6

The persons are—

113.3.49A.6.a

the principal accountable person for the higher-risk building;

113.3.49A.6.b

any special measures manager for the higher-risk building;

113.3.49A.6.c

the regulator.

113.3.49A.7

In this section—

            “ higher-risk building ” has the meaning given in section 115 of
the Building Safety Act 2022;
“ principal accountable person ” has the meaning given in section 115 of that
Act;
“ the regulator ” has the meaning given in section 115 of that Act;
“ special measures manager ” has the meaning given in paragraph 1 of Schedule
7  to that Act.

#### Interpretation

##### Interpretation of 

115

In  this Part —

                  “ accountable person ” has the meaning given by section 72;
“ building safety risk ” has the meaning given by section 62;
“ compliance notice ” has the same meaning as in section 99;
“ contravention ” includes a failure to comply;
“ the data protection legislation ” has the meaning given by section 30;
“ fire and rescue authority ” has the meaning given by section 30;
“ higher-risk building ” has the meaning given by section 65;
“ local authority ” has the meaning given by section 30;
“ long lease ” means—
a lease granted for a term certain exceeding 21 years, whether or not it is
(or may become) terminable before the end of that term by notice given by the
tenant or by re-entry or forfeiture, or
a lease for a term fixed by law under a grant with a covenant or obligation
for perpetual renewal, other than a lease by sub-demise from one which is not
a long lease;
“ major incident ” has the meaning given by section 63;
“ maximum summary term for either-way offences ” has the meaning given by
section 30;
“ occupied ”: any reference to an “occupied” higher-risk building is to be
read in accordance with section 71;
“ owner ” means the person—
for the time being receiving the rackrent of the premises in question, whether
on the person’s own account or as agent or trustee for another person, or
who would so receive it if those premises were let at a rackrent;
and for this purpose “ rackrent ” has the meaning given by section 126 of the
Building Act 1984;
“ prescribed ” means prescribed by regulations made by the Secretary of State;
“ principal accountable person ” has the meaning given by section 73;
“ registered provider of social housing ” has the meaning given by section 80
of the Housing and Regeneration Act 2008;
“ the regulator ” has the meaning given by section 2;
“ resident ” and “resident of a higher-risk building” have the meaning given
by section 71;
“ residential unit ” means—
a dwelling, or
any other unit of living accommodation;
“ responsible ”: any reference to the part of a higher-risk building for which
an accountable person is responsible is to be read in accordance with section
74;
“ special measures manager ” has the meaning given by  paragraph 1  of
Schedule 7 ;
“ special measures order ” has the meaning given by  paragraph 1  of  Schedule
7 ;
“ the tribunal ” means the First-tier Tribunal.

#### Remediation of certain defects

##### Remediation of certain defects

116

116.1

remediation of relevant defects in relevant buildings.

116.2

In those sections—

116.2.a

sections 117 to 121 define “relevant building”, “qualifying lease”, “the
qualifying time”, “relevant defect” and “associate”;

116.2.b

section 122 and  Schedule 8  contain protections for tenants in respect of
costs connected with relevant defects, and impose liabilities on certain
landlords;

116.2.c

section 123 makes provision about remediation orders, under which a landlord
in a relevant building is required to remedy certain relevant defects;

116.2.d

section 124 makes provision about remediation contribution orders, under which
an associate of a landlord in a relevant building is required to contribute
towards the costs of remedying certain relevant defects;

116.2.e
