##### Meaning of “relevant building”

117

117.1

This section applies for the purposes of sections 119 to  124  and  Schedule 8
.

117.2

“ Relevant building ” means a self-contained building, or self-contained part
of a building, in England that contains at least two dwellings and—

117.2.a

is at least 11 metres high, or

117.2.b

has at least 5 storeys.

This is subject to subsection (3).

117.3

“ Relevant building ” does not include a self-contained building or self-
contained part of a building—

117.3.a

in relation to which a right under Part 1 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1987
(tenants’ right of first refusal) or Part 3 of that Act (compulsory
acquisition by tenants of landlord’s interest) has been exercised,

117.3.b

in relation to which the right to collective enfranchisement (within the
meaning of Chapter 1 of Part 1 of the Leasehold Reform, Housing and Urban
Development Act 1993) has been exercised,

117.3.c

if the freehold estate in the building or part of the building is leaseholder
owned (within the meaning of regulations made by the Secretary of State), or

117.3.d

which is on commonhold land.

117.4

For the purposes of this section a building is “self-contained” if it is
structurally detached.

117.5

For the purposes of this section a part of a building is “self-contained” if—

117.5.a

the part constitutes a vertical division of the building,

117.5.b

the structure of the building is such that the part could be redeveloped
independently of the remainder of the building, and

117.5.c

the relevant services provided for occupiers of that part—

117.5.c.i

are provided independently of the relevant services provided for occupiers of
the remainder of the building, or

117.5.c.ii

could be so provided without involving the carrying out of any works likely to
result in a significant interruption in the provision of any such services for
occupiers of the remainder of the building.

117.6

In subsection  (5)  “ relevant services ” means services provided by means of
pipes, cables or other fixed installations.

##### Section 117: height of buildings and number of storeys

118

118.1

This section applies for the purpose of section 117.

118.2

The height of a building is to be measured from ground level to the finished
surface of the floor of the top storey of the building (ignoring any storey
which is a roof-top machinery or plant area or consists exclusively of
machinery or plant rooms).

118.3

When determining the number of storeys in a building—

118.3.a

any storey below ground level is to be disregarded;

118.3.b

any mezzanine floor is to be regarded as a storey if its internal floor area
is at least half of the internal floor area of the largest storey in the
building which is not below ground level.

118.4

In subsection  (2)  “ ground level ”, in relation to a building, means—

118.4.a

the level of the surface of the ground immediately adjacent to the building,
or

118.4.b

where the level of the surface of the ground on which the building is situated
is not uniform, the level of the lowest part of the surface of the ground
immediately adjacent to it.

118.5

For the purposes of subsection  (3)  a storey is “below ground level” if any
part of the finished surface of the ceiling of the storey is below the level
of the surface of the ground immediately adjacent to that part of the
building.

##### Meaning of “qualifying lease” and “the qualifying time”

119

119.1

This section applies for the purposes of sections 122 to  124  and  Schedule 8
.

119.2

A lease is a “qualifying lease” if—

119.2.a

it is a long lease of a single dwelling in a relevant building,

119.2.b

the tenant under the lease is liable to pay a service charge,

119.2.c

the lease was granted before 14 February 2022, and

119.2.d

at the beginning of 14 February 2022 (“the qualifying time”)—

119.2.d.i

the dwelling was a relevant tenant’s only or principal home,

119.2.d.ii

a relevant tenant did not own any other dwelling in the United Kingdom, or

119.2.d.iii

a relevant tenant owned no more than two dwellings in the United Kingdom apart
from their interest under the lease.

119.3

Where a dwelling was at the qualifying time let under two or more leases to
which subsection  (2) (a)  and  (b)  apply, any of those leases which is
superior to any of the other leases is not a “qualifying lease”.

119.3A

A connected replacement lease (see section 119A) is also a “qualifying lease”.

119.4

For the purposes of this section—

119.4.a

“ long lease ” means a lease granted for a term of years certain exceeding 21
years, whether or not it is (or may become) terminable before the end of that
term by notice given by or to the tenant or by re-entry, forfeiture or
otherwise;

119.4.b

a person “owns” a dwelling in England, Wales or Northern Ireland if the person
has a freehold interest in it or is a tenant under a long lease of it;

119.4.c

“ relevant tenant ” means a person who, at the qualifying time, was the
tenant, or any of the tenants, under the lease mentioned in subsection  (2) ;

119.4.d

“ service charge ” has the meaning given by section 18 of the Landlord and
Tenant Act 1985.

##### Meaning of “connected replacement lease”

119A

119A.1

For the purposes of section 119 (and this section) a lease (the “new lease”)
is a “connected replacement lease” if—

119A.1.a

the new lease is a lease of a single dwelling in a relevant building,

119A.1.b

the tenant under the new lease is liable to pay a service charge,

119A.1.c

the new lease was granted on or after 14 February 2022,

119A.1.d

the new lease replaces—

119A.1.d.i

one other lease, which is a qualifying lease (whether under section 119(2) or
(3A)), or

119A.1.d.ii

two or more other leases, at least one of which is a qualifying lease (whether
under section 119(2) or (3A)), and

119A.1.e

there is continuity in the property let.

119A.2

For the purposes of subsection (1)(d), the new lease replaces another lease
if—

119A.2.a

the term of the new lease begins during the term of the other lease, and the
new lease is granted in substitution of the other lease, or

119A.2.b

the term of the new lease begins at the end of the term of the other lease
(regardless of when the lease is granted).

119A.3

For the purposes of subsection (2)(a), the circumstances in which the new
lease is granted in substitution of another lease include circumstances where—

119A.3.a

the new lease is granted by way of a surrender and regrant of the other lease
(including a deemed surrender and regrant, whether deemed under an enactment
or otherwise);

119A.3.b

the new lease is granted under—

119A.3.b.i

section 24 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1954 (renewed business leases),

119A.3.b.ii

section 14 of, or Schedule 1 to, the Leasehold Reform Act 1967 (extension of
leases of houses), or

119A.3.b.iii

section 56 of the Leasehold Reform, Housing and Urban Development Act 1993
(extension of leases of flats),

in a case where that provision of that Act applies by virtue of the other
lease.

119A.4

For the purposes of subsection (1)(e) there is continuity in the property let
if—

119A.4.a

the newly let property is exactly the same as the already let property,

119A.4.b

the newly let property consists of some or all of the already let property,
together with other property (whether or not that other property was
previously let) (a “property combination”), or

119A.4.c

the newly let property consists of some, but not all, of the already let
property (but no other property) (a “property reduction”).

119A.5

But there is no continuity in the property let by virtue of a property
reduction if, as respects any lease in the relevant chain of qualifying
leases, there was continuity in the property let by virtue of a property
combination.

119A.6

For that purpose, the “relevant” chain of qualifying leases is the chain of
qualifying leases of which the new lease would be part were it a connected
replacement lease.

119A.7

For the purposes of subsection (1)(e) there is also continuity in the property
let if the new lease is granted to rectify any error in the lease, or any
lease, which the new lease replaces.

119A.8

Where a dwelling is at any time on or after 14 February 2022 let under two or
more leases to which subsection (1)(a) and (b) apply, any of the leases which
is superior to any of the other leases is not a connected replacement lease.

119A.9

For the purposes of sections 122 to  124  and Schedule 8, all of the leases in
a chain of qualifying leases are to be treated as a single qualifying lease
which has a term that—

119A.9.a

began when the term of the initial qualifying lease in that chain began, and

119A.9.b

ends when the term of the current connected replacement lease in that chain
ends.

119A.10

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the meaning of
“ connected replacement lease ” (including provision changing the meaning).

119A.11

The provision that may be made in regulations under this section includes—

119A.11.a

provision which amends this section;

119A.11.b

provision which has retrospective effect.

119A.12

Provision in regulations under this section made by virtue of section
168(2)(a) (consequential provision etc) may (in particular) amend this Act.

119A.13

In this section—

“ already let property ”, in relation to a new lease, means the property let
by the lease or leases which the new lease replaces; “ chain of qualifying
leases ” means— an initial qualifying lease which is the preceding qualifying
lease in relation to a connected replacement lease (the “first replacement
lease”), the first replacement lease, and any other connected replacement
lease if the preceding qualifying lease in relation to it is— the first
replacement lease, or any other connected replacement lease which is in the
chain of qualifying leases; and a chain of qualifying leases may accordingly
consist of different leases at different times (if further connected
replacement leases are granted); “ current connected replacement lease ”, in
relation to a particular time, means a connected replacement lease during the
term of which that time falls; “ initial qualifying lease ” means a lease
which is a qualifying lease under section 119(2); “ new lease ” has the
meaning given in subsection (1); “ newly let property ” means the property let
by the new lease; “ preceding qualifying lease ”, in relation to the new
lease, means— in a case within subsection (1)(d)(i), the lease which the new
lease replaces; in a case within subsection (1)(d)(ii), a lease which— the new
lease replaces, and is a qualifying lease.

119A.14

The definitions in section 119(4) also apply for the purposes of this section.

##### Meaning of “relevant defect” 

120

120.1

This section applies for the purposes of sections 122 to  124  and  Schedule 8
.

120.2

“ Relevant defect ”, in relation to a building, means a defect as regards the
building that—

120.2.a

arises as a result of anything done (or not done), or anything used (or not
used), in connection with relevant works, and

120.2.b

causes a building safety risk.

120.3

In subsection  (2)  “ relevant works ” means any of the following—

120.3.a

works relating to the construction or conversion of the building, if the
construction or conversion was completed in the relevant period;

120.3.b

works undertaken or commissioned by or on behalf of a relevant landlord or
management company, if the works were completed in the relevant period;

120.3.c

works undertaken after the end of the relevant period to remedy a relevant
defect (including a defect that is a relevant defect by virtue of this
paragraph).

“The relevant period” here means the period of 30 years ending with the time
this section comes into force.

120.4

In subsection  (2)  the reference to anything done (or not done) in connection
with relevant works includes anything done (or not done) in the provision of
professional services in connection with such works.

120.4A

“ Relevant steps ”, in relation to a relevant defect, means steps which have
as their purpose—

120.4A.a

preventing or reducing the likelihood of a fire or collapse of the building
(or any part of it) occurring as a result of the relevant defect,

120.4A.b

reducing the severity of any such incident, or

120.4A.c

preventing or reducing harm to people in or about the building that could
result from such an incident.

120.5

For the purposes of this section—

“ building safety risk ”, in relation to a building, means a risk to the
safety of people in or about the building arising from— the spread of fire, or
the collapse of the building or any part of it; “ conversion ” means the
conversion of the building for use (wholly or partly) for residential
purposes; “ relevant landlord or management company ” means a landlord under a
lease of the building or any part of it or any person who is party to such a
lease otherwise than as landlord or tenant.

##### Associated persons

121

121.1

For the purposes of sections 122 to  124  and  Schedule 8 , a partnership or
body corporate is associated with another person in the circumstances
mentioned in subsections  (2)  to  (5) .

121.2

Where a person’s interest in a relevant building was held on trust at the
qualifying time, any partnership or body corporate which was a beneficiary of
the trust at that time is to be regarded, for the purposes of the provisions
mentioned in subsection  (1)  as they apply in relation to the relevant
building, as associated with the person.

121.3

A partnership is associated with any person who was a partner in the
partnership, other than a limited partner, at any time in the period of 5
years ending at the qualifying time (“ the relevant period ”).

121.4

A body corporate is associated with any person who was a director of the body
corporate at any time in the relevant period.

121.5

A body corporate is associated with another body corporate if—

121.5.a

at any time in the relevant period a person was a director of both of them, or

121.5.b

at the qualifying time, one of them controlled the other or a third body
corporate controlled both of them.

Subsections  (6)  to  (8)  set out the cases in which a body corporate is
regarded as controlling another body corporate.

121.6

A body corporate (X) controls a company (Y) if X possesses or is entitled to
acquire—

121.6.a

at least half of the issued share capital of Y,

121.6.b

such rights as would entitle X to exercise at least half of the votes
exercisable in general meetings of Y,

121.6.c

such part of the issued share capital of Y as would entitle X to at least half
of the amount distributed, if the whole of the income of Y were in fact
distributed among the shareholders, or

121.6.d

such rights as would, in the event of the winding up of Y or in any other
circumstances, entitle it to receive at least half of the assets of Y which
would then be available for distribution among the shareholders.

121.7

A body corporate (X) controls a limited liability partnership (Y) if X—

121.7.a

holds a majority of the voting rights in Y,

121.7.b

is a member of Y and has a right to appoint or remove a majority of other
members, or

121.7.c

is a member of Y and controls alone, or pursuant to an agreement with other
members, a majority of the voting rights in Y.

121.8

A body corporate (X) controls another body corporate (Y) if X has the power,
directly or indirectly, to secure that the affairs of Y are conducted in
accordance with X’s wishes.

121.9

In subsection  (7)  a reference to “voting rights” is to the rights conferred
on members in respect of their interest in a limited liability partnership to
vote on those matters which are to be decided on by a vote of the members of
the limited liability partnership.

121.10

In determining whether one body corporate (X) controls another, X is treated
as possessing—

121.10.a

any rights and powers possessed by a person as nominee for it, and

121.10.b

any rights and powers possessed by a body corporate which it controls
(including rights and powers which such a body corporate would be taken to
possess by virtue of this paragraph).

121.11

In this section “ partnership ” means—

121.11.a

a partnership within the meaning of the Partnership Act 1890, or

121.11.b

a limited partnership registered under the Limited Partnerships Act 1907,

or a firm or entity of a similar character formed under the law of a country
or territory outside the United Kingdom (and the reference to “limited
partner” is to be read accordingly).

121.12

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that, in relation to a
prescribed reference in a provision mentioned in subsection  (1)  to anyone
associated with another person, subsections  (2)  to  (5)  have effect with
prescribed modifications.

##### Remediation costs under qualifying leases etc

122

Schedule 8 —

122.a

provides that certain service charge amounts relating to relevant defects in a
relevant building are not payable, and

122.b

makes provision for the recovery of those amounts from persons who are
landlords under leases of the building (or any part of it).

##### Remediation orders

123

123.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for and in connection
with remediation orders.

123.2

A “remediation order” is an order, made by the First-tier Tribunal on the
application of an interested person, requiring a relevant landlord to  do one
or both of the following by a specified time—

123.2.a

remedy specified relevant defects in a specified relevant building;

123.2.b

take specified relevant steps in relation to a specified relevant defect in a
specified relevant building.

123.3

In this section “ relevant landlord ”, in relation to a relevant defect in a
relevant building, means a landlord under a lease of the building or any part
of it who is required, under the lease or by virtue of an enactment, to repair
or maintain anything relating to the relevant defect.

123.4

In subsection  (3)  the reference to a landlord under a lease includes any
person who is party to the lease otherwise than as landlord or tenant.

123.5

In this section “ interested person ”, in relation to a relevant building,
means—

123.5.a

the regulator (as defined by section 2),

123.5.b

a local authority (as defined by section 30) for the area in which the
relevant building is situated,

123.5.c

a fire and rescue authority (as defined by section 30) for the area in which
the relevant building is situated,

123.5.d

a person with a legal or equitable interest in the relevant building or any
part of it, or

123.5.e

any other person prescribed by the regulations.

123.6

In this section—

“ relevant building ”: see section 117; “ relevant defect ”: see section 120;
“ relevant steps ”: see section 120; “ specified ” means specified in the
order.

123.7

A decision of the First-tier Tribunal or Upper Tribunal made under or in
connection with this section (other than one ordering the payment of a sum) is
enforceable with the permission of the county court in the same way as an
order of that court.

123.8

In proceedings for a remediation order, a direction given by the First-tier
Tribunal requiring a relevant landlord to provide or produce an expert report
is to be regarded as a decision for the purposes of subsection (7).

123.9

In subsection  (8) , “ expert report ” means an expert report or survey
relating to—

123.9.a

relevant defects, or potential relevant defects, in a relevant building;

123.9.b

relevant steps taken or that might be taken in relation to a relevant defect
in a relevant building.

##### Remediation contribution orders

124

124.1

The First-tier Tribunal may, on the application of an interested person, make
a remediation contribution order in relation to a relevant building if it
considers it just and equitable to do so.

124.2

“ Remediation contribution order ”, in relation to a relevant building, means
an order requiring a specified body corporate or partnership to make payments
to a specified person, for the purpose of meeting costs incurred or to be
incurred in remedying  , or otherwise in connection with,  relevant defects
(or specified relevant defects) relating to the relevant building.

124.2A

The following descriptions of costs, among others, fall within subsection (2)—

124.2A.a

costs incurred or to be incurred in taking relevant steps in relation to a
relevant defect in the relevant building;

124.2A.b

costs incurred or to be incurred in obtaining an expert report relating to the
relevant building;

124.2A.c

temporary accommodation costs incurred or to be incurred in connection with a
decant from the relevant building (or from part of it) that took place or is
to take place—

124.2A.c.i

to avoid an imminent threat to life or of personal injury arising from a
relevant defect in the building,

124.2A.c.ii

(in the case of a decant from a dwelling) because works relating to the
building created or are expected to create circumstances in which those
occupying the dwelling cannot reasonably be expected to live, or

124.2A.c.iii

for any other reason connected with relevant defects in the building, or works
relating to the building, that is prescribed by regulations made by the
Secretary of State.

124.2B

The Secretary of State may make regulations for the purposes of this section
specifying descriptions of costs which are, or are not, to be regarded as
falling within subsection (2).

124.3

A body corporate or partnership may be specified  as a person required to make
payments  only if it is—

124.3.a

a landlord under a lease of the relevant building or any part of it,

124.3.b

a person who was such a landlord at the qualifying time,

124.3.c

a developer in relation to the relevant building, or

124.3.d

a person associated with a person within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (c) .

124.4

An order may—

124.4.a

require the making of payments of a specified amount,  ...;

124.4.aa

if it does not require the making of payments of a specified amount, determine
that a specified body corporate or partnership is liable for the reasonable
costs of specified things done or to be done;

124.4.b

require a payment to be made at a specified time, or to be made on demand
following the occurrence of a specified event.

124.5

In this section—

“ associated ”: see section 121; “ developer ”, in relation to a relevant
building, means a person who undertook or commissioned the construction or
conversion of the building (or part of the building) with a view to granting
or disposing of interests in the building or parts of it; “ expert report ”
has the meaning given by section 123(9); “ interested person ”, in relation to
a relevant building, means— the Secretary of State, the regulator (as defined
by section 2), a local authority (as defined by section 30) for the area in
which the relevant building is situated, a fire and rescue authority (as
defined by section 30) for the area in which the relevant building is
situated, a person with a legal or equitable interest in the relevant building
or any part of it, or any other person prescribed by regulations made by the
Secretary of State; “ partnership ” has the meaning given by section 121; “
relevant building ”: see section 117; “ relevant defect ”: see section 120; “
relevant steps ”: see section 120; “ specified ” means specified in the order.
“ temporary accommodation costs ”, in relation to a decant from a relevant
building, means— the costs of the temporary accommodation, and other costs
resulting from the decant, including removal costs, storage costs and
reasonable travel costs; “ works ” means works— to remedy a relevant defect in
a relevant building, or in connection with the taking of relevant steps in
relation to such a defect.

124.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that this section applies,
with or without modifications, in relation to a building that would, but for
section 117 (3) , be a relevant building.

##### Meeting remediation costs of insolvent landlord

125

. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .

#### Insolvency of certain persons with an interest in higher-risk and relevant buildings

##### Notifications by insolvency practitioners

125A

125A.1

This section applies if an insolvency practitioner is appointed in relation to
a responsible person for a higher-risk building or a relevant building.

125A.2

For the purposes of this section, a person is “a responsible person” for a
building if—

125A.2.a

in the case of a higher-risk building, the person is an accountable person for
the building (see section 72 for the meaning of “accountable person” for a
higher-risk building);

125A.2.b

in the case of a relevant building that is not a higher-risk building, the
person would be an accountable person for the building if section 72 were read
as applying to such a building (and as if the reference in that section to a
residential unit were a reference to a dwelling).

125A.3

The insolvency practitioner must give the information in subsection  (6)
(“the required information”) to—

125A.3.a

the local authority for the area in which the building for which the person is
a responsible person is situated, or (if applicable) each local authority in
whose area a building for which the person is a responsible person is
situated, and

125A.3.b

the fire and rescue authority for the area in which the building for which the
person is a responsible person is situated, or (if applicable) each fire and
rescue authority in whose area a building for which the person is a
responsible person is situated.

125A.4

If the insolvency practitioner is appointed in relation to an accountable
person for a higher-risk building, the practitioner must also give the
required information to the regulator.

125A.5

The required information must be provided within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the insolvency practitioner is appointed.

125A.6

The information is as follows—

125A.6.a

the name and address of the person in relation to whom the insolvency
practitioner is appointed;

125A.6.b

the address of each higher-risk building or relevant building for which the
person is a responsible person (but see subsection  (7) );

125A.6.c

an official copy of the register of title and title plan relating to each
registered estate or interest the person holds in such a building, if any (but
see subsection  (7) );

125A.6.d

the nature of the practitioner’s appointment;

125A.6.e

the practitioner’s name, address, telephone number and email address (if any);

125A.6.f

so much of the information set out in the table in rule 1.6 of the Insolvency
(England and Wales) Rules 2016 ( S.I. 2016/1024 ) as is known to the
practitioner.

125A.7

A local authority or fire and rescue authority need only be notified about
buildings, or registered estates or interests in buildings, in their area.

125A.8

In this section “ insolvency practitioner ” means—

125A.8.a

an administrator;

125A.8.b

an administrative receiver;

125A.8.c

a receiver appointed by the courts or by a mortgagee;

125A.8.d

a liquidator;

125A.8.e

a trustee in bankruptcy.

125A.9

In this section—

“ fire and rescue authority ” has the meaning given by section 30; “ higher-
risk building ” has the same meaning as in Part 4 (see section 65); “ local
authority ” has the meaning given by section 30; “ register of title ” means
the register kept under section 1 of the Land Registration Act 2002; “ the
regulator ” has the meaning given by section 2; “ relevant building ” has the
meaning given by section 117; “ title plan ” means a plan based on the
Ordnance Survey map and referred to in the register of title.

#### Building industry schemes

##### Building industry schemes

126

126.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

126.1.a

establish a scheme to be maintained by the Secretary of State, or a person
designated by the Secretary of State and acting on the Secretary of State’s
behalf, and

126.1.b

make provision about the scheme.

126.2

A scheme may be established for any purpose connected with—

126.2.a

securing the safety of people in or about buildings in relation to risks
arising from buildings, or

126.2.b

improving the standard of buildings,

including securing that safety, or improving that standard, by securing that
persons in the building industry remedy defects in buildings or contribute to
costs associated with remedying defects in buildings.

126.3

Regulations that establish a scheme must prescribe—

126.3.a

the descriptions of persons in the building industry who may be members of the
scheme (“eligible persons”), and

126.3.b

the conditions that an eligible person must meet in order to become, and
remain, a member of the scheme (“membership conditions”),

and may provide for different categories of membership.

126.4

The membership conditions that may be prescribed include in particular
conditions relating to—

126.4.a

the remedying of defects in buildings with which an eligible person has a
connection of a prescribed kind;

126.4.b

the making of financial contributions towards meeting costs associated with
remedying defects in buildings (including buildings with which an eligible
person has no connection);

126.4.c

the use (or use in prescribed cases) of construction products (or construction
products of a prescribed description) of prescribed persons carrying out
activities in relation to construction products;

126.4.d

the provision of information to the Secretary of State or any other person;

126.4.e

the competence or conduct of any individual connected with an eligible person
(for example, any director or senior manager of an eligible person) or any
person with whom an eligible person contracts;

126.4.f

whether persons with whom an eligible person contracts are members of a
scheme.

In paragraph  (e)  “ conduct ” includes conduct occurring before the coming
into force of this section.

126.5

The descriptions of persons prescribed by virtue of subsection  (4) (c)  may
in particular be prescribed by reference to—

126.5.a

being eligible to be members of a scheme and not being members of that scheme;

126.5.b

their conduct in relation to remedying defects in buildings or contributing to
costs associated with remedying defects in buildings.

126.6

The membership conditions that may be prescribed by virtue of subsection  (4)
(c)  include in particular a condition requiring an eligible person to ensure
that no prescribed product of prescribed persons carrying out activities in
relation to construction products is used in prescribed cases.

126.7

The Secretary of State must ensure that a list of members of a scheme is kept
and published (and may publish a list of persons who are eligible persons but
are not members of a scheme).

126.8

Regulations may make provision about the keeping and publication of other
lists.

##### Building industry schemes: supplementary

127

127.1

This section supplements section 126.

127.2

Regulations may make provision about—

127.2.a

applications for membership of a scheme;

127.2.b

renewal of membership at prescribed intervals;

127.2.c

termination of a person’s membership;

127.2.d

the suspension of a person from membership.

127.3

Regulations may provide for the charging of fees, in connection with—

127.3.a

an application for membership;

127.3.b

renewal of membership;

127.3.c

a review;

127.3.d

any other prescribed matter.

127.4

Regulations may provide for membership conditions to be framed by reference
to—

127.4.a

standards, or a document, from time to time published by any person;

127.4.b

the opinion of the Secretary of State, or a designated person, in relation to
any matter.

127.5

Regulations may make provision about the determination of disputes.

127.6

Regulations may make provision about the termination of a scheme.

127.7

In section 126 and this section—

“ building ” means a building in England; “ building industry ”: a reference
to persons in the building industry is to persons carrying on, for business
purposes, activities connected with the design, construction, management or
maintenance of buildings, including persons carrying out activities in
relation to construction products in England; “ construction product ” has the
meaning given by regulations; “ persons carrying out activities in relation to
construction products ” include (without limitation)— a manufacturer of
construction products, a person who markets or supplies construction products
to others, and a person who imports construction products into the United
Kingdom for use, marketing or supply; “ prescribed ” means prescribed by the
regulations; “ regulations ” means regulations under section 126; “ scheme ”
means a scheme established under section 126; “ standard ” (except in
subsection (4) of this section) is to be read in accordance with section 30.

#### Prohibitions on development and building control

##### Prohibition on development for prescribed persons

128

128.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations prohibit a person of a prescribed
description from carrying out development of land in England (or a prescribed
description of such development).

128.2

The descriptions of persons which may be prescribed include in particular
persons who—

128.2.a

are eligible to be members of a scheme established under section 126, and

128.2.b

are not members of that scheme.

128.3

A prohibition under the regulations may be imposed for any purpose connected
with—

128.3.a

securing the safety of people in or about buildings in relation to risks
arising from buildings, or

128.3.b

improving the standard of buildings,

including securing that safety, or improving that standard, by securing that
persons in the building industry remedy defects in buildings or contribute to
costs associated with remedying defects in buildings.

128.4

A prohibition under the regulations applies despite planning permission (or
any prescribed description of planning permission) having been granted.

128.5

The regulations may provide that, in prescribed cases, no prescribed
certificate under the 1990 Act may be granted (and any purported grant is of
no effect).

128.6

The regulations may require a person of a prescribed description to give a
notification relating to development (and may make provision about the content
and form of a notification and the way in which it is to be given).

128.7

The regulations may contain exceptions.

128.8

The regulations may make provision about enforcement, including in particular
provision applying (with or without modifications), in relation to a breach of
the regulations, any provision of Part 7 of the 1990 Act (enforcement).

128.9

For the purposes of this section—

128.9.a

“ the 1990 Act ” means the Town and Country Planning Act 1990;

128.9.b

“ building ” means a building in England;

128.9.c

“ development ” has the meaning given by section 55 of the 1990 Act;

128.9.d

“ planning permission ” has the meaning given by section 336 of the 1990 Act;

128.9.e

“ prescribed ” means prescribed by regulations under this section;

128.9.f

“ standard ” is to be read in accordance with section 30.

##### Building control prohibitions

129

129.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations impose a building control
prohibition, as regards buildings or proposed buildings, in relation to
persons of a prescribed description.

129.2

The descriptions of persons which may be prescribed include in particular
persons who—

129.2.a

are eligible to be members of a scheme established under section 126, and

129.2.b

are not members of that scheme.

129.3

A building control prohibition may be imposed for any purpose connected with—

129.3.a

securing the safety of people in or about buildings in relation to risks
arising from buildings, or

129.3.b

improving the standard of buildings,

including securing that safety, or improving that standard, by securing that
persons in the building industry remedy defects in buildings or contribute to
costs associated with remedying defects in buildings.

129.4

A “ building control prohibition ”, in relation to a person, prohibits—

129.4.a

the person from applying for building control approval or from depositing
plans,

129.4.b

the person from giving an initial notice (whether or not jointly with anyone
else) or a public body’s notice, public body’s plans certificate or public
body’s final certificate,

129.4.c

the granting of building control approval to the person,

129.4.d

the passing of plans deposited by the person,

129.4.e

the acceptance of an initial notice given by the person (whether or not
jointly with anyone else) or a public body’s notice, public body’s plans
certificate or public body’s final certificate given by the person,

129.4.f

the giving of a final certificate in relation to works carried out by the
person,

129.4.g

the person from giving a prescribed document,

129.4.h

the giving of a prescribed document to the person or in respect of works
carried out by the person, or

129.4.i

the acceptance of any prescribed document given by the person or in respect of
works carried out by the person.

129.5

A building control prohibition applies despite any provision made by or under
the Building Act 1984.

129.6

The regulations may contain exceptions.

129.7

The regulations may provide that anything done in contravention of the
regulations is of no effect.

129.8

Any reference in this section to a building or proposed building is to a
building or proposed building in England.

129.9

In this section—

“ building” and “building control approval ”, and references to the deposit
and passing of plans, are to be read in accordance with Part 1 of the Building
Act 1984; “ initial notice”, “final certificate”, “public body’s notice”,
“public body’s plans certificate” and “public body’s final certificate ” have
the same meaning as in Part 2 of that Act; “ prescribed ” means prescribed by
regulations under this section; “ standard ” is to be read in accordance with
section 30.

#### Building liability orders

##### Building liability orders

130

130.1

The High Court may make a building liability order if it considers it just and
equitable to do so.

130.2

A “building liability order” is an order providing that any relevant liability
(or any relevant liability of a specified description) of a body corporate (“
the original body ”) relating to a specified building is also—

130.2.a

a liability of a specified body corporate, or

130.2.b

a joint and several liability of two or more specified bodies corporate.

130.3

In this section “ relevant liability ” means a liability (whether arising
before or after commencement) that is incurred—

130.3.a

under the Defective Premises Act 1972 or section 38 of the Building Act 1984,
or

130.3.b

as a result of a building safety risk.

130.4

A body corporate may be specified only if it is, or has at any time in the
relevant period been, associated with the original body.

130.5

A building liability order—

130.5.a

may be made in respect of a liability of a body corporate that has been
dissolved (including where dissolution occurred before commencement);

130.5.b

continues to have effect even if the body corporate is dissolved after the
making of the order.

130.6

In this section—

“ associate ”: see section 131; “ building safety risk ”, in relation to a
building, means a risk to the safety of people in or about the building
arising from the spread of fire or structural failure; “ commencement ” means
the time this section comes into force; “ the relevant period ” means the
period— beginning with the beginning of the carrying out of the works in
relation to which the relevant liability was incurred, and ending with the
making of the order; “ specified ” means specified in the building liability
order.

##### Building liability orders: associates

131

131.1

For the purposes of section 130, a body corporate (A) is associated with
another body corporate (B) if—

131.1.a

one of them controls the other, or

131.1.b

a third body corporate controls both of them.

Subsections  (2)  to  (4)  set out the cases in which a body corporate is
regarded as controlling another body corporate.

131.2

A body corporate (X) controls a company (Y) if X possesses or is entitled to
acquire—

131.2.a

at least half of the issued share capital of Y,

131.2.b

such rights as would entitle X to exercise at least half of the votes
exercisable in general meetings of Y,

131.2.c

such part of the issued share capital of Y as would entitle X to at least half
of the amount distributed, if the whole of the income of Y were in fact
distributed among the shareholders, or

131.2.d

such rights as would, in the event of the winding up of Y or in any other
circumstances, entitle it to receive at least half of the assets of Y which
would then be available for distribution among the shareholders.

131.3

A body corporate (X) controls a limited liability partnership (Y) if X—

131.3.a

holds a majority of the voting rights in Y,

131.3.b

is a member of Y and has a right to appoint or remove a majority of other
members, or

131.3.c

is a member of Y and controls alone, or pursuant to an agreement with other
members, a majority of the voting rights in Y.

131.4

A body corporate (X) controls another body corporate (Y) if X has the power,
directly or indirectly, to secure that the affairs of Y are conducted in
accordance with X’s wishes.

131.5

In subsection  (3)  a reference to “voting rights” is to the rights conferred
on members in respect of their interest in a limited liability partnership to
vote on those matters which are to be decided on by a vote of the members of
the limited liability partnership.

131.6

In determining under any of subsections  (2)  to  (4)  whether one body
corporate (X) controls another, X is treated as possessing—

131.6.a

any rights and powers possessed by a person as nominee for it, and

131.6.b

any rights and powers possessed by a body corporate which it controls
(including rights and powers which such a body corporate would be taken to
possess by virtue of this paragraph).

131.7

For the purposes of section 130 as it applies in relation to a building, where
a person’s interest in the building is held on trust, a body corporate which
is a beneficiary of the trust is to be regarded as associated with the person.

##### Order for information in connection with building liability order

132

132.1

A person of a prescribed description may apply to the High Court for an
information order.

132.2

An “information order” is an order requiring a specified body corporate to
give, by a specified time, specified information or documents relating to
persons who are, or have at any time in a specified period been, associated
with the body corporate.

132.3

An information order may be made only if it appears to the court—

132.3.a

that the body corporate is subject to a relevant liability (within the meaning
of section 130), and

132.3.b

that it is appropriate to require the information or documents to be provided
for the purpose of enabling the applicant (or the applicant and others) to
make, or consider whether to make, an application for a building liability
order.

132.4

In this section—

“ associate ”: section 131 applies for the purposes of this section as it
applies for the purposes of section 130; “ building liability order ”: see
section 130; “ prescribed ” means prescribed by regulations made by the
Secretary of State; “ specified ” means specified in the information order.

#### Remediation and redress: other provisions

##### Service charges in respect of remediation works

133

133.1

The Landlord and Tenant Act 1985 is amended as follows.

133.2

In section 20(1)(b) (limitation of service charges: consultation requirements)
at the beginning insert  “except in the case of works to which  section 20D
applies,” .

133.3

In section 20ZA (consultation requirements: supplementary) after subsection
(5) insert—

133.3.5A

And in the case of works to which  section 20D  applies, regulations under
subsection (4) may also include provision requiring the landlord—

133.3.5A.a

to give details of the steps taken or to be taken under  section 20D (2) ,

133.3.5A.b

to give reasons about prescribed matters, and any other prescribed
information, relating to the taking of such steps, and

133.3.5A.c

to have regard to observations made by tenants or the recognised tenants’
association in relation to the taking of such steps.

133.4

After section 20C insert—

########### Limitation of service charges: remediation works

133.4.20D

133.4.20D.1

This section applies to works of a prescribed description (“remediation
works”) on a building in England of a prescribed description.

133.4.20D.2

The landlord must—

133.4.20D.2.a

take reasonable steps to ascertain whether any grant is payable in respect of
the remediation works and, if so, to obtain the grant;

133.4.20D.2.b

take reasonable steps to ascertain whether monies may be obtained from a third
party in connection with the undertaking of the remediation works and, if so,
to obtain monies from the third party;

133.4.20D.2.c

take prescribed steps relating to any other prescribed kind of funding.

133.4.20D.3

In  subsection (2) (b)  the reference to obtaining monies from a third party
includes obtaining monies—

133.4.20D.3.a

under a policy of insurance;

133.4.20D.3.b

under a guarantee or indemnity;

133.4.20D.3.c

pursuant to a claim made against—

133.4.20D.3.c.i

a developer;

133.4.20D.3.c.ii

a person involved in the design of the building or of works to the building;
or

133.4.20D.3.c.iii

a person involved in carrying out works in relation to the building.

133.4.20D.4

Where any funding of a kind mentioned in  subsection (2)  is obtained, the
amount of the funding is to be deducted from the remediation costs (and the
amount of any service charge is to be reduced accordingly).

133.4.20D.5

In the case of a failure to comply with  subsection (2) , a tenant may make an
application for an order that all or any of remediation costs are not to be
regarded as relevant costs to be taken into account in determining the amount
of any service charge payable by—

133.4.20D.5.a

the tenant, or

133.4.20D.5.b

anyone else specified in the application.

133.4.20D.6

An application is to be made to the prescribed court or tribunal.

133.4.20D.7

The court or tribunal to which the application is made may make such order on
the application as it considers just and equitable in the circumstances.

133.4.20D.8

Nothing in this section requires the landlord to do anything mentioned in
subsection (2)  before carrying out remediation works.

133.4.20D.9

The Secretary of State may issue guidance about the taking of steps under
subsection (2) , and may revise or withdraw any issued guidance.

133.4.20D.10

Where on an application under this section it is alleged that a person failed
to comply with  subsection (2) —

133.4.20D.10.a

proof of a failure to comply with any applicable guidance may be relied on as
tending to establish that there was such a failure, and

133.4.20D.10.b

proof of compliance with any applicable guidance may be relied on as tending
to establish that there was no such failure.

133.4.20D.11

In this section—

“ developer ”, in relation to a building, means a person who undertakes or
commissions the construction or conversion of the building with a view to
granting or disposing of interests in the building (or parts of it); “
prescribed ” means prescribed by regulations made by the Secretary of State; “
remediation costs ” means costs incurred or to be incurred in carrying out the
remediation works; “ third party ” means a person other than a tenant.

########### Regulations under 

133.4.20E

133.4.20E.1

In this section “ regulations ” means regulations under  section 20D .

133.4.20E.2

Regulations are to be made by statutory instrument.

133.4.20E.3

A power to make regulations includes power to make—

133.4.20E.3.a

incidental, transitional or saving provision;

133.4.20E.3.b

different provision for different purposes.

133.4.20E.4

A statutory instrument containing regulations is subject to annulment in
pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

##### Duties relating to work to dwellings etc

134

134.1

In the Defective Premises Act 1972 after section 2 insert—

########### Duties relating to work to dwellings etc

134.1.2A

134.1.2A.1

This section applies where a person, in the course of a business, takes on
work in relation to any part of a relevant building.

134.1.2A.2

In this section “ relevant building ” means a building consisting of or
containing one or more dwellings.

134.1.2A.3

The person owes a duty to—

134.1.2A.3.a

the person for whom the work is done, and

134.1.2A.3.b

each person who holds or acquires an interest (whether legal or equitable) in
a dwelling in the building,

to see that the work is done in a workmanlike or (as the case may be)
professional manner, with proper materials and so that as regards the work the
dwelling is fit for habitation when the work is completed.

134.1.2A.4

The duty under this section does not apply in relation to a dwelling if—

134.1.2A.4.a

the work taken on is work for or in connection with the provision of the
dwelling (as to which see section 1), or

134.1.2A.4.b

it is expected that, on completion of the work, it will have ceased to be a
dwelling or will otherwise have ceased to exist.

134.1.2A.5

A person (A) who takes on any work to which this section applies for another
(B) on terms that A is to do it in accordance with instructions given by or on
behalf of B is, to the extent to which A does it properly in accordance with
those instructions, to be treated for the purposes of this section as
discharging the duty imposed on A by this section except where A owes a duty
to B to warn B of any defects in the instructions and fails to discharge that
duty.

134.1.2A.6

A person is not treated for the purposes of  subsection (5)  as having given
instructions for the doing of work merely because the person has agreed to the
work being done in a specified manner, with specified materials or to a
specified design.

134.1.2A.7

A person who, in the course of a business which consists of or includes
carrying out or arranging for the carrying out of work of a kind mentioned in
subsection (1) , arranges for another to take on work of that kind is treated
for the purposes of this section as included among the persons who have taken
on the work.

134.1.2A.8

For the purposes of the Limitation Act 1980, a cause of action in respect of a
breach of a duty imposed by this section is treated as accruing at the time
the work is completed; but if after that time a person does further work to
rectify the work the person has already done, any such cause of action in
respect of that further work is treated as accruing at the time when the
further work is finished.

134.2

The amendment made by this section applies in relation to work completed after
the coming into force of this section.

##### Limitation periods

135

135.1

After section 4A of the Limitation Act 1980 insert—

########### Special time limit for certain actions in respect of damage or defects in relation to buildings

135.1.4B

135.1.4B.1

Where by virtue of a relevant provision a person becomes entitled to bring an
action against any other person, no action may be brought after the expiration
of 15 years from the date on which the right of action accrued.

135.1.4B.2

An action referred to in subsection (1) is one to which—

135.1.4B.2.a

sections 1, 28, 32, 35, 37 and 38 apply;

135.1.4B.2.b

the other provisions of this Act do not apply.

135.1.4B.3

In this section “ relevant provision ” means—

135.1.4B.3.a

section 1 or 2A of the Defective Premises Act 1972;

135.1.4B.3.b

section 38 of the Building Act 1984.

135.1.4B.4

Where by virtue of section 1 of the Defective Premises Act 1972 a person
became entitled, before the commencement date, to bring an action against any
other person, this section applies in relation to the action as if the
reference in subsection (1) to 15 years were a reference to 30 years.

135.1.4B.5

In subsection (4) “ the commencement date ” means the day on which section 135
of the Building Safety Act 2022 came into force.

135.2

In section 1(5) of the Defective Premises Act 1972, for “the Limitation Act
1939, the Law Reform (Limitation of Actions, &c.) Act 1954 and the Limitation
Act 1963” substitute  “the Limitation Act 1980” .

135.3

The amendment made by  subsection (1)  in relation to an action by virtue of
section 1 of the Defective Premises Act 1972 is to be treated as always having
been in force.

135.4

In a case where—

135.4.a

by virtue of section 1 of the Defective Premises Act 1972 a person became
entitled, before the day on which this section came into force, to bring an
action against any other person, and

135.4.b

the period of 30 years from the date on which the right of action accrued
expires in the initial period,

section 4B of the Limitation Act 1980 (inserted by subsection (1)) has effect
as if it provided that the action may not be brought after the end of the
initial period.

135.5

Where an action is brought that, but for  subsection (3) , would have been
barred by the Limitation Act 1980, a court hearing the action must dismiss it
in relation to any defendant if satisfied that it is necessary to do so to
avoid a breach of that defendant’s Convention rights.

135.6

Nothing in this section applies in relation to a claim which, before this
section came into force, was settled by agreement between the parties or
finally determined by a court or arbitration (whether on the basis of
limitation or otherwise).

135.7

In this section—

“ Convention rights ” has the same meaning as in the Human Rights Act 1998; “
the initial period ” means the period of one year beginning with the day on
which this section comes into force.

#### New homes ombudsman scheme

##### Establishment of the new homes ombudsman scheme

136

136.1

The Secretary of State must make arrangements for there to be a scheme, to be
known as the “new homes ombudsman scheme”, which meets the conditions in
section 137 (1) .

136.2

Examples of arrangements under  subsection (1)  are arrangements—

136.2.a

with another person under which that other person agrees to establish and
maintain the new homes ombudsman scheme in accordance with the terms of the
arrangements,

136.2.b

under which the new homes ombudsman scheme is established and maintained by
(or on behalf of) the Secretary of State, or

136.2.c

for the maintenance of the new homes ombudsman scheme, in accordance with the
terms of the arrangements, by a person other than the person who established
it.

136.3

The Secretary of State may—

136.3.a

give financial assistance (by way of grant, loan, guarantee or in any other
form) to a person for the establishment or maintenance of the new homes
ombudsman scheme;

136.3.b

make payments to such a person (otherwise than as financial assistance) in
accordance with arrangements under  subsection (1) .

136.4

Before making arrangements under subsection (1), the Secretary of State must
consult—

136.4.a

the Welsh Ministers,

136.4.b

the Scottish Ministers, and

136.4.c

the relevant Northern Ireland department.

136.5

In this section, “ the relevant Northern Ireland department ” means—

136.5.a

the Northern Ireland department designated for the purposes of this section by
the First Minister and deputy First Minister acting jointly, or

136.5.b

failing such a designation, the Executive Office in Northern Ireland.

##### The new homes ombudsman scheme

137

137.1

The conditions referred to in section 136 (1)  are that—

137.1.a

membership of the scheme is open to all developers,

137.1.b

the scheme enables qualifying complainants to have complaints against members
of the scheme investigated and determined by an independent individual, and

137.1.c

the scheme contains the provisions required by  Schedule 9 .

137.2

A “qualifying complainant” is a person who, at the time the complaint is made,
is a relevant owner of a home which, at that time, is a new build home.

137.3

The individual who is to investigate and determine complaints under the scheme
is to be known as “ the new homes ombudsman ”.

137.4

The scheme may also include provision for persons other than qualifying
complainants to have complaints against members of the scheme investigated and
determined under the scheme.

137.5

The scheme may provide that the new homes ombudsman is not required to
investigate a complaint if the new homes ombudsman is satisfied that the
complaint (or a complaint which is materially the same) is being, or has been,
dealt with under another redress scheme or in legal proceedings.

137.6

In this section, “ redress scheme ” means a scheme under which complaints may
be made to, and investigated and determined by, an independent person.

137.7

Schedule 9  contains further provision about the new homes ombudsman scheme.

137.8

Schedule 10  contains amendments connected with the establishment of the new
homes ombudsman scheme.

##### “Relevant owner”, “new build home” and “developer”

138

138.1

This section provides for the meaning of terms used in section 137 (and in
this section).

138.2

A person is a “relevant owner” of a home if the person—

138.2.a

is an individual,

138.2.b

has a relevant interest in land that includes the home, and

138.2.c

meets the occupation condition.

138.3

A person meets the occupation condition if the person—

138.3.a

occupies the home, or

138.3.b

is the landlord under a lease of land that includes the home granted for a
term not exceeding 21 years to another individual for that individual’s
occupation of the home.

138.4

In relation to a home in Scotland or Northern Ireland, subsection (3) has
effect as if in paragraph (b) the words “for a term not exceeding 21 years”
were omitted.

138.5

A home is a “new build home” if—

138.5.a

the home is, or is contained in—

138.5.a.i

a building the construction of which began after the coming into force of this
section, or

138.5.a.ii

a building that has been converted, or to which any other works have been
carried out, so that it consists of or contains the home, where the conversion
or works began after the coming into force of this section,

138.5.b

there is a person who is, or was, a developer in relation to the home, and

138.5.c

no more than two years have elapsed since the first acquisition, by any
person, of a relevant interest in land that includes the home from the person
mentioned in  paragraph (b) .

138.6

“ Relevant interest ” means—

138.6.a

in relation to land in England or Wales, a legal estate which is—

138.6.a.i

an estate in fee simple absolute in possession, or

138.6.a.ii

a term of years absolute granted for a term of more than 21 years from the
date of the grant;

138.6.b

in relation to land in Scotland, the interest of an owner of land;

138.6.c

in relation to land in Northern Ireland, a legal estate which is—

138.6.c.i

an estate in fee simple absolute in possession,

138.6.c.ii

an estate in fee simple in possession subject to a rent payable under a fee
farm grant, or

138.6.c.iii

a term of years absolute granted for a term of more than 21 years from the
date of the grant.

138.7

A “developer” is a person—

138.7.a

who undertakes or commissions—

138.7.a.i

the construction of a new building that is to consist of or contain a home,

138.7.a.ii

the conversion of, or carrying out of any other works to, an existing building
so that it consists of or contains a home, or

138.7.a.iii

the conversion of, or carrying out of any other works to, an existing building
so as to alter the number of homes contained in it,

with a view to granting, or disposing of, a relevant interest in land that
includes the home or, in a case falling within  sub-paragraph (iii) , any of
the homes, or

138.7.b

who is of a description specified in regulations made by the relevant national
authority.

138.8

Regulations under  subsection (7) (b)  may, among other things, specify a
description of persons by reference to a connection with a person mentioned in
subsection (7) (a) .

138.9

In  subsection (7) (b) , “ the relevant national authority ” means—

138.9.a

in relation to homes in England, the Secretary of State,

138.9.b

in relation to homes in Wales, the Welsh Ministers,

138.9.c

in relation to homes in Scotland, the Scottish Ministers, and

138.9.d

in relation to homes in Northern Ireland, the Northern Ireland department
designated for the purposes of this section by the First Minister and deputy
First Minister acting jointly.

138.10

Before making regulations under  subsection (7) (b) , the relevant national
authority must consult each other person who is the relevant national
authority in relation to regulations under that subsection.

138.11

If no Northern Ireland department has been designated for the purposes of this
section then, for the purposes of subsection  (10) , “ the relevant national
authority ” in relation to homes in Northern Ireland is the Executive Office
in Northern Ireland.

138.12

“ Home ” means a private residence.

138.13

“ Occupies ” means occupies as a private residence (and “ occupation ” is to
be construed accordingly).

##### Regulations under section 138

139

139.1

The power to make regulations under section 138(7) (b)  is exercisable—

139.1.a

in the case of regulations made by the Secretary of State or the Welsh
Ministers, by statutory instrument, and

139.1.b

in the case of regulations made by a Northern Ireland department, by statutory
rule for the purposes of the Statutory Rules (Northern Ireland) Order 1979 (
S.I. 1979/1573 (N.I. 12)) .

(For regulations under section 138(7) (b)  made by the Scottish Ministers, see
section 27 of the  Interpretation and Legislative Reform (Scotland) Act 2010
(asp 10) ).

139.2

Regulations under section 138(7) (b) —

139.2.a

may make different provision for different purposes;

139.2.b

may contain consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional or saving
provision.

139.3

Regulations under section 138(7) (b) —

139.3.a

if made by the Secretary of State, may not be made unless a draft of the
statutory instrument containing them has been laid before, and approved by a
resolution of, each House of Parliament;

139.3.b

if made by the Welsh Ministers, may not be made unless a draft of the
statutory instrument containing them has been laid before, and approved by a
resolution of, Senedd Cymru;

139.3.c

if made by the Scottish Ministers, are subject to the affirmative procedure
(see section 29 of the  Interpretation and Legislative Reform (Scotland) Act
2010 (asp 10) );

139.3.d

if made by a Northern Ireland department, may not be made unless a draft of
the regulations has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, the
Northern Ireland Assembly.

##### Power to require persons to join scheme and to provide information

140

140.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

140.1.a

require persons who are developers, or developers of a specified description,
to become members of the new homes ombudsman scheme;

140.1.b

require persons who are required to become members of the scheme under
paragraph (a)  to remain members of the scheme for a period specified in the
regulations (even if they are no longer developers);

140.1.c

require members of the scheme to inform persons of a specified description of
the scheme;

140.1.d

make provision for civil sanctions to be imposed in respect of a breach of a
requirement imposed by regulations under  paragraph (a) ,  (b)  or  (c) ;

140.1.e

make provision for the investigation of suspected breaches of such a
requirement.

In  this subsection , “ developer ” has the meaning given in section 138 and “
specified ” means specified in the regulations.

140.2

Before making regulations under subsection (1), the Secretary of State must
consult—

140.2.a

the Welsh Ministers,

140.2.b

the Scottish Ministers, and

140.2.c

the relevant Northern Ireland department.

140.3

Provision made by virtue of  subsection (1) (a)  may provide for exceptions to
the requirement to become a member of the scheme.

140.4

Provision made by virtue of  subsection (1) (a)  or  (b)  may require persons
who are members of the new homes ombudsman scheme to—

140.4.a

obtain a certificate confirming their membership of the scheme;

140.4.b

display or publish the certificate in accordance with the regulations;

140.4.c

produce a copy of the certificate, on request, in accordance with the
regulations.

140.5

Provision made for the imposition of a civil sanction by virtue of  subsection
(1) (d)  must include—

140.5.a

provision for appeals to a court or tribunal against the imposition of the
sanction, and

140.5.b

such other provision as the Secretary of State considers appropriate for
safeguarding the interests of persons on whom the sanction may be imposed.

140.6

Provision made by virtue of  subsection (1) (d)  or  (e)  may—

140.6.a

confer functions on a person (including functions involving the exercise of a
discretion);

140.6.b

require a person on whom functions are so conferred to have regard to any
relevant guidance issued by the Secretary of State relating to the exercise of
those functions.

140.7

The Secretary of State may make payments to a person on whom functions are
conferred by virtue of  subsection (6) .

140.8

In this section, “ the relevant Northern Ireland department ” means—

140.8.a

the Northern Ireland department designated for the purposes of this section by
the First Minister and deputy First Minister acting jointly, or

140.8.b

failing such a designation, the Executive Office in Northern Ireland.

##### Register of members

141

141.1

The person who maintains the new homes ombudsman scheme must keep a register
of persons who are members of the scheme.

141.2

The register must be made available for inspection by members of the public at
all reasonable times.

##### Developers’ code of practice

142

142.1

The Secretary of State may issue or approve a code of practice about the

142.2

The Secretary of State may from time to time revise or replace the code or
approve its revision or replacement.

142.3
