published.

142.4

The Secretary of State must consult the Welsh Ministers, the Scottish
Ministers and the relevant Northern Ireland department before—

142.4.a

issuing, revising or replacing the code, or

142.4.b

approving the code or a revision or replacement of it.

142.5

In this section, “ the relevant Northern Ireland department ” means—

142.5.a

the Northern Ireland department designated for the purposes of this section by
the First Minister and deputy First Minister acting jointly, or

142.5.b

failing such a designation, the Executive Office in Northern Ireland.

##### Amendment of the Government of Wales Act 2006

143

In Schedule 7B to the Government of Wales Act 2006 (general restrictions on
legislative competence of Senedd Cymru), in paragraph 10(2), at the end
insert—

143.o

the new homes ombudsman.

#### New build home warranties

##### New build home warranties

144

144.1

This section applies where a person (“the developer”) carries out a
development in England that results in the creation of one or more dwellings
(“new build homes”).

144.2

The developer must, at the time of or before granting or disposing of a
relevant interest in a new build home—

144.2.a

provide to the purchaser a new build home warranty for the new build home, and

144.2.b

provide to a prescribed person a new build home warranty for any common parts.

144.3

A “new build home warranty” for a thing is an arrangement, satisfying any
requirements under subsection (4), under which—

144.3.a

the developer agrees, in specified circumstances, to remedy any specified
defect (or any defect) in the thing occurring in a specified period, and

144.3.b

a prescribed person obtains the benefit of a policy of insurance relating to
specified defects (or any defects) in the thing.

“Specified” here means specified in the arrangement.

144.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations impose requirements about new build
home warranties, including in particular requirements as to—

144.4.a

the kinds of defect which the developer must agree to remedy;

144.4.b

the circumstances in which the developer must agree to remedy a defect
(including the minimum duration of the period mentioned in subsection  (3) (a)
);

144.4.c

the developer agreeing to meet prescribed costs incurred by a person occupying
a new build home, where works to remedy a defect are carried out;

144.4.d

the policy of insurance (including risks that must be covered, the minimum
amount of cover, the minimum duration of the period of cover, and the maximum
amount of any excess);

144.4.e

the solvency of the insurer or underwriter;

144.4.f

the standard of service provided by or on behalf of the insurer in relation to
the policy;

144.4.g

the ability of a person who has the benefit of the warranty to transfer that
benefit to another person.

144.5

The regulations must provide that the period of cover under the policy of
insurance must be at least 15 years beginning with the day on which the
relevant interest is granted or disposed of.

144.6

In this section—

“ carries out a development ”: the reference to a person carrying out a
development is to undertaking or commissioning— the construction of a
building, or the conversion of, or carrying out of any other works to, a
building, with a view to granting, or disposing of, relevant interests in one
or more dwellings created as a result of the construction, conversion or
carrying out of works; “ common parts ”, in relation to a new build home,
means any part of a building, where— that part is provided for the use,
benefit and enjoyment of the residents of the new build home and the residents
of other dwellings (whether alone or with other persons), and the right to use
that part is conferred in connection with the grant or disposal of the
relevant interest in the new build home; “ defect ”: any reference to a defect
includes, in relation to land, contamination; “ prescribed ” means prescribed
by regulations made by the Secretary of State; “ purchaser ” means the person
to whom the relevant interest is granted or disposed of; “ relevant interest ”
means a legal estate which is— an estate in fee simple absolute in possession,
or a term of years absolute granted for a term of more than 21 years from the
date of the grant.

##### New build home warranties: financial penalties

145

145.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for and in connection
with the imposition of a financial penalty in cases where the Secretary of
State, or a person designated by the Secretary of State, is satisfied beyond
reasonable doubt that a person has, without reasonable excuse, failed to
comply with section 144 (2) .

145.2

The regulations may include provision—

145.2.a

about the procedure to be followed in imposing penalties;

145.2.b

about the amount of penalties;

145.2.c

for the imposition of interest or additional penalties for late payment;

145.2.d

conferring rights of appeal against penalties.

145.3

The regulations must provide that the amount of a financial penalty (excluding
interest or any additional penalty) may not exceed the greater of—

145.3.a

10% of the value of the relevant interest at the time the person granted or
disposed of the relevant interest, and

145.3.b

£10,000.

#### Construction products

##### Construction products

146

Schedule 11  contains provision for regulations relating to construction
products.

#### Liability relating to construction products

##### Liability relating to construction products: general definitions

147

In this section, section 148 and section 149—

“ the 1991 Regulations ” means the Construction Products Regulations 1991 (
S.I. 1991/1620 ); “ the 2011 Regulation ” means  Regulation (EU) No. 305/2011
(regulation laying down harmonised conditions for the marketing of
construction products); “ the 2019 Regulations ” means the Construction
Products (Amendment etc.) (EU Exit) Regulations 2019 ( S.I. 2019/465 ); “
construction products regulations ” means regulations under paragraph  1  of
Schedule 11 ; “ construction product requirement ” means a requirement under—
construction products regulations, the 2011 Regulation, or the 2019
Regulations; “ relevant building ” means— a building which consists of a
dwelling, or a building which contains two or more dwellings; “ relevant
interest ”, in relation to a building in England and Wales, means— in a case
where the building consists of a dwelling, a legal or equitable interest in
the building, and in a case where the building contains one or more dwellings,
a legal or equitable interest in— the building, or any dwelling contained in
the building; “ relevant interest ”, in relation to a building in Scotland,
means— in a case where the building consists of a dwelling, any right or
interest (including a servitude or heritable security) in or over the
building, and in a case where the building contains one or more dwellings, any
right or interest (including a servitude or heritable security) in or over—
the building, or any dwelling contained in the building; “ requirement ”
includes a prohibition or restriction.

##### Liability relating to construction products

148

148.1

This section applies where Conditions A to D are met.

148.2

Condition A is that, at any time after the coming into force of this section—

148.2.a

a person fails to comply with a construction product requirement in relation
to a construction product,

148.2.b

a person who markets or supplies a construction product makes a misleading
statement in relation to it, or

148.2.c

a person manufactures a construction product that is inherently defective.

148.3

Condition B is that, after Condition A is met, the construction product
referred to in subsection  (2) (a) ,  (b)  or  (c)  is installed in, or
applied or attached to, a relevant building in the course of works carried out
in the construction of, or otherwise in relation to, the building.

148.4

Condition C is that, when those works are completed—

148.4.a

in a case where the relevant building consists of a dwelling, the building is
unfit for habitation, or

148.4.b

in a case where the relevant building contains one or more dwellings, a
dwelling contained in the building is unfit for habitation.

148.5

Condition D is that the facts referred to in subsection  (2) (a) ,  (b)  or
(c)  were the cause, or one of the causes, of the building or dwelling being
unfit for habitation.

148.6

The person referred to in subsection  (2) (a) ,  (b)  or  (c)  is liable to
pay damages to a person with a relevant interest in relation to the relevant
building for personal injury, damage to property or economic loss suffered by
that person as a result of the facts referred to in subsection  (4) (a)  or
(b) .

148.7

A term of an agreement which purports to exclude or restrict, or has the
effect of excluding or restricting, any liability arising under this section
is void.

148.8

For the purposes of section 10B(1) of the Limitation Act 1980 and section
18ZD(1) of the Prescription and Limitation (Scotland) Act 1973, the right of
action that a person has by virtue of this section is to be regarded as having
accrued—

148.8.a

in a case where the works referred to in subsection  (3)  are carried out in
the construction of the relevant building, when the construction is completed,
and

148.8.b

in any other case, when the works are completed.

148.9

In subsection  (2) (a)  “construction product”—

148.9.a

in relation to a construction product requirement under construction products
regulations, has the meaning specified in those regulations;

148.9.b

in relation to a construction product requirement under the 2011 Regulation,
has the meaning specified in the 2011 Regulation;

148.9.c

in relation to a construction product requirement under the 2019 Regulations,
has the meaning specified in the 2011 Regulation as it had effect immediately
before IP completion day.

148.10

In subsection  (2) (b)  and  (c)  “ construction product ” has the meaning
specified in the 2011 Regulation.

##### Liability for past defaults relating to cladding products

149

149.1

This section applies where Conditions A to D are met.

149.2

Condition A is that, at any time before the coming into force of this section—

149.2.a

a person fails to comply with a cladding product requirement in relation to a
cladding product,

149.2.b

a person who markets or supplies a cladding product makes a misleading
statement in relation to it, or

149.2.c

a person manufactures a cladding product that is inherently defective.

149.3

Condition B is that, after Condition A has been met, the cladding product is
attached to, or included in, the external wall of a relevant building in the
course of works carried out in the construction of, or otherwise in relation
to, the building.

149.4

Condition C is that, when those works are completed—

149.4.a

in a case where the relevant building consists of a dwelling, the building is
unfit for habitation, or

149.4.b

in a case where the relevant building contains one or more dwellings, a
dwelling contained in the building is unfit for habitation.

149.5

Condition D is that the facts referred to in subsection (2)(a), (b) or (c)
were the cause, or one of the causes, of the building or dwelling being unfit
for habitation.

149.6

The person referred to in subsection (2)(a), (b) or (c) is liable to pay
damages to a person with a relevant interest in relation to the relevant
building for personal injury, damage to property or economic loss suffered by
that person as a result of the facts referred to in subsection (4)(a) or (b).

149.7

A term of an agreement which purports to exclude or restrict, or has the
effect of excluding or restricting, any liability arising under this section
is void.

149.8

For the purposes of section 10B(2) of the Limitation Act 1980 and section
18ZD(2) of the Prescription and Limitation (Scotland) Act 1973, the right of
action that a person has by virtue of this section is to be regarded as having
accrued—

149.8.a

in a case where the works referred to in subsection (3) are carried out in the
construction of the relevant building, when the construction is completed, and

149.8.b

in any other case, when the works are completed.

149.9

Where an action is brought under this section in England and Wales that, but
for section 10B(2) of the Limitation Act 1980, would have been barred by that
Act, a court hearing the action must dismiss it in relation to any defendant
if satisfied that it is necessary to do so to avoid a breach of that
defendant’s Convention rights.

149.10

Where an action is brought under this section in Scotland that, but for
section 18ZD(2) of the Prescription and Limitation (Scotland) Act 1973, would
have been barred by that Act, a court hearing the action must dismiss it in
relation to any defender if satisfied that it is necessary to do so to avoid a
breach of that defender’s Convention rights.

149.11

In this section “ cladding product requirement ” means—

149.11.a

in relation to a time before IP completion day, a requirement relating to a
cladding product under—

149.11.a.i

the 1991 Regulations, or

149.11.a.ii

the 2011 Regulation as it had effect in EU law at that time, and

149.11.b

in relation to a time after IP completion day, a requirement relating to a
cladding product under—

149.11.b.i

the 2011 Regulation, or

149.11.b.ii

the 2019 Regulations.

149.12

In this section—

“ cladding product ” means a cladding system or any component of a cladding
system; “ Convention rights ” has the same meaning as in the Human Rights Act
1998; “ external wall ”, in relation to a building, includes any part of a
roof pitched at an angle of more than 70 degrees to the horizontal if that
part of the roof adjoins a space within the building to which persons have
access otherwise than for the purpose of carrying out repairs or maintenance.

##### Liability relating to construction products: limitation in England and Wales

150

In the Limitation Act 1980, after section 10A insert—

######### Special time limit for actions relating to construction products

150.10B

150.10B.1

An action under section 148 of the Building Safety Act 2022 shall not be
brought after the expiration of 15 years from the date on which the right of
action accrued.

150.10B.2

An action under section 149 of the Building Safety Act 2022 shall not be
brought after—

150.10B.2.a

if the right of action accrued before the commencement date, the expiration of
the period of 30 years from the date on which it accrued, and

150.10B.2.b

if the right of action accrued on or after the commencement date, the
expiration of the period of 15 years beginning with the date on which it
accrued.

150.10B.3

In a case where—

150.10B.3.a

a right of action under section 149 of the Building Safety Act 2022 accrued
before the commencement date, and

150.10B.3.b

the expiration of the period of 30 years beginning with the date on which the
right of action accrued falls in the year beginning with the commencement
date,

subsection (2)(a) has effect as if it referred to the expiration of that year.

150.10B.4

In subsections (2) and (3) “the commencement date” is the day on which section
149 of the Building Safety Act 2022 came into force.

150.10B.5

No other period of limitation prescribed by Part 1 of this Act applies in
relation to an action referred to in subsections (1) and (2).

150.10B.6

Sections 28, 32 and 35 of this Act apply in relation to an action referred to
subsections (1) and (2), but otherwise Parts 2 and 3 of this Act (except
sections 37 and 38) do not apply for the purposes of this section.

##### Liability relating to construction products: limitation in Scotland

151

151.1

The Prescription and Limitation (Scotland) Act 1973 is amended as follows.

151.2

After section 18ZC insert—

########### Actions relating to construction products

151.2.18ZD

151.2.18ZD.1

An action under section 148 of the Building Safety Act 2022 may not be brought
after the expiration of 15 years from the date on which the right of action
accrued (see subsection (8) of that section).

151.2.18ZD.2

An action under section 149 of the Building Safety Act 2022 may not be brought
after—

151.2.18ZD.2.a

if the right of action accrued before the commencement date, the expiration of

151.2.18ZD.2.b

if the right of action accrued on or after the commencement date, the

151.2.18ZD.3.b

the expiration of the period of 30 years beginning with the date on which the

date,

subsection (2)(a) has effect as if it referred to the expiration of that year.

relation to an action referred to in subsection (1) or (2).

151.2.18ZD.6

there is to be disregarded any time during which the person seeking to bring
the action (P)—

151.2.18ZD.6.a

was under a legal disability by reason of nonage or unsoundness of mind, or

151.2.18ZD.6.b

failed to bring the action by reason of—

151.2.18ZD.6.b.i

fraud on the part of the person against whom the action is to be brought (D)
or the part of any person acting on D’s behalf, or

151.2.18ZD.6.b.ii

after P could with reasonable diligence have discovered the fraud or error
mentioned in that paragraph).

151.2.18ZD.7

person acting on D’s behalf, intended the fraud or the words or conduct to
cause P to fail to bring the action.

#### Construction products: costs contribution orders

##### Costs contribution orders: general definitions

152

In this section and sections 153 to 155—

“ the 2011 Regulation ” means  Regulation (EU) No. 305/2011  (regulation
laying down harmonised conditions for the marketing of construction products);
“ the 2019 Regulations ” means the Construction Products (Amendment etc.) (EU
Exit) Regulations 2019 ( S.I. 2019/465 ); “ the 2020 Regulations ” means the
Construction Products (Amendment etc.) (EU Exit) Regulations 2020 ( S.I.
2020/1359 ); “ construction product ”— in relation to a construction product
requirement under construction products regulations, has the meaning specified
in those regulations; in relation to a construction product requirement under
the 2011 Regulation, has the meaning specified in the 2011 Regulation (or, in
Northern Ireland, in the 2011 Regulation as having effect in EU law from time
to time); in relation to a construction product requirement under the 2019
Regulations, has the meaning specified in the 2011 Regulation as it had effect
immediately before IP completion day; in relation to a construction product
requirement under the 2020 Regulations, has the meaning given by regulation 2
of those Regulations; “ construction products regulations ” means regulations
under paragraph 1 of  Schedule 11 ; “ construction product requirement ”, in
England and Wales or Scotland, means a requirement under— construction
products regulations, the 2011 Regulation, or the 2019 Regulations; “
construction product requirement ”, in Northern Ireland, means a requirement
under— construction product regulations, the 2011 Regulation as having effect
from time to time in EU law, the 2019 Regulations, or the 2020 Regulations;
references to an “interest” in a building or dwelling include— in England and
Wales, any legal or equitable interest in the building or dwelling; in
Scotland, any right or interest (including a servitude or heritable security)
in or over the building or dwelling; in Northern Ireland, any estate within
the meaning given by section 45(2) of the Interpretation Act (Northern
Ireland) 1954 in the building or dwelling; “ relevant building ” means— a
building which consists of a dwelling, or a building which contains two or
more dwellings; “ requirement ” includes a prohibition or restriction.

##### Costs contribution orders made by courts

153

153.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for courts to make
costs contribution orders on the application of the Secretary of State.

153.2

The regulations may only make provision for the making of costs contribution
orders under this section in cases where—

153.2.a

Conditions A to D are met, and

153.2.b

any prescribed conditions are met.

153.3

Condition A is that a person (“ the defaulter ”) is convicted of an offence
consisting of a failure to comply with a construction product requirement in
relation to a construction product.

153.4

Condition B is that, after the failure to comply referred to in subsection
(3), the construction product is installed in, or applied or attached to, a
relevant building in the course of works carried out in the construction of,
or otherwise in relation to, the building.

153.5

Condition C is that, when those works are completed—

153.5.a

in a case where the relevant building consists of a dwelling, the building is
unfit for habitation, or

153.5.b

in a case where the relevant building contains one or more dwellings, a
dwelling contained in the building is unfit for habitation.

153.6

Condition D is that the failure to comply referred to in subsection (3) was
the cause, or one of the causes, of the building or dwelling being unfit for
habitation.

153.7

A “costs contribution order” under this section is an order requiring the
defaulter to pay an amount to a person with a prescribed interest in the
building or any dwelling contained in the building.

153.8

Regulations under this section must provide for the amount to be paid to a
person under a costs contribution order under this section to be such amount
as the court making the order considers just and equitable in respect of the
costs that the person has reasonably incurred, or in the view of the court is
likely to reasonably incur, in respect of works to make the building or
dwelling fit for habitation.

153.9

The regulations may make provision as to the matters which may or must be
taken into account by a court in determining—

153.9.a

whether, against whom and in favour of whom to make a costs contribution order
under this section;

153.9.b

the amount required to be paid by a person under a costs contribution order
under this section.

153.10

The regulations may make provision in relation to—

153.10.a

enforcement of a costs contribution order under this section;

153.10.b

court powers to order the defaulter to pay—

153.10.b.i

any costs incurred by the Secretary of State under regulations under section
155 (assessments) in respect of the application, and

153.10.b.ii

any costs incurred by the Secretary of State in making the application.

153.11

The regulations may make provision about how a costs contribution order under
this section relates to other remedies, including in particular—

153.11.a

provision to secure that, taking a costs contribution order under this section
together with other remedies—

153.11.a.i

a person does not incur liability more than once in respect of the same costs;

153.11.a.ii

a person is not entitled to be reimbursed more than once for the same costs;

153.11.b

provision preventing a person to whom any amount is payable under a costs
contribution order under this section from pursuing any other legal remedy for
the recovery of such an amount.

153.12

In this section “ prescribed ” means prescribed by regulations under this
section.

##### Costs contribution orders made by the Secretary of State

154

154.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for the Secretary of
State to make costs contribution orders.

154.2

The regulations may only make provision for the making of costs contribution
orders in cases where—

154.2.a

Conditions A to D are met, and

154.2.b

any prescribed conditions are met.

154.3

Condition A is that a person (“ the defaulter ”) is convicted of an offence
consisting of a failure to comply with a construction product requirement in
relation to a construction product.

154.4

Condition B is that, after the failure to comply referred to in subsection
(3), the construction product is installed in, or applied or attached to, a
relevant building in the course of works carried out in the construction of,
or otherwise in relation to, the building.

154.5

Condition C is that, when those works are completed—

154.5.a

in a case where the relevant building consists of a dwelling, the building is
unfit for habitation, or

154.5.b

in a case where the relevant building contains one or more dwellings, a
dwelling contained in the building is unfit for habitation.

154.6

Condition D is that the failure to comply referred to in subsection (3) was
the cause, or one of the causes, of the building or dwelling being unfit for
habitation.

154.7

A “costs contribution order” under this section is an order requiring the
defaulter to make a payment to a person with a prescribed interest in the
building or any dwelling contained in the building.

154.8

Regulations under this section must provide for the amount to be paid to a
person under a costs contribution order under this section to be such amount
as the Secretary of State considers just and equitable in respect of the costs
that the person has reasonably incurred, or in the view of the Secretary of
State is likely to reasonably incur, in respect of works to make the building
or dwelling fit for habitation.

154.9

The regulations may make provision as to the matters which may or must be
taken into account by the Secretary of State in determining—

154.9.a

whether, against whom, and in favour of whom, to make a costs contribution
order under this section;

154.9.b

the amount required to be paid by a person under a costs contribution order
under this section.

154.10

The regulations may make provision for the Secretary of State to issue a
warning notice to a person before determining whether to make a costs
contribution order under this section against that person.

154.11

The regulations may make provision requiring that a costs contribution order
under this section—

154.11.a

be made in a prescribed form;

154.11.b

contain prescribed information.

154.12

The regulations may make provision about service of a costs contribution order
under this section including—

154.12.a

how an order is to be served;

154.12.b

when an order is to be taken as having been served;

154.12.c

the persons on whom an order must be served.

154.13

The regulations may make provision in relation to—

154.13.a

enforcement of a costs contribution order made under this section (including
enforcement by the Secretary of State);

154.13.b

powers of the Secretary of State to order the defaulter to pay any costs
incurred by the Secretary of State under section 155 in respect of a costs
contribution order under this section.

154.14

The regulations may make provision about how a costs contribution order under
this section relates to other remedies, including in particular—

154.14.a

provision to secure that, taking a costs contribution order under this section
together with other remedies—

154.14.a.i

a person does not incur liability more than once in respect of the same costs;

154.14.a.ii

a person is not entitled to be reimbursed more than once for the same costs;

154.14.b

provision preventing a person to whom any amount is payable under a costs
contribution order under this section from pursuing any other legal remedy for
the recovery of such an amount.

154.15

The regulations may make provision for persons to apply to the Secretary of
State for a review of a costs contribution order under this section.

154.16

The regulations may make provision for appeals to a court or tribunal in
relation to—

154.16.a

a decision of the Secretary of State to make or not make a costs contribution
order under this section;

154.16.b

a refusal by the Secretary of State to review a costs contribution order under
this section;

154.16.c

the outcome of a review by the Secretary of State of a costs contribution
order under this section.

154.17

The regulations may in particular include provision suspending a requirement
to pay an amount due under a costs contribution order under this section
pending the determination or withdrawal of an appeal or the determination of a
review.

154.18

In this section “ prescribed ” means prescribed by regulations under this
section.

##### Costs contribution orders: assessments

155

155.1

For the purposes of sections 153 and 154, the Secretary of State may by
regulations make provision for the Secretary of State to appoint persons to
assess—

155.1.a

whether the conditions for the imposition of a costs contribution order under
either of those sections are met;

155.1.b

the works required to make a building or dwelling fit for habitation;

155.1.c

what interest a person has in a building or dwelling;

155.1.d

the costs that a person has reasonably incurred or is likely to reasonably
incur in respect of works referred to in paragraph (b);

155.1.e

the amount that a person should be required to pay under a costs contribution
order.

155.2

The regulations may include provision about the criteria to be met by a person
before they may be appointed as an assessor.

155.3

The regulations may make provision about assessments, including provision—

155.3.a

conferring power on an assessor to require that persons provide such
information as the assessor may reasonably require for the purposes of an
assessment;

155.3.b

for the provision of information by an assessor to the Secretary of State
(including any information provided under paragraph (a)).

155.4

Regulations under subsection (3)(a) may include provision for criminal
offences relating to a failure to provide information, or to the provision of
false or misleading information.

155.5

Regulations under subsection (3)(a) creating a criminal offence must have the
effect that—

155.5.a

the offence is—

155.5.a.i

triable summarily only, or

155.5.a.ii

triable summarily or on indictment,

155.5.b

the offence is punishable only—

155.5.b.i

with a fine, or

155.5.b.ii

with a term of imprisonment or a fine (or both),

155.5.c

where the offence is triable summarily only, any fine with which the offence
is punishable in Scotland or Northern Ireland does not exceed level 5 on the
standard scale,

155.5.d

where the offence is triable summarily or on indictment, any fine with which
the offence is punishable on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern
Ireland does not exceed the statutory maximum, and

155.5.e

any term of imprisonment with which the offence is punishable on summary
conviction does not exceed—

155.5.e.i

in England and Wales, the relevant period,

155.5.e.ii

in Scotland, 12 months, and

155.5.e.iii

in Northern Ireland, 6 months.

155.6

In subsection (5)(e)(i), “ the relevant period ” means—

155.6.a

in relation to an offence that is triable summarily only—

155.6.a.i

where the offence is committed before the coming into force of section 281 of
the Criminal Justice Act 2003, 6 months, and

155.6.a.ii

where the offence is committed after that time, 51 weeks;

155.6.b

in relation to an offence that is triable summarily or on indictment—

155.6.b.i

where the offence is committed before the coming into force of paragraph 24(2)
of Schedule 22 to the Sentencing Act 2020, 6 months, and

155.6.b.ii

where the offence is committed after that time, 12 months.

155.7

Regulations under subsection (3)(b) may make provision for the purpose of
securing that there is (taking into account any power or duty to provide
information under the regulations) no contravention of the data protection
legislation.

155.8

In subsection (7), “ data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in
the Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act).

#### Fire safety

##### Amendment of Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order 2005

156

156.1

The Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order 2005 ( S.I. 2005/1541 ) is amended
as follows.

156.2

In article 5 (duties under the Order), for “22”, in each place it occurs,
substitute  “22B” .

156.3

In article 9 (risk assessment)—

156.3.a

in paragraph (6) for the words from “record” to the end substitute  “make a
record of the assessment or review, which must in particular include the
information prescribed by paragraph (7).” ;

156.3.b

in paragraph (7)(a) omit “significant”.

156.4

After article 9 insert—

########### Risk assessment: assistance

156.4.9A

156.4.9A.1

The responsible person must not appoint a person to assist them with making or
reviewing an assessment under article 9 unless that person is competent.

156.4.9A.2

A person is to be regarded as competent for the purposes of this article where
the person has sufficient training and experience or knowledge and other
qualities to enable the person properly to assist in making or reviewing the
assessment.

156.4.9A.3

Where the responsible person appoints more than one person, the responsible
person must make arrangements for ensuring adequate co-operation between them.

156.5

In article 11(2) (fire safety arrangements) omit the words from “where” to the
end.

156.6

After article 21 insert—

########### Provision of information to residents of domestic premises

156.6.21A

156.6.21A.1

This article applies in relation to a building containing two or more sets of
domestic premises.

156.6.21A.2

The responsible person must give residents of the domestic premises
comprehensible and relevant information about the relevant fire safety
matters.

156.6.21A.3

The relevant fire safety matters are—

156.6.21A.3.a

the risks to residents of the domestic premises identified by the risk
assessment;

156.6.21A.3.b

the preventive and protective measures;

156.6.21A.3.c

the name of the responsible person and an address in the United Kingdom at
which the responsible person, or someone acting on their behalf, will accept
notices and other documents;

156.6.21A.3.d

the identity of any person appointed by the responsible person to assist them
with making or reviewing an assessment under article 9;

156.6.21A.3.e

the identity of any persons nominated by the responsible person under article
13(3)(b);

156.6.21A.3.f

any risks of which the responsible person has been informed under article
22(1)(c);

156.6.21A.3.g

any other matters specified in regulations made by the relevant authority.

156.6.21A.4

The information is to be provided at such times, and in such form, as may be
specified in regulations made by the relevant authority.

156.6.21A.5

The responsible person must keep records of the relevant fire safety matters.

156.6.21A.6

The “relevant authority”—

156.6.21A.6.a

in relation to premises in England, means the Secretary of State;

156.6.21A.6.b

in relation to premises in Wales, means the Welsh Ministers.

156.6.21A.7

Regulations under this article are to be made by statutory instrument.

156.6.21A.8

A statutory instrument containing regulations made by the Secretary of State
under this article is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of
either House of Parliament.

156.6.21A.9

A statutory instrument containing regulations made by the Welsh Ministers
under this article is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of
Senedd Cymru.

156.7

In article 22 (co-operation and co-ordination)—

156.7.a

in the heading, at the end insert  “between responsible persons” ;

156.7.b

before paragraph (1) insert—

156.7.b.A1

A person who is a responsible person in relation to any premises must take
such steps as are reasonably practicable to ascertain whether any other
responsible person shares, or has duties in respect of, the premises.

;

156.7.c

in paragraph (1) before sub-paragraph (1)(a) insert—

156.7.c.za

inform the other responsible persons concerned of that person’s name and an
address in the United Kingdom at which that person, or someone acting on their
behalf, will accept notices and other documents;

156.7.c.zb

inform the other responsible persons concerned of the part of the premises for
which that person considers themselves to be a responsible person, and keep a
record of that information;

.

156.8

After article 22 insert—

########### Provision of information to new responsible person

156.8.22A

156.8.22A.1

Paragraph  (2)  applies where a person (the “outgoing person”) ceases to be a
responsible person for premises and another person (the “new responsible
person”) becomes a responsible person for the premises in place of the
outgoing person.

156.8.22A.2

The outgoing person must give the new responsible person any relevant fire
safety information held by the outgoing person.

156.8.22A.3

“ Relevant fire safety information ” means—

156.8.22A.3.a

records kept under article 9(6) of assessments and reviews under article 9;

156.8.22A.3.b

the identity of any person appointed by the responsible person to assist them
with making or reviewing an assessment under article 9;

156.8.22A.3.c

the name of any other person who is a responsible person in relation to the
premises and an address in the United Kingdom at which that person, or someone
acting on their behalf, will accept notices and other documents (where known);

156.8.22A.3.d

where the premises consist of or include a higher-risk building, the identity
of any other person who is an accountable person in relation to the premises
(where known);

156.8.22A.3.e

any information given under regulation 38 of the Building Regulations 2010 (
S.I. 2010/2214 ) (fire safety information);

156.8.22A.3.f

any other matters specified in regulations made by the relevant authority.

156.8.22A.4

The information is to be provided at such times, and in such form, as may be
specified in regulations made by the relevant authority.

156.8.22A.5

A responsible person must keep records of relevant fire safety information.

156.8.22A.6

In this article—

“ accountable person ” has the meaning given by section 72 of the Building
Safety Act 2022; “ higher-risk building ” has the meaning given by section 65
of that Act; “ relevant authority ”— in relation to premises in England, means
the Secretary of State; in relation to premises in Wales, means the Welsh
Ministers.

156.8.22A.7

Regulations under this article are to be made by statutory instrument.

156.8.22A.8

A statutory instrument containing regulations made by the Secretary of State
under this article is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of
either House of Parliament.

156.8.22A.9

A statutory instrument containing regulations made by the Welsh Ministers
under this article is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of
Senedd Cymru.

########### Co-operation with accountable persons

156.8.22B

156.8.22B.1

This article applies in relation to premises which consist of or include a
residential unit in a higher-risk building.

156.8.22B.2

The responsible person (“ P ”) must take such steps as are reasonably
practicable to ascertain whether there are one or more other persons who are
accountable persons in relation to the premises.

156.8.22B.3

If there are, P must co-operate with each accountable person for the purpose
of the accountable person carrying out their duties under the Building Safety
Act 2022.

156.8.22B.4

In this article—

“ accountable person ” has the meaning given by section 72 of the Building
Safety Act 2022; “ higher-risk building ” has the meaning given by section 65
of that Act; “ residential unit ” has the meaning given by section 115 of that
Act.

156.9

In article 29(5) (alterations notices), omit paragraphs (b) and (c).

156.10

In article 32 (offences)—

156.10.a

in paragraph (1)(a) for “22” substitute  “22B” ;

156.10.b

in paragraph (4) omit “not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale”;

156.10.c

in paragraph (7) omit “not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale”.

156.11

In article 50 (guidance)—

156.11.a

in paragraph (1) for “22” substitute  “22B” ;

156.11.b

in paragraph (1A)—

156.11.b.i

for “22” substitute  “22B” ;

156.11.b.ii

omit “in relation to a relevant building (or part of the building)”;

156.11.b.iii

in sub-paragraph (a) omit “risk based”;

156.11.b.iv

in sub-paragraph (b) omit “risk based”.

#### Architects

##### Architects: discipline and continuing professional development

157

157.1

The Architects Act 1997 is amended as follows.

157.2

In section 3 (the register), after  subsection (2)  insert—

157.2.2A

The Register shall show disciplinary orders made in relation to a registered
person for such period as may be prescribed.

157.3

In section 9 (competence to practise)—

157.3.a

in  subsection (1) , in the words after  paragraph (c) , after “practical
experience” insert  “or undertaken such recent training” ,

157.3.b

after  subsection (1)  insert—

157.3.b.1A

Before prescribing recent practical experience or training for the purposes of
subsection (1), the Board shall consult the bodies representative of
architects which are incorporated by royal charter and such other professional
and educational bodies as it thinks appropriate.

, and

157.3.c

after  subsection (2)  insert—

157.3.c.3

Where the Board decides that the name of a person to whom paragraph (b) of
subsection (1) applies is by virtue of that subsection to be removed from Part
1 of the Register—

157.3.c.3.a

the person shall be entitled to apply to the Board within a prescribed period
for an extension of time to gain the prescribed experience or undertake the
prescribed training or to otherwise satisfy the Board of the person’s
competence to practise, and

157.3.c.3.b

the Board shall not remove the name of the person from the Register unless—

157.3.c.3.b.i

the person has not made an application for an extension of time within the
prescribed period,

157.3.c.3.b.ii

an extension of time granted by the Board has expired and the Board is not
satisfied that the person has gained the prescribed experience or undertaken
the prescribed training or is otherwise competent to practise, or

157.3.c.3.b.iii

the Board has decided not to grant an extension of time in respect of an
application made by the person.

157.3.c.4

For the purposes of this section, a person is competent to practise if the
person has the skills, knowledge, experience and behaviours required for a
person to practise as an architect.

### General

#### Liability of officers of body corporate etc

161

161.1

Where an offence under  Part 2  or  4  committed by a body corporate—

161.1.a

is committed with the consent or connivance of any director, manager,
secretary or other similar officer of the body corporate, or any person who
was purporting to act in any such capacity, or

161.1.b

is attributable to any neglect on the part of any such person,

that person as well as the body corporate commits the offence and is liable to
be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

161.2

In  subsection (1)  “ director ”, in relation to a body corporate whose
affairs are managed by its members, means a member of the body corporate.

161.3

Subsection (1)  also applies in relation to a body that is not a body
corporate, with the substitution for the reference to a director of the body
of a reference—

161.3.a

in the case of a partnership, to a partner;

161.3.b

in the case of an unincorporated body other than a partnership—

161.3.b.i

where the body’s affairs are managed by its members, to a member of the body;

161.3.b.ii

in any other case, to a member of the governing body.

161.4

Where—

161.4.a

a relevant company is an accountable person for a higher-risk building (within
the meaning of Part 4), and

161.4.b

one or more (but not all) directors of the relevant company have been
appointed for a building safety purpose and are entitled to remuneration from
the company,

this section, so far as relating to Part 4, does not apply in relation to a
director who is not entitled to remuneration from the relevant company.

161.5

In subsection (4)—

                           “ building safety purpose ” means the purpose of
supporting the relevant company in complying with its duties under Part 4 or
under regulations made under that Part;
“ relevant company ” means—
a resident management company within the meaning of section 111,
an RTM company within the meaning of Chapter 1 of Part 2 of the Commonhold and
Leasehold Reform Act 2002 (right to manage), or
a company that is a commonhold association within the meaning of Part 1 of
that Act (see section 34).

#### Review of regulatory regime

162

162.1

The Secretary of State must appoint an independent person to carry out a
review of—

162.1.a

the effectiveness of the regulator in—

162.1.a.i

exercising its building functions,

162.1.a.ii

securing the safety of people in or about buildings in relation to risks
arising from buildings, and

162.1.a.iii

improving the standard of buildings,

162.1.b

the adequacy and effectiveness of—

162.1.b.i

provision made by or under  Parts 2  and  4  of this Act, and

162.1.b.ii

provision made by or under the Building Act 1984 (except  section 105C ) that
applies in relation to England,

162.1.c

the effectiveness of the regulation of construction products in the United
Kingdom,

162.1.d

such matters connected with any of the matters mentioned in  paragraphs (a)
to  (c)  as the person considers appropriate, and

162.1.e

any other matter specified in the appointment.

162.2

On completion of a review, the appointed person must make a written report to
the Secretary of State—

162.2.a

setting out the result of the review, and

162.2.b

making such recommendations (if any) as the person considers appropriate.

162.3

The Secretary of State must publish a copy of the report.

162.4

The first appointment must be made within the period of 5 years beginning with
the day on which this Act is passed.

162.5

Any other appointment must be made within the period of 5 years beginning with
the day on which the most recent appointment was made.

162.6

In this section—

                           “ building function ” has the meaning given by
section 3;
“ independent ” means appearing to the Secretary of State to be independent
of—
the Secretary of State,
the regulator,
the profession of registered building inspectors,
the built environment industry (as defined by section 30),
persons carrying on activities connected with the manufacture, importation,
marketing or supply of construction products (as defined by  paragraph 24  of
Schedule 11 ), and
local authorities (as so defined);
“ the regulator ” has the meaning given by section 2.

#### Application to Parliament

165

165.1

The following provisions do not apply in relation to the Parliamentary Estate—

165.1.a

sections 99, 100 and 103 (compliance notices under  Part 4 );

165.1.b

paragraphs 1  to  3  of  Schedule 2  (powers of entry of authorised officers).

165.2

If the Palace of Westminster (or any part of it) is a higher-risk building
within the meaning of  Part 4 , for the purposes of that Part the accountable
persons for the building are the Corporate Officer of the House of Lords and
the Corporate Officer of the House of Commons, acting jointly.

165.3

No contravention by a Corporate Officer of a provision made by or under  Part
2  or  4  makes the Corporate Officer criminally liable.

165.4

Subsection (3)  does not affect the criminal liability of relevant members of
the House of Lords staff or of the House of Commons staff (as defined by
sections 194 and 195 of the Employment Rights Act 1996).

165.5

In  subsection (3)  “ Corporate Officer ” means—

165.5.a

the Corporate Officer of the House of Lords,

165.5.b

the Corporate Officer of the House of Commons, or

165.5.c

the Corporate Officers acting jointly.

165.6

In this section “ Parliamentary Estate ” means any building or other premises
occupied for the purposes of either House of Parliament.

166

166.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision that is consequential
on this Act.

166.2

166.2.a

166.2.b

an Act passed later in the same session of Parliament as this Act.

section 167.

#### Power of Welsh Ministers to make consequential provision

167

167.1

The Welsh Ministers may by regulations make provision, in relation to Wales,
that is consequential on  Part 3  or section 156.

167.2

The regulations may amend, repeal or revoke provision made by or under—

167.2.a

an Act passed before this Act;

167.2.b

an Act passed later in the same session of Parliament as this Act;

167.2.c

an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru passed before this Act.

167.3

The regulations may make—

167.3.a

transitional, transitory or saving provision;

167.3.b

different provision for different purposes.

167.4

The regulations are to be made by statutory instrument.

167.5

A statutory instrument containing (whether alone or with other provision)
regulations under this section that amend or repeal provision made by an Act,
or by an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru, may not be made unless a draft of the
instrument has been laid before and approved by a resolution of Senedd Cymru.

167.6

Any other statutory instrument containing regulations under this section is
subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of Senedd Cymru.

#### Regulations

168

168.1

This section applies to regulations under any provision of this Act except—

168.1.a

section 138 (7) (b)  (new homes ombudsman scheme: meaning of “developer”),

168.1.b

section 167 (power of Welsh Ministers to make consequential provision),

168.1.c

section 170 (commencement and transitional provision), and

168.1.d

Schedule 11  (construction products regulations).

168.2

A power to make regulations includes power to make—

168.2.a

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional, transitory or saving
provision;

168.2.b

different provision for different purposes or for different areas.

168.3

Regulations may describe a building by reference to its height, size, design,
use, purpose or any other characteristic.

168.4

A power to make regulations about the way in which anything is to be given to
the regulator (as defined by section 2) includes power to provide that the
thing is to be given in a way specified in a direction made and published by
the regulator in accordance with the regulations.

168.5

Regulations are to be made by statutory instrument.

168.6

A statutory instrument containing (whether alone or with other provision)—

168.6.a

regulations under section 12, 62, 65 (5) , 68, 71, 72, 74,   119A,  123, 126,
128, 129 or 140 or  paragraph 6  of  Schedule 3  or  paragraph 2 (12) ,  13
(10)  or  15 (4)  of  Schedule 7  or paragraph  3 (5) ,  12  or  15  of
Schedule 8 ,

168.6.b

regulations made by virtue of section 65 (3) (c) ,

168.6.c

regulations under section 89 (except regulations only making provision of a
kind mentioned in section 89 (2) ),

168.6.d

regulations under section 90 (except regulations only making provision of a
kind mentioned in section 90 (3)  or  (4) ),

168.6.e

regulations under section 92 (except regulations only making provision of a
kind mentioned in section 92 (3) ),

168.6.f

regulations under sections 153 to 155, or

168.6.g

regulations under section 166 that amend or repeal provision made by an Act,

may not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and
approved by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

168.7

Any other statutory instrument containing regulations is subject to annulment
in pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

169.3

Section 2 (2)  and  Schedule 1  (amendments of the Health and Safety at Work
etc Act 1974) extend to England and Wales and Scotland.

169.4

The amendments made by  Schedule 10  (amendments in connection with the new
homes ombudsman scheme) have the same extent as the provision amended.

169.5

Sections 147 to 149 (liability relating to construction products) extend to
England and Wales and Scotland.

169.6

Section 151 (liability relating to construction products: limitation in
Scotland) extends to Scotland only.

169.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

169.7.a

provide for the provisions mentioned in subsection (5) to extend also to
Northern Ireland, and

169.7.b

make provision (including provision amending this Act or any other enactment)
in relation to the application of the provisions mentioned in subsection (5)
in Northern Ireland.

170.5

The other provisions of this Act come into force on such day as the Secretary
of State may by regulations appoint.

170.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations make transitional or saving
provision in connection with the coming into force of any provision of this
Act.

170.7

Regulations under  subsection (4) (a)  or  (b)  may make transitional or
saving provision.

170.8

The powers to make regulations under this section include power to make
different provision for different purposes or for different areas.

170.9

Regulations under this section are to be made by statutory instrument.

#### Short title

171

This Act may be cited as the Building Safety Act 2022.

######## Powers of the Executive: buildings in England

                 Authorised officers: investigatory powers

Section 22

##### Entry to non-domestic premises without warrant

1

1.1

An authorised officer may enter any non-domestic premises which the officer
has reason to believe it is necessary for the officer to enter for a relevant
purpose—

1.1.a

at any reasonable time, or

1.1.b

at any time, in a situation which in the officer’s opinion is or may be
dangerous.

1.2

The officer may be accompanied by any person, and bring anything, required for
any purpose for which the officer is exercising the power of entry.

1.3

If the officer has reasonable cause to expect any obstruction in the exercise
of any relevant power, the officer may be accompanied by a constable.

1.4

The officer may—

1.4.a

take measurements and photographs, and may make recordings;

1.4.b

take samples of anything.

1.5

The officer may seize anything if it appears to the officer—

1.5.a

to be evidence of an offence under this Act or the Building Act 1984, and

1.5.b

to be necessary to seize it to prevent the evidence being concealed, lost,
altered or destroyed.

##### Entry to non-domestic premises with warrant

2

2.1

A justice of the peace may issue a warrant in respect of non-domestic premises
specified in the warrant if satisfied, on an information in writing made by an
authorised officer, that it is necessary—

2.1.a

for an authorised officer to enter the premises for a relevant purpose, and

2.1.b

to confer a power to enter by force (if necessary).

2.2

The warrant authorises any authorised officer to enter the premises at any
time (subject to  sub-paragraph (3) ) for the purposes specified in the
warrant, by force (if necessary).

2.3

The warrant may limit the times at which the power of entry may be exercised.

2.4

Sub-paragraphs (2)  to  (5)  of  paragraph 1  apply in relation to the power
of entry conferred by a warrant under  this paragraph  as they apply in
relation to the power of entry conferred by  sub-paragraph (1)  of that
paragraph.

##### Entry to domestic premises (with warrant)

3

3.1

A justice of the peace may issue a warrant in respect of domestic premises
specified in the warrant if satisfied, on an information in writing made by an
authorised officer, that—

3.1.a

it is necessary for an authorised officer to enter the premises for a relevant
purpose, and

3.1.b

one of the following conditions is met—

3.1.b.i

that entry to the premises for the relevant purpose has been, or is likely to
be, refused;

3.1.b.ii

that no person entitled to grant entry to the premises can be found;

3.1.b.iii

that requesting entry may frustrate or seriously prejudice the purpose of
entry.

3.2

The warrant—

3.2.a

authorises any authorised officer to enter the premises at any time (subject
to  sub-paragraph (3) ) for the purposes specified in the warrant, and

3.2.b

confers such additional powers as may be specified in the warrant.

3.3

The warrant may limit the times at which the power of entry may be exercised.

3.4

For this purpose “ additional powers ” means—

3.4.a

the power to enter by force (if necessary);

3.4.b

the powers under  sub-paragraphs (2)  to  (5)  of  paragraph 1 .

3.5

An additional power may be specified in the warrant only if the justice of the
peace is satisfied that it is necessary to confer the power.

##### Power to require information, documents etc

4

4.1

An authorised officer may for a relevant purpose require a person to give
specified information or documents to the officer by such time as may be
specified.

4.2

In the case of a document consisting of information held in electronic form,
the officer may require it to be produced—

4.2.a

in a legible form, or

4.2.b

in a form from which it can readily be produced in legible form.

4.3

The officer may inspect and take copies of (or of any information in) any
document that is produced.

4.4

An authorised officer may for a relevant purpose require a person to provide
such facilities and assistance to the officer as may be specified, by such
time as may be specified.

4.5

A requirement under this paragraph is imposed by the authorised officer in
question giving, to the person in question, a notice in writing that states—

4.5.a

that it is a notice containing a requirement under this paragraph, and

4.5.b

the consequences of failing to comply with the requirement.

4.6

Information provided by a person under  sub-paragraph (1)  is not admissible
in evidence against that person in criminal proceedings except—

4.6.a

in proceedings for an offence under section 24,

4.6.b

in proceedings for an offence under  paragraph 6 (1) ,

4.6.c

in proceedings for an offence of perverting the course of justice, or

4.6.d

if in the proceedings—

4.6.d.i

in giving evidence the person makes a statement inconsistent with the
information, and

4.6.d.ii

evidence as to the information that was provided is adduced, or a question
relating to it is asked, by or on behalf of the person.

4.7

In this paragraph—

                                    “ document ” includes information recorded
in any form;
“ specified ”, in relation to a requirement, means specified in the notice
imposing the requirement.

##### Retention of evidence etc

5

Anything that has been seized under  paragraph 1 (5) , or any document
produced under  paragraph 4 , may be retained for so long as is necessary in
all the circumstances.

##### Offence of failing to provide information, documents etc

6

6.1

A person who fails without reasonable excuse to comply with a requirement
under  paragraph 4  commits an offence.

6.2

A person guilty of an offence under  this paragraph  is liable—

6.2.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum
summary term for either-way offences or a fine (or both);

6.2.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both).

##### Interpretation

7

7.1

In  this Schedule  —

                                    “ authorised officer ”, in relation to the
exercise of any power conferred by or the doing of anything else mentioned in
a paragraph of  this Schedule  for the purpose of a relevant building
function, means a person authorised under section 22 in relation to that
paragraph for the purposes of that function;
“ domestic premises ” means premises (in England or Wales) used wholly or
mainly as a private dwelling;
“ non-domestic premises ” means premises (in England or Wales) that are not
domestic premises;
“ relevant purpose ”, in relation to an authorised officer, means the purpose
of any relevant building function specified in the officer’s authorisation.

7.2

In sub-paragraph (1) “ relevant building function ” has the meaning given by
section 22.

##### Saving for material subject to legal professional privilege

8

Nothing in this Schedule confers power to—

8.a

seize anything, or

8.b

compel the production by any person of a document or information,

in respect of which a claim to legal professional privilege could be
maintained in legal proceedings.

Cooperation and information sharing

Section 27

##### Interpretation



1

In  this Schedule  any reference to a function under an enactment includes a
function under an instrument made under the enactment.

##### Local authorities, fire and rescue authorities etc



2

2.1

The regulator and a local authority must cooperate with each other in the
exercise of their relevant functions.

2.2

The regulator and a fire and rescue authority must cooperate with each other
in the exercise of—

2.2.a

any building function of the regulator,

2.2.b

any function of the authority under—

2.2.b.i

section 6 or 7 of the Fire and Rescue Services Act 2004,

2.2.b.ii

the Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order 2005, or

2.2.b.iii

section 13 of this Act, and

2.2.c

any other prescribed function of the authority.

2.3

The regulator and an FSO authorised person must cooperate with each other in
the exercise of their relevant functions.

2.4

A relevant person may disclose information held in connection with any of
their relevant functions to another relevant person for the purposes of a
relevant function of either of them.

2.5

In  this paragraph —

“ FSO authorised person ” has the meaning given by section 14; “ relevant
function ” means— in relation to the regulator, any building function; in
relation to a local authority, a function under any of the following— the
Prevention of Damage by Pests Act 1949; Part 2 of the Public Health Act 1961;
Part 11 of the Local Government (Miscellaneous Provisions) Act 1982; the
Building Act 1984; Part 3 of the Environmental Protection Act 1990; Parts 1 to
4 of the Housing Act 2004; section 13 of this Act; or any other prescribed
function; in relation to a fire and rescue authority, a function under any of
the following— the Fire and Rescue Services Act 2004; the Regulatory Reform
(Fire Safety) Order 2005; section 13 of this Act; or any other prescribed
function; in relation to an FSO authorised person, any function under— the
Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order 2005, or section 14 of this Act; “
relevant person ” means— the regulator; a local authority; a fire and rescue
authority; an FSO authorised person.

##### Ombudsmen



3

3.1

The regulator and a person mentioned in  sub-paragraph (4)  must cooperate
with each other in the exercise of—

3.1.a

any building function of the regulator, and

3.1.b

any relevant function of the person.

3.2

The regulator may disclose to a person mentioned in  sub-paragraph (4)
information held in connection with any of its building functions, for the
purpose of any of those functions or any relevant functions of the person.

3.3

A person mentioned in  sub-paragraph (4)  may disclose to the regulator
information held in connection with any of their relevant functions, for the
purpose of any of those functions or any building function of the regulator.

3.4

The persons are—

3.4.a

the Regulator of Social Housing;

3.4.b

a person who administers a relevant scheme.

3.5

“ Relevant scheme ” means—

3.5.a

a scheme approved under Schedule 2 to the Housing Act 1996 (housing
complaints: social landlords),

3.5.b

a redress scheme to which persons are required by virtue of section 83 of the
Enterprise and Regulatory Reform Act 2013 (lettings agency work) to be
members,

3.5.c

a redress scheme to which persons are required by virtue of section 84 of that
Act (property management work) to be members, or

3.5.d

the new homes ombudsman scheme.

3.6

In  this paragraph  “ relevant function ” means—

3.6.a

in relation to the Regulator of Social Housing, any of its functions;

3.6.b

in relation to a person who administers a relevant scheme, any function
relating to that scheme.

##### Secretary of State



4

4.1

The regulator may disclose to the Secretary of State information held in
connection with any of its building functions, for the purpose of any of those
functions or any relevant function of the Secretary of State.

4.2

The Secretary of State may disclose to the regulator information held in
connection with any relevant function, for the purpose of any relevant
function or any building function of the regulator.

4.3

In  this paragraph  “ relevant function ” means any function of the Secretary
of State (whether or not under an enactment) that relates to buildings.

##### Police



5

5.1

The regulator may disclose to a constable information held by it in connection
with any of its building functions.

5.2

A constable to whom information is disclosed in pursuance of  sub-paragraph
(1)  must not use the information for a purpose other than—

5.2.a

a purpose relating to the prevention, detection, investigation or prosecution
of an offence (whether or not under this Act);

5.2.b

a purpose of the police relating to public health or public safety;

5.2.c

a purpose relating to national security.

##### Public authorities



6

6.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision requiring the
regulator and any prescribed public authority to cooperate with each other in
the exercise of—

6.1.a

any building function of the regulator, and

6.1.b

any prescribed function of the public authority, so far as it relates to
England.

6.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision authorising a
relevant person and any prescribed public authority to disclose prescribed
information to each other for the purpose of—

6.2.a

any relevant function of the relevant person, and

6.2.b

any prescribed function of the public authority, so far as it relates to
England.

6.3

In  this paragraph  “relevant person” and “relevant function” have the meaning
given in  paragraph 2 .

56

After section 91A insert—

######### Cooperation and the sharing of information: Wales

56.91B

56.91B.1

Relevant persons (as defined by subsection (7)) must cooperate with each other
in the exercise of any of the following functions—

56.91B.1.a

any function of a local authority under this Act,

56.91B.1.b

any function of a Welsh fire and rescue authority under—

56.91B.1.b.i

section 6 or 7 of the Fire and Rescue Services Act 2004, or

56.91B.1.b.ii

the Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order 2005, and

56.91B.1.c

any function of a fire inspector under that Order.

56.91B.2

A relevant person may disclose information held in connection with any of
their relevant functions to another relevant person for the purposes of a
relevant function of either of them.

56.91B.3

The Welsh Ministers and a relevant person must cooperate with each other in
the exercise of any of the following functions—

56.91B.3.a

a function of the Welsh Ministers under Part 2A;

56.91B.3.b

a function mentioned in the relevant paragraph of subsection (1).

56.91B.4

The Welsh Ministers may disclose information held in connection with a
function under Part 2A to a relevant person for the purposes of—

56.91B.4.a

a function of the Welsh Ministers under Part 2A, or

56.91B.4.b

 a function mentioned in the relevant paragraph of subsection (1).

56.91B.5

A relevant person may disclose information held in connection with a function
mentioned in the relevant paragraph of subsection (1) to the Welsh Ministers
for the purposes of—

56.91B.5.a

a function mentioned in the relevant paragraph of subsection (1), or

56.91B.5.b

a function of the Welsh Ministers under Part 2A.

56.91B.6

In subsections (3) to (5) “the relevant paragraph” of subsection (1), in
relation to a kind of relevant person, means the paragraph of subsection (1)
relating to a relevant person of that kind.

56.91B.7

In this section—

“ fire inspector ” means an inspector or assistant inspector appointed under
section 28(1) of the Fire and Rescue Services Act 2004; “ relevant person ”
means a local authority in Wales, Welsh fire and rescue authority or fire
inspector; “ relevant function ” means— in relation to a local authority, any
function of a local authority under— the Prevention of Damage by Pests Act
1949, Part 2 of the Public Health Act 1961, Part 11 of the Local Government
(Miscellaneous Provisions) Act 1982, Part 3 of the Environmental Protection
Act 1990, Parts 1 to 4 of the Housing Act 2004, or this Act, or any prescribed
function of a local authority; in relation to a Welsh fire and rescue
authority, any function of such an authority under— the Fire and Rescue
Services Act 2004, or the Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order 2005, or any
prescribed function of such an authority; in relation to a fire inspector, any
function of a fire inspector under the Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order
2005; “ Welsh fire and rescue authority ” means a fire and rescue authority,
within the meaning of Part 1 of the Fire and Rescue Services Act 2004, for an
area in Wales.

56.91B.8

Except as provided by subsection (9), the disclosure of information under this
section does not breach—

56.91B.8.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

56.91B.8.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

56.91B.9

This section does not authorise a disclosure of information if the disclosure
would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, take into account the powers conferred by this
section).

77

After section 120 insert—

######### Regulations

77.120A

77.120A.1

This section applies to regulations under section 54A, 55, 56A, 56B,  90A ,
91A, 92,  105B ,  105C ,  120D ,  120I  or  125A .

77.120A.2

A power to make regulations includes power to make—

77.120A.2.a

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional, transitory or saving
provision;

77.120A.2.b

different provision for different purposes or for different areas.

77.120A.3

Regulations may describe a building by reference to its height, size, design,
use, purpose or any other characteristic.

77.120A.4

Regulations under section 54A may make such consequential amendments of this
Act as the appropriate national authority considers appropriate.

77.120A.5

Regulations under section  90A  may make such consequential amendments of this
Act as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

77.120A.6

Regulations are to be made by statutory instrument.

77.120A.7

A statutory instrument containing (whether alone or with other provision)—

77.120A.7.a

regulations under section 54A,  90A ,  105C  or  125A , or

77.120A.7.b

regulations under section  120D (2) (b)  or  (6) , or regulations made by
virtue of  section 120D (4) (c) ,

may not be made by the Secretary of State unless a draft of the instrument has
been laid before and approved by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

77.120A.8

Any other statutory instrument containing regulations made by the Secretary of
State is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

77.120A.9

A statutory instrument containing (whether alone or with other provision)
regulations under section 54A,  120I (2) or  125A  may not be made by the
Welsh Ministers unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and
approved by a resolution of Senedd Cymru.

77.120A.10

Any other statutory instrument containing regulations made by the Welsh
Ministers is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of Senedd
Cymru.

######### Proposals and consultation relating to regulations made by the Secretary of State

77.120B

77.120B.1

The regulator may at any time make proposals to the Secretary of State for the
making of regulations under this Act.

77.120B.2

Before making a proposal, the regulator must consult such persons as it
considers appropriate.

77.120B.3

Before making any regulations under this Act, other than regulations proposed
by the regulator, the Secretary of State must consult—

77.120B.3.a

the regulator, and

77.120B.3.b

any other person that the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

77.120B.4

This section does not apply in relation to regulations under  section 120D .

######### Consultation relating to regulations made by the Welsh Ministers

77.120C

77.120C.1

Before making any regulations under this Act except building regulations or
regulations under  section 120I , the Welsh Ministers must consult such
persons as they consider appropriate.

77.120C.2

Before making any regulations under  section 120I , the Welsh Ministers must
consult—

77.120C.2.a

the Building Regulations Advisory Committee for Wales, and

77.120C.2.b

any other person that the Welsh Ministers consider appropriate.

77.120C.3

See also section 14 (consultation requirements for building regulations).
