##### Enforcement

29

After section 105 insert—

######### Enforcement of decisions of the First-tier and Upper Tribunal

29.105A

29.105A.1

A decision of the First-tier Tribunal or Upper Tribunal made under or in
connection with this Act is enforceable with the permission of the county
court in the same way as an order of that court.

29.105A.2

Subsection (1) does not apply to a decision of the First-tier Tribunal or
Upper Tribunal ordering the payment of a sum (as to which see section 27 of
the Tribunals, Courts and Enforcement Act 2007 (enforcement)).

##### Appeal: local authority decision not to consider application etc

30

After section 101 insert—

######### Appeal against refusal to consider application etc

########## Appeal: refusal to consider application etc on ground is higher-risk building work

30.101A

30.101A.1

This section applies where—

30.101A.1.a

a local authority for an area in England refuses to consider an application
for building control approval, or

30.101A.1.b

a local authority refuses to consider an initial notice (within the meaning of
section 47) or an amendment notice (within the meaning of section 51A),

on the ground that all or part of the work to which the application or notice
relates is higher-risk building work.

30.101A.2

The person intending to carry out the work may appeal to the appropriate
national authority, before the end of the prescribed period, on the ground
that none of the work is higher-risk building work.

30.101A.3

Building regulations may make provision about appeals under this section,
including in particular provision—

30.101A.3.a

about the making of an appeal;

30.101A.3.b

requiring an appellant to notify the local authority of the making of an
appeal;

30.101A.3.c

imposing duties on the local authority in cases where an appeal is made;

30.101A.3.d

for and in connection with the appropriate national authority appointing a
person to determine the appeal (including provision conferring functions on
that person and providing that their decision is treated as the decision of
the appropriate national authority);

30.101A.3.e

about the procedure to be adopted in connection with the determination of the
appeal.

30.101A.4

The provision that may be made by virtue of subsection (3)(a) includes
provision about—

30.101A.4.a

the form and content of a notice of appeal;

30.101A.4.b

the information and documents that are to accompany a notice of appeal;

30.101A.4.c

the way in which a notice of appeal, and anything that is to accompany it, is
to be given.

30.101A.5

The decision made on the appeal is final (subject to subsection  (6) ).

30.101A.6

The appellant or the local authority may, before the end of the prescribed
period and with the permission of the High Court, appeal to the High Court
against the decision of the appropriate national authority on a point of law.

Special measures

Section 102

##### Introductory

1

In this Schedule—

“ special measures manager ” means a person appointed under paragraph  4 ; “
special measures order ” means an order under paragraph  4 .

##### Notification by regulator before applying for special measures order

2

2.1

This paragraph applies where the regulator proposes to make an application
under paragraph  4  for a special measures order in relation to an occupied
higher-risk building.

2.2

The regulator must give a notice (an “initial notice”) of the proposal to—

2.2.a

each accountable person for the building,

2.2.b

each resident of the building who is aged 16 or over,

2.2.c

each owner of a residential unit in the building,

2.2.d

any managing agent for the building or any relevant part of the building,

2.2.e

any recognised tenants’ association for the building or any part of the
building,

2.2.f

any manager appointed under section 24 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1987 in
relation to the building or any part of the building,

2.2.g

the fire and rescue authority for the area in which the building is situated,

2.2.h

the local housing authority for the area in which the building is situated,

2.2.i

where any accountable person for the building is a registered provider of
social housing, the Regulator of Social Housing, and

2.2.j

where any part of the building contains premises occupied for the purposes of
a business, each responsible person (within the meaning of article 3 of the
Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order 2005) in relation to those premises.

2.3

The initial notice must—

2.3.a

state that the regulator proposes to make an application for a special
measures order in relation to the building,

2.3.b

specify the address of the building,

2.3.c

specify the reasons for the proposed application,

2.3.d

specify the terms of the order that the regulator proposes to invite the
tribunal to make (including the name and address of the person the regulator
proposes to be the special measures manager for the building),

2.3.e

specify a period in which recipients of the notice may make representations in
response to the notice, and

2.3.f

state that any representations must be in writing to such postal or email
address as is specified in the notice.

2.4

Where the terms specified by virtue of sub-paragraph  (3) (d)  include a term
requiring an accountable person for the building to make payments to the
special measures manager for the building, the regulator must give to the
persons mentioned in sub-paragraph  (2)  a financial management proposal with
the initial notice.

2.5

After the end of the period mentioned in sub-paragraph  (3) (e)  the regulator
must—

2.5.a

decide whether to make the application, and

2.5.b

give a notice (a “final notice”) of its decision to the persons mentioned in
sub-paragraph  (2) .

2.6

The final notice must—

2.6.a

state whether or not the regulator intends to make the application,

2.6.b

specify the reasons for reaching that decision, and

2.6.c

if the regulator intends to make the application, specify the terms of the
order that the regulator intends to invite the tribunal to make (including the
name and address of the person the regulator proposes to be the special
measures manager for the building).

2.7

Where the terms specified by virtue of sub-paragraph  (6) (c)  include a term
requiring an accountable person for the building to make payments to the
special measures manager for the building, the regulator must give to the
persons mentioned in sub-paragraph  (2)  a financial management proposal with
the final notice.

2.8

The regulator must comply with sub-paragraphs  (5)  to  (7)  before making the
application.

2.9

The duty under sub-paragraph  (2) ,  (4) , (5)(b) or  (7)  does not apply in
relation to a person mentioned in sub-paragraph  (2)  if the regulator—

2.9.a

is not aware of the person, and

2.9.b

has taken all reasonable steps to ascertain the identity of the persons
mentioned in that sub-paragraph.

2.10

In this paragraph—

“ financial management proposal ” has the meaning given by paragraph  3 ; “
relevant part ”, in relation to a higher-risk building, means any part of the
building except premises occupied for the purposes of a business.

2.11

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision in relation to
notices under this paragraph, including in particular provision about—

2.11.a

the form of the notice;

2.11.b

the way in which the notice must be given.

2.12

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the list in sub-paragraph  (2)
.

##### Meaning of “financial management proposal”

3

3.1

In this Schedule “ financial management proposal ”, in relation to a higher-
risk building, means a document setting out—

3.1.a

an estimate of the relevant expenses the regulator expects a special measures
manager for the building to incur (including a reasonable amount in respect of
contingencies),

3.1.b

the measures to which the relevant expenses relate, and

3.1.c

if there is more than one accountable person for the building—

3.1.c.i

the regulator's proposed apportionment of the relevant expenses between them,
and

3.1.c.ii

the reasons for that proposal (including any calculation giving rise to it).

3.2

In this Schedule “ relevant expenses ” means expenses incurred by the special
measures manager for a higher-risk building in connection with the exercise of
their functions in relation to the building.

##### Special measures order

4

4.1

The regulator may apply to the tribunal for an order under this paragraph in
relation to an occupied higher-risk building (a “special measures order”).

4.2

A special measures order is an order appointing a person to be the manager (a
“special measures manager”) for the building to carry out the functions of all
accountable persons for the building under, or under regulations made under,
this Part.

4.3

A special measures order may also appoint the manager to carry out any
function as a receiver in relation to commonhold building safety assessments.

4.4

The tribunal may make a special measures order if satisfied that there has
been a serious failure, or a failure on two or more occasions, by an
accountable person for the building to comply with a duty imposed on that
person under, or under regulations made under, this Part.

4.5

A special measures order may make provision with respect to—

4.5.a

payments to be made by an accountable person for the building to the special
measures manager in connection with relevant expenses incurred, or to be
incurred, by the manager,

4.5.b

any other matter relating to the exercise of the manager’s functions, and

4.5.c

any incidental or ancillary matter.

4.6

A special measures order may not make the provision mentioned in sub-paragraph
(5)(a) in relation to a higher-risk building on commonhold land.

4.7

A special measures order continues in force until it is discharged.

4.8

In this Schedule “ commonhold building safety assessment ” means income raised
from commonhold unit-holders by virtue of section 38A of the Commonhold and
Leasehold Reform Act 2002.

##### Special measures order: supplementary

5

5.1

This paragraph applies where a special measures order is made in relation to a
higher-risk building.

5.2

While the order is in force any function of an accountable person for the
building under, or under regulations made under, this Part is to be treated as
a function of the special measures manager for the building, except any
function relating to—

5.2.a

the making of an application to the tribunal, or

5.2.b

the making of an appeal to the tribunal.

5.3

Any compliance notice given under section 99 relating to the building ceases
to have effect (but this does not affect any liability incurred as a result of
a contravention of a compliance notice occurring before the making of the
order).

##### Payments received by special measures manager to be held on trust

6

6.1

This paragraph applies where a special measures order relating to a higher-
risk building requires one or more accountable persons for the building to
make payments to the special measures manager for the building.

6.2

The manager must hold the payments (together with any income accruing on those
payments) as either—

6.2.a

a single trust fund, or

6.2.b

in two or more separate trust funds.

6.3

The manager must hold any trust fund—

6.3.a

on trust to defray relevant expenses, and

6.3.b

subject to that, on trust for the accountable person or persons for the
building for the time being.

6.4

The accountable person or persons for the building for the time being are to
be treated as entitled by virtue of sub-paragraph (3)(b) to—

6.4.a

if there is one accountable person for the building, the residue of the fund
or funds;

6.4.b

otherwise, to such shares in that residue as the accountable persons may agree
in writing or (in default of agreement) as the tribunal may direct.

6.5

An application for a direction under sub-paragraph (4)(b) may be made by—

6.5.a

the regulator,

6.5.b

an accountable person for the building, or

6.5.c

the manager.

##### Effect of special measures order on relevant contracts and legal proceedings

7

7.1

Sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (6)  apply while a special measures order relating
to a higher-risk building is in force.

7.2

A relevant contract has effect as if relevant rights and liabilities of an
accountable person for the building arising under the contract were rights and
liabilities of the special measures manager for the building.

7.3

A contract is a “relevant contract” if—

7.3.a

it is effective on the date the special measures order is made,

7.3.b

one of the parties to it is an accountable person for the building,

7.3.c

one or more rights or liabilities of that person under the contract are
relevant rights or liabilities,

7.3.d

it is specified for the purposes of this sub-paragraph in the special measures
order or falls within a description of contracts so specified, and

7.3.e

the manager gives notice in writing to the parties to it stating that sub-
paragraph  (2)  is to apply to it.

7.4

A right or liability of an accountable person for the building under a
relevant contract is a “relevant right or liability” if it relates to a
function of that person under, or under regulations made under, this Part in
relation to the building.

7.5

The notice under sub-paragraph  (3) (e)  must state which rights or
liabilities under the contract are relevant rights or liabilities.

7.6

The special measures manager for the building may bring, continue or defend a
relevant cause of action.

7.7

A cause of action is a “relevant cause of action” if—

7.7.a

it accrued to or against an accountable person for the building before the
date the special measures order was made,

7.7.b

it relates to a function of that person under, or under regulations made
under, this Part in relation to the building,

7.7.c

it is specified for the purposes of this sub-paragraph in the special measures
order or falls within a description of causes of action so specified, and

7.7.d

the manager gives notice in writing to any person the manager considers would
have an interest in the cause of action that sub-paragraph  (6)  is to apply
to it.

7.8

Where, by virtue of this paragraph, the special measures manager for the
building is subject to a liability to pay damages in respect of anything done
(or not done) before the date of their appointment by or on behalf of an
accountable person for the building, that person is liable to reimburse to the
manager an amount equal to the amount of damages paid by the manager.

##### Special measures orders and orders under section 24 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1987

8

8.1

Sub-paragraph (2) applies where—

8.1.a

the tribunal makes a special measures order in relation to a higher-risk
building, and

8.1.b

an order under section 24 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1987 appointing a
manager in relation to that building is in force (a “section 24 order”).

8.2

The tribunal may amend the section 24 order so as to ensure that the functions
to be carried out by virtue of that order do not include any function that the
special measures order provides is to be carried out by the special measures
manager.

8.3

In section 24 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1987, after subsection (2B)
insert—

8.3.2C

Where a special measures order relating to the building is in force, an order
under this section may not provide for a manager to carry out a function which
the special measures order provides is to be carried out by the special
measures manager for the building.

8.3.2D

In this section—

“ special measures manager ” means a person appointed under paragraph 4 of
Schedule 7 to the Building Safety Act 2022; “ special measures order ” means
an order under paragraph 4 of Schedule 7 to the Building Safety Act 2022.

9

9.1

The Landlord and Tenant Act 1987 is amended as follows.

9.2

In section 21(2) after “subsection (3)” insert  “and section 24ZA” .

9.3

After section 24 insert—

########### Application for appointment of manager by special measures manager

9.3.24ZA

9.3.24ZA.1

A special measures manager for an occupied higher-risk building may apply to
the appropriate tribunal for an order under section 24 (as modified by
subsection (4)) appointing a manager to act in relation to premises to which
this section applies.

9.3.24ZA.2

This section applies to premises consisting of the whole or part of the
higher-risk building if the building or part contains two or more flats.

9.3.24ZA.3

Section 22 applies in relation to such an application as if—

9.3.24ZA.3.a

for subsection (1) there were substituted—

9.3.24ZA.3.a.1

Before an application for an order under section 24 is made in respect of any
premises to which section 24ZA applies by a special measures manager for an
occupied higher-risk building, a notice under this section must (subject to
subsection (3)) be served by the special measures manager on—

9.3.24ZA.3.a.1.a

the landlord;

9.3.24ZA.3.a.1.b

any person (other than the landlord) by whom obligations relating to the
management of the premises or any part of them are owed to tenants of flats
contained in those premises under a tenancy;

9.3.24ZA.3.a.1.c

each accountable person for the higher-risk building.

;

9.3.24ZA.3.b

for subsection (2)(a) there were substituted—

9.3.24ZA.3.b.a

specify the special measures manager’s name and an address in England and
Wales at which any person on whom the notice is served may serve notices,
including notices in proceedings, on the special measures manager in
connection with this Part;

;

9.3.24ZA.3.c

in subsection (2)(b)—

9.3.24ZA.3.c.i

for “tenant” there were substituted  “special measures manager” ;

9.3.24ZA.3.c.ii

for “this Part” there were substituted  “section 24ZA” ;

9.3.24ZA.3.d

in subsection (2)(c) for “tenant” there were substituted  “special measures
manager” .

9.3.24ZA.4

Section 24 applies in relation to such an application as if—

9.3.24ZA.4.a

in subsection (1) for “this Part” there were substituted  “section 24ZA” ;

9.3.24ZA.4.b

for subsection (2) there were substituted—

9.3.24ZA.4.b.2

The appropriate tribunal may only make an order under this section where it is
satisfied—

9.3.24ZA.4.b.2.a

that—

9.3.24ZA.4.b.2.a.i

the relevant person is in breach of any obligation owed by the person to the
special measures manager by virtue of a special measures order, and

9.3.24ZA.4.b.2.a.ii

it is just and convenient to make the order in all the circumstances of the
case; or

9.3.24ZA.4.b.2.b

that other circumstances exist which make it just and convenient for the order
to be made.

;

9.3.24ZA.4.c

subsections (2A), (2B) and (10) were omitted.

9.3.24ZA.5

In this section “ special measures manager ” has the meaning given by section
24(2D).

##### Provision of financial assistance by regulator

10

10.1

The regulator may give financial assistance to the special measures manager
for a higher-risk building by way of loans or grants.

10.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision in relation to
financial assistance given under this paragraph, including in particular
provision about—

10.2.a

the circumstances in which financial assistance may be given;

10.2.b

the kind of financial assistance that may be given;

10.2.c

conditions that may or must be attached to any financial assistance (including
conditions as to repayment).

10.3

In this paragraph “ special measures manager ”, in relation to a higher-risk
building, includes the person who was the special measures manager for that
building immediately before the special measures order relating to the
building was discharged.

##### Special measures order: further directions

11

11.1

This paragraph applies while a special measures order relating to a higher-
risk building is in force.

11.2

On an application by a person mentioned in sub-paragraph (3) the tribunal may
give directions to the special measures manager for the building or any other
person with respect to—

11.2.a

any matter relating to the exercise of the manager’s functions, and

11.2.b

any incidental or ancillary matter.

11.3

The persons are—

11.3.a

the regulator,

11.3.b

an accountable person for the building, or

11.3.c

the manager.

##### Regulator to keep certain matters under review

12

12.1

This paragraph applies while a special measures order relating to a higher-
risk building is in force.

12.2

The regulator must, from time to time (and at least once every 12 months),
review the following matters—

12.2.a

the measures taken by the special measures manager in exercising the manager’s
functions;

12.2.b

the expenses incurred by the manager in connection with taking those measures;

12.2.c

any payments made by accountable persons for the building to the manager in
respect of any of those expenses;

12.2.d

any amounts received by the manager by way of commonhold building safety
assessments in relation to the building.

12.3

If, on such a review, the regulator considers that any term of the order
should be varied, it must make such application under paragraph 14 as it
considers appropriate.

##### Notification by regulator before applying to vary special measures order

13

13.1

This paragraph applies where the regulator proposes to make an application
under paragraph 14 to vary a special measures order relating to a higher-risk
building.

13.2

The regulator must give a notice (an “initial notice”) of the proposal to—

13.2.a

each accountable person for the building,

13.2.b

each resident of the building who is aged 16 or over,

13.2.c

each owner of a residential unit in the building,

13.2.d

any managing agent for the building or any relevant part of the building,

13.2.e

any recognised tenants’ association for the building or any part of the
building,

13.2.f

any manager appointed under section 24 of the Landlord and Tenant Act in
relation to the building or any part of the building,

13.2.g

the fire and rescue authority for the area in which the building is situated,

13.2.h

the local housing authority for the area in which the building is situated,

13.2.i

where any accountable person for the building is a registered provider of
social housing, the Regulator of Social Housing, and

13.2.j

where any part of the building contains premises occupied for the purposes of
a business, each responsible person (within the meaning of article 3 of the
Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order 2005) in relation to those premises.

13.3

The initial notice must—

13.3.a

state that the regulator proposes to make an application to vary the special
measures order specified in the notice,

13.3.b

specify the reasons for the proposed application,

13.3.c

specify the terms of the order that the regulator proposes to invite the
tribunal to make,

13.3.d

specify a period in which recipients of the notice may make representations in
response to the notice, and

13.3.e

state that any representations must be in writing to such postal or email
address as is specified in the notice.

13.4

After the end of the period mentioned in sub-paragraph (3)(d) the regulator
must—

13.4.a

decide whether to make the application, and

13.4.b

give a notice (a “final notice”) of its decision to the persons mentioned in
sub-paragraph (2).

13.5

The final notice must—

13.5.a

state whether or not the regulator intends to make the application,

13.5.b

specify the reasons for reaching that decision, and

13.5.c

if the regulator intends to make the application, specify the terms of the
order that the regulator intends to invite the tribunal to make.

13.6

The regulator must comply with sub-paragraphs (4) and (5) before making the
application.

13.7

The duty under sub-paragraph (2) or (4)(b) does not apply in relation to a
person mentioned in sub-paragraph (2) if the regulator—

13.7.a

is not aware of the person, and

13.7.b

has taken all reasonable steps to ascertain the identity of the persons
mentioned in that sub-paragraph.

13.8

In this paragraph “ relevant part ”, in relation to a higher-risk building,
has the meaning given by paragraph 2(10).

13.9

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision in relation to
notices under this paragraph, including in particular provision about—

13.9.a

the form of the notice;

13.9.b

the way in which the notice must be given.

13.10

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the list in sub-paragraph (2).

##### Variation or discharge of special measures order

14

14.1

The tribunal may vary or discharge a special measures order relating to a
higher-risk building on an application by—

14.1.a

the regulator,

14.1.b

an accountable person for the building, or

14.1.c

the special measures manager for the building.

14.2

An application to vary a special measures order so as to change the identity
of the manager may only be made by the regulator.

14.3

In considering whether to vary or discharge an order the tribunal must have
regard to—

14.3.a

the likelihood of variation or discharge of the order resulting in a
recurrence of the circumstances which led to the order being made, and

14.3.b

whether it is just and convenient in all the circumstances to vary or
discharge the order.

14.4

Sub-paragraphs (2) and (3) do not apply on an application where each person
mentioned in sub-paragraph (1) agrees to the application (and for this purpose
where there is more than one accountable person each accountable person must
agree).

14.5

Sub-paragraph (4) does not require the agreement of the special measures
manager where that person lacks capacity to agree to the application.

14.6

Where the order is varied or discharged, the tribunal may give directions to
any person with respect to—

14.6.a

any matter relating to the variation or discharge, and

14.6.b

any incidental or ancillary matter.

14.7

Where the order is discharged the tribunal must direct the special measures
manager to—

14.7.a

prepare a reconciliation account, and

14.7.b

give a copy of the account to—

14.7.b.i

the regulator, and

14.7.b.ii

each accountable person for the building.

14.8

The tribunal may give a direction under sub-paragraph (6)(a) (at the time the
order is discharged or after that time) for the making of a payment—

14.8.a

by an accountable person for the building to the special measures manager, or

14.8.b

by the special measures manager to an accountable person for the building.

14.9

In this paragraph—

“ reconciliation account ” means a document— setting out, in relation to the
period during which the special measures order was in force, a comparison
between— the receipts and expenses of the manager in connection with the
exercise of their functions in relation to the building, and the credits to,
and debits from, all relevant accounts, and containing a statement explaining
any differences; “ relevant account ” means an account in which any of the
following are (or have been) held— payments made by an accountable person for
the building to the manager; amounts received by the manager by way of
commonhold building safety assessments in relation to the building.

14.10

In this paragraph “ special measures manager ”, in relation to a higher-risk
building, includes the person who was the special measures manager for that
building immediately before the special measures order relating to the
building was discharged.

##### Notifications about special measures order

15

15.1

The regulator must take all reasonable steps to notify the persons mentioned
in sub-paragraph  (2)  of the making, variation or discharge of a special
measures order in relation to a higher-risk building.

15.2

The persons are—

15.2.a

each accountable person for the building,

15.2.b

each resident of the building who is aged 16 or over,

15.2.c

each owner of a residential unit in the building,

15.2.d

any managing agent for the building or any relevant part of the building,

15.2.e

any recognised tenants’ association for the building or any part of the
building,

15.2.f

any manager appointed under section 24 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1987 in
relation to the building or any part of the building,

15.2.g

the fire and rescue authority for the area in which the building is situated,

15.2.h

the local housing authority for the area in which the building is situated,

15.2.i

where any accountable person for the building is a registered provider of
social housing, the Regulator of Social Housing, and

15.2.j

where any part of the building contains premises occupied for the purposes of
a business, each responsible person (within the meaning of article 3 of the
Regulatory Reform (Fire Safety) Order 2005) in relation to those premises.

15.3

In this paragraph “ relevant part ”, in relation to a higher-risk building,
has the meaning given by paragraph  2 (10) .

15.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the list in sub-paragraph  (2)
.

##### Special measures order: change in accountable person etc

16

16.1

Sub-paragraphs (2) and (3) apply where at any time (“ the relevant time ”)
during which a special measures order relating to a higher-risk building is in
force, an accountable person for the building (“the outgoing person”) ceases
to be responsible for all or any part of the building (“the relevant part of
the building”).

16.2

From the relevant time the special measures order ceases to apply to the
outgoing person in relation to the relevant part of the building.

16.3

From the relevant time the special measures order applies to any person who,
immediately after the relevant time—

16.3.a

is an accountable person for the building, and

16.3.b

is responsible for the relevant part of the building or any part of the
relevant part,

as it applied to the outgoing person in relation to the relevant part or part
of the relevant part (as the case may be) immediately before the relevant
time.

16.4

But sub-paragraphs (2) and (3) do not affect any liability under the order to
which the outgoing person became subject before the relevant time.

16.5

Where an enactment requires interests, charges or other obligations affecting
land to be registered, sub-paragraph (3) has effect whether or not the special
measures order is registered.

16.6

Nothing in this paragraph affects the powers of the tribunal under paragraph
14 (power to vary special measures order etc).

##### Interpretation

17

In this Schedule—

“ commonhold building safety assessment ” has the meaning given by paragraph
4 ; “ local housing authority ” has the meaning given by section 261 of the
Housing Act 2004; “ managing agent ”: for the purposes of this Schedule a
person (A) is a managing agent for any part of a building if— A has been
appointed to discharge the obligations of a person (B) relating to the
management by B of that part of the building, and B has a legal estate in that
part of the building which is— an estate in fee simple absolute in possession,
or; a term of years absolute granted for a term of more than 21 years from the
date of the grant; “ recognised tenants association ” has the meaning given by
section 29 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1985; “ relevant expenses ” has the
meaning given by paragraph  3 ; “ special measures manager ” has the meaning
given by paragraph  1 ; “ special measures order ” has the meaning given by
paragraph  1 .

Remediation costs under qualifying leases etc

Section 122

##### Interpretation

1

1.1

In  this Schedule —

“ associated ”: see section 121; ... “ joint venture ” includes a partnership
(as defined by section 121); “ prescribed ” means prescribed by regulations
made by the Secretary of State; “ qualifying lease ”: see section 119; “ the
qualifying time ” has the same meaning as in section 119; “ relevant building
”: see section 117; “ relevant defect ”: see section 120; “ relevant measure
”, in relation to a relevant defect, means— a measure taken to remedy the
relevant defect, or a relevant step taken in relation to the relevant defect;
“ relevant step ”: see section 120; ... “ service charge ” has the meaning
given by section 18 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1985.

1.2

The definition of “service charge” applies in relation to a lease of premises
that do not include a dwelling as it applies in relation to a lease of a
dwelling.

##### No service charge payable for defect for which landlord or associate responsible

2

2.1

This paragraph  applies in relation to a lease of any premises in a relevant
building.

2.2

No service charge is payable under the lease in respect of a relevant measure
relating to a relevant defect if a relevant landlord—

2.2.a

is responsible for the relevant defect, or

2.2.b

is associated with a person responsible for a relevant defect.

2.3

For the purposes of  this paragraph  a person is “responsible for” a relevant
defect if—

2.3.a

in the case of an initial defect, the person was, or was in a joint venture
with, the developer or undertook or commissioned works relating to the defect;

2.3.b

in any other case, the person undertook or commissioned works relating to the
defect.

2.4

In  this paragraph —

“ developer ” means a person who undertook or commissioned the construction or
conversion of the building (or part of the building) with a view to granting
or disposing of interests in the building or parts of it; “ initial defect ”
means a defect which is a relevant defect by virtue of section 120 (3) (a) ; “
relevant landlord ” means the landlord under the lease at the qualifying time
or any superior landlord at that time.

##### No service charge payable if landlord meets contribution condition

3

3.1

No service charge is payable under a qualifying lease in respect of a relevant
measure relating to any relevant defect if the landlord under the lease at the
qualifying time (“the relevant landlord”) met the contribution condition.

3.2

The contribution condition is that the landlord group’s net worth at the
qualifying time was more than N x £2,000,000,

where N is the number of relevant buildings within sub-paragraph  (3) .

3.3

A relevant building is within this sub-paragraph if a member of the landlord
group was, at the qualifying time, a landlord under a lease of the relevant
building or any part of it.

3.4

For the purposes of  this paragraph —

3.4.a

“ the landlord group ” means the relevant landlord and any person associated
with the relevant landlord;

3.4.b

the net worth of the landlord group at the qualifying time is to be determined
in accordance with regulations made by the Secretary of State.

3.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the amount for the time being
specified in sub-paragraph  (2) .

3.6

This paragraph  does not apply if, at the qualifying time, the relevant
landlord was—

3.6.a

a private registered provider of social housing (as to which see section 80 of
the Housing and Regeneration Act 2008),

3.6.b

a local authority (as defined by section 30), or

3.6.c

a prescribed person.

##### No service charge payable where lease below certain value

4

4.1

No service charge is payable under a qualifying lease in respect of a relevant
measure relating to any relevant defect if the value of the qualifying lease
at the qualifying time was less than—

4.1.a

£325,000, if the premises demised by the qualifying lease are in Greater
London;

4.1.b

£175,000, in any other case.

4.2

For the purposes of  this paragraph  the value of a qualifying lease at the
qualifying time is its value determined in accordance with  paragraph 6  and
regulations made under it.

##### Limit on service charge in other cases

5

5.1

A service charge which would otherwise be payable under a qualifying lease in
respect of a relevant measure relating to any relevant defect is payable only
if (and so far as) the sum of—

5.1.a

the amount of the service charge, and

5.1.b

the total amount of relevant service charges which fell due before the service
charge fell due,

does not exceed the permitted maximum.

5.2

In  this paragraph  “ relevant service charge ” means a service charge under
the lease in respect of a relevant measure relating to any relevant defect
that—

5.2.a

fell due in the pre-commencement period, or

5.2.b

falls due after commencement.

5.3

In  sub-paragraph (2)  “ the pre-commencement period ” means the period—

5.3.a

beginning 5 years before commencement or, if later, on the day the relevant
person became the tenant under the qualifying lease, and

5.3.b

ending with commencement.

“ The relevant person ” means the person who was the tenant under the
qualifying lease at commencement.

5.4

In  this paragraph —

“ commencement ” means the time  this paragraph  comes into force; “ the
permitted maximum ”: see  paragraph 6 .

##### 
                     

6

6.1

In  paragraph 5  “ the permitted maximum ”, in relation to a qualifying lease,
has the following meaning.

6.2

The permitted maximum is (subject to  sub-paragraphs (3)  to  (5) )—

6.2.a

if the premises demised by the qualifying lease are in Greater London,
£15,000;

6.2.b

otherwise, £10,000.

6.3

Where the value of the qualifying lease at the qualifying time exceeded
£1,000,000 but did not exceed £2,000,000, the permitted maximum is £50,000.

6.4

Where the value of the qualifying lease at the qualifying time exceeded
£2,000,000, the permitted maximum is £100,000.

6.5

Where the qualifying lease is a shared ownership lease and the tenant’s total
share was less than 100% at the qualifying time—

6.5.a

the value of the qualifying lease at that time is to be determined as if the
tenant’s total share at that time was 100%;

6.5.b

the permitted maximum is the tenant’s total share (as at that time) of what
would otherwise be the permitted maximum.

6.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the
determination of the value of a qualifying lease for the purposes of
paragraph 4  and  this paragraph .

6.7

The regulations may in particular provide that, except in prescribed cases,
the value of a qualifying lease at the qualifying time is to be determined by—

6.7.a

ascertaining the consideration given on the latest disposal of the qualifying
lease on the open market to have been made before that time, and

6.7.b

if that disposal occurred before 2022, uprating the consideration in
accordance with the regulations.

6.8

In  this paragraph  “shared ownership lease” and “total share” have the
meaning given by section 7 of the Leasehold Reform, Housing and Urban
Development Act 1993.

##### Annual limit on service charges

7

7.1

A relevant service charge which would otherwise be payable under a qualifying
lease is payable only if (and so far as) the sum of—

7.1.a

the amount of the service charge, and

7.1.b

the total amount of relevant service charges which fell due in the period of
12 months ending with the day on which the service charge fell due,

does not exceed one tenth of the permitted maximum.

7.2

In  this paragraph —.

“ the permitted maximum ” means the permitted maximum as defined by  paragraph
6  in relation to the lease; “ relevant service charge ” means a service
charge under a qualifying lease in respect of a relevant measure relating to
any relevant defect.

##### No service charge payable for cladding remediation

8

8.1

No service charge is payable under a qualifying lease in respect of cladding
remediation.

8.2

In  this paragraph  “ cladding remediation ” means the removal or replacement
of any part of a cladding system that—

8.2.a

forms the outer wall of an external wall system, and

8.2.b

is unsafe.

##### No service charge payable for legal or professional services relating to liability for relevant defects

9

9.1

No service charge is payable under a qualifying lease in respect of legal or
other professional services relating to the liability (or potential liability)
of any person incurred as a result of a relevant defect.

9.1A

Sub-paragraph (1) does not apply to the extent that the service charge is
payable to a management company in respect of legal or other professional
services provided to the company in connection with an application or possible
application by the company for or relating to a remediation contribution order
under section 124.

9.2

In  this paragraph  the reference to services includes services provided in
connection with—

9.2.a

obtaining legal advice,

9.2.b

any proceedings before a court or tribunal,

9.2.c

arbitration, or

9.2.d

mediation.

9.3

In sub-paragraph (1A) “ management company ” means—

9.3.a

a resident management company, or

9.3.b

an RTM company within the meaning of Chapter 1 of Part 2 of the Commonhold and
Leasehold Reform Act 2002 (right to manage).

9.4

“ Resident management company ” means a body corporate which is party to a
lease of a building where—

9.4.a

the body corporate is limited by guarantee and the members of that body are
tenants under leases of dwellings in the building (“leaseholders”), or

9.4.b

the majority of the shares of the body corporate are held by leaseholders.

##### Paragraphs 

10

10.1

This paragraph  supplements paragraphs  2  to  4 ,  8  and  9  (the “relevant
paragraphs”).

10.2

Where a relevant paragraph provides that no service charge is payable under a
lease in respect of a thing—

10.2.a

no costs incurred or to be incurred in respect of that thing (or in respect of
that thing and anything else)—

10.2.a.i

are to be regarded for the purposes of the relevant provisions as relevant
costs to be taken into account in determining the amount of a service charge
payable under the lease, or

10.2.a.ii

are to be met from a relevant reserve fund;

10.2.b

any amount payable under the lease, or met from a relevant reserve fund, is
limited accordingly (and any necessary adjustment must be made by repayment,
reduction of subsequent charges or otherwise).

10.3

In  this paragraph —

“ the relevant provisions ” means sections 18 to 30 of the Landlord and Tenant
Act 1985 (service charges) and section 42 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1987
(service charge contributions to be held on trust); “ relevant reserve fund ”
means— a trust fund within the meaning of section 42 of the Landlord and
Tenant Act 1987, an express trust of a kind mentioned in subsection (9) of
that section, comprising payments made by the tenant under the lease and
others, or any other fund comprising payments made by the tenant under the
lease and others, and held for the purposes of meeting costs incurred or to be
incurred in respect of the relevant building in question or any part of it (or
in respect of that building or part and anything else).

10.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations modify the application of  this
paragraph  as it applies in relation to a lease of premises that do not
include a dwelling.

##### No increase in service charge for other tenants

11

Where—

11.a

an amount (“ the original amount ”) would, apart from  this Schedule , be
payable by a tenant under a lease of premises in a relevant building, and

11.b

a greater amount would (apart from  this paragraph ) be payable under the
lease as a result of  this Schedule ,

the lease has effect as if the amount payable were the original amount.

##### Recovery of service charge amounts from landlords

12

12.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for and in connection
with the recovery, from a prescribed relevant landlord, of any amount that is
not recoverable under a lease as a result of  this Schedule .

12.2

In  this paragraph  “ relevant landlord ”, in relation to a lease, means the
landlord under the lease or any superior landlord.

##### Presumption: qualifying lease

13

13.1

This paragraph  applies in relation to a lease that meets the conditions in
paragraphs  (a)  to  (c)  of section 119 (2) .

13.2

The lease is to be treated for the purposes of  this Schedule  as a qualifying
lease unless—

13.2.a

the landlord under the lease has taken all reasonable steps (and any
prescribed steps) to obtain a qualifying lease certificate from a tenant under
the lease, and

13.2.b

no such certificate has been provided to the landlord.

13.3

In  this paragraph  “ qualifying lease certificate ” means a certificate,
complying with any prescribed requirements, that the condition in section 119
(2) (d)  was met in relation to the lease at the qualifying time.

13.4

The requirements that may be prescribed include requirements as to—

13.4.a

the information to be provided in the certificate,

13.4.b

the form of the certificate, and

13.4.c

the execution of the certificate.

##### Presumptions relating to landlord under qualifying lease

14

14.1

The person who was the landlord under a qualifying lease at the qualifying
time (“the relevant landlord”) is to be treated for the purposes of  this
Schedule  as having met the contribution condition (as defined by paragraph  3
) unless the landlord under the lease provides to the tenant under the lease a
certificate, complying with any prescribed requirements, that the relevant
landlord did not meet that condition.

14.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that (in some or all cases)
the condition in paragraph  2 (2)  is to be treated for the purposes of  this
Schedule  as met in relation to a lease to which paragraph  2  applies unless
the landlord under the lease provides to the tenant under the lease a
certificate that complies with any prescribed requirements.

14.3

The requirements that may be prescribed include requirements as to—

14.3.a

the information to be provided in the certificate,

14.3.b

the form of the certificate, and

14.3.c

the execution of the certificate.

##### Information from tenants

15

15.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision requiring a tenant
under a qualifying lease to give prescribed information or documents to the
landlord under the lease or any superior landlord.

15.2

The regulations may provide that the information or documents are to be given
in a prescribed way.

##### Information from landlords

16

16.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision requiring a relevant
landlord to give prescribed information or documents to a relevant tenant or
other prescribed person.

16.2

Information or documents may be prescribed if they relate to any matter with
which  this Schedule  is concerned.

16.3

The regulations may require the information or documents to be given in a
prescribed way.

16.4

The regulations may provide that where a relevant landlord fails to comply
with the regulations, prescribed costs—

16.4.a

are not to be regarded as relevant costs to be taken into account in
determining the amount of a service charge payable under a relevant lease, and

16.4.b

must not be met from a relevant reserve fund.

16.5

The regulations may make provision for and in connection with an application
to the First-tier Tribunal for an order—

16.5.a

determining whether a relevant landlord has failed to comply with the
regulations, and

16.5.b

if so, requiring the relevant landlord to provide specified information or
documents to a specified person by a specified time.

“Specified” here means specified in the order.

16.6

Nothing in sub-paragraph  (5)  limits the effect of regulations made by virtue
of sub-paragraph  (4) .

16.7

Information or documents may be specified in an order under sub-paragraph  (5)
only if the regulations require them to be provided to the specified person.

16.8

In  this paragraph —

“ relevant costs ” has the meaning given by section 18 of the Landlord and
Tenant Act 1985 (and this applies in relation to a lease of premises that does
not include a dwelling as it applies in relation to a lease of a dwelling); “
relevant landlord ” means a landlord under a relevant lease; “ relevant lease
” means a lease of premises in a relevant building; “ relevant reserve fund ”
has the meaning given by paragraph  10 ; “ relevant tenant ” means a tenant
under a relevant lease.

17

In section 21 of the Landlord and Tenant Act 1985 (service charge
information), in subsection (6A) (inserted by section 112), after “2022)”
insert  “or relevant buildings (as defined by section 117 of that Act)” .

##### Anti-avoidance

18

A covenant or agreement (whenever made) is void insofar as it purports to
exclude or limit any provision made under  this Schedule .

                 The new homes ombudsman scheme

Section 137 (1)

##### Appointment of the new homes ombudsman

1

The scheme must include provision about the appointment of the new homes
ombudsman.

##### Membership

2

2.1

The scheme must include provision about the procedure for becoming and
remaining a member of the scheme.

2.2

That provision may include—

2.2.a

a requirement to pay a fee;

2.2.b

a requirement to provide information;

2.2.c

a requirement to have internal procedures in place for the handling and
resolution of complaints about matters in relation to which complaints may be
made under the scheme.

2.3

If the scheme includes a requirement mentioned in  sub-paragraph (2) (c) , it
must also include a requirement to publish the procedures.

3

The scheme may provide for different categories of member and the provision
mentioned in  paragraph 2  (including provision about fees) may differ as
between such categories.

##### Fees

4

The fees payable by a member may be calculated by reference to the total of
the costs incurred, or to be incurred, in the operation of the scheme
(including costs unconnected with the member in question).

5

Where a scheme is maintained by a person other than—

5.a

the Secretary of State, or

5.b

a person acting on behalf of the Secretary of State,

fees may be set at a level such that the total of all fees payable by members
exceeds the total of the costs of operating the scheme.

##### Complaints under the scheme: subject matter and procedure

6

The scheme must include provision about—

6.a

the matters in relation to which complaints against members of the scheme may
be made under the scheme (which may include complaints about non-compliance
with a code of practice issued or approved under section 142), and

6.b

the procedure for making complaints under the scheme.

7

The provision mentioned in  paragraph 6 (b) —

7.a

must not include any requirement to pay a fee;

7.b

may differ as between different categories of member;

7.c

may include provision about the use of any internal procedures a member has in
place for the handling or resolution of complaints.

##### Complaints under the scheme: investigation and determination

8

8.1

The scheme must include provision about the investigation and determination by
the new homes ombudsman of complaints made under the scheme.

8.2

That provision must include provision—

8.2.a

requiring the new homes ombudsman, in determining a complaint, to have regard
to any code of practice issued or approved under section 142,

8.2.b

for the new homes ombudsman to require members of the scheme to provide
information, and

8.2.c

for the new homes ombudsman to require members of the scheme to provide
complainants whose complaints are determined to be well-founded with any one
or more of the forms of redress in  paragraph 9 .

9

The forms of redress are—

9.a

paying compensation;

9.b

making an apology;

9.c

providing an explanation;

9.d

taking such other action in the interests of the complainant as the new homes
ombudsman may specify.

##### Enforcement of determinations

10

10.1

The scheme must include provision about the enforcement of determinations made
by the new homes ombudsman.

10.2

That provision may include provision for the expulsion of a member from the
scheme (and the requirement in section 137 (1) (a)  is not to be read as
preventing the new homes ombudsman scheme from including such provision).

10.3

If provision described in  sub-paragraph (2)  is included in the scheme,
provision must also be made about the circumstances in which an expelled
member can rejoin the scheme.

##### Making of recommendations

11

11.1

The scheme must include provision about the making of improvement
recommendations by the new homes ombudsman where following the investigation
of a complaint the ombudsman identifies widespread or regular unacceptable
standards of conduct or standards of quality of work on the part of members of
the scheme.

11.2

“Improvement recommendations” are recommendations about changes that members
may make in order to improve standards of conduct or standards of quality of
work.

##### Predecessor schemes

12

The scheme must include provision about the acceptance and handling of
complaints transferred from a scheme previously available under section 136
but which is no longer available.

##### Complaints about the scheme

13

The scheme must include provision about how complaints about the operation of
the scheme may be made by—

13.a

members of the scheme, and

13.b

persons who have asked for a complaint to be investigated under the scheme.

##### Co-operation

14

14.1

The scheme may include provision about co-operation with persons who exercise
functions under other redress schemes and, in particular, provision about
arrangements for a person exercising functions under the scheme to do so
jointly with a person exercising functions under another redress scheme,
including for the making of joint determinations by the new homes ombudsman
and an independent person making determinations under another redress scheme.

14.2

In  sub-paragraph (1) , “ redress scheme ” has the same meaning as in section
137.

##### Provision of information

15

15.1

Where the scheme is maintained by a person other than the Secretary of State,
the scheme must include provision about the provision of information to the
Secretary of State, the Welsh Ministers, the Scottish Ministers and the
relevant Northern Ireland department.

15.2

In this paragraph, “ the relevant Northern Ireland department ” means the
Northern Ireland department designated for the purposes of this paragraph by
the First Minister and deputy First Minister acting jointly.

##### Reports

16

The scheme must include provision about the making of reports on the operation
of the scheme.

If at any stage in the course of conducting an investigation under the new

;

Construction products regulations

Section 146

##### Introductory

1

1.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision in relation to the
marketing and supply of construction products in the United Kingdom.

1.2

Regulations under  this paragraph  are called “construction products
regulations”.

##### General safety requirements

2

2.1

Construction products regulations may—

2.1.a

prohibit the marketing or supply of construction products which are not safe
products;

2.1.b

impose other requirements for the purpose of securing that construction
products which are not safe products are not marketed or supplied;

2.1.c

impose requirements in relation to the marketing or supply of construction
products which are safe products.

2.2

For the purposes of  this paragraph  a construction product is a “safe
product” if, under normal or reasonably foreseeable conditions of use, and
taking into account any matters specified for the purposes of  this paragraph
by construction products regulations—

2.2.a

the product does not present any risk to the health or safety of persons, or

2.2.b

if it does, the risk is as low as it can be compatibly with using the product.

2.3

In  this paragraph —

“ use ” includes storage, transportation or packaging; “ reasonably
foreseeable conditions ” include reasonably foreseeable circumstances in which
the construction product might come under stress (for example, a fire).

##### Construction products with designated standards or technical assessments

3

Construction products regulations may make provision for and in relation to—

3.a

designated standards for construction products (see  paragraph 4 );

3.b

technical assessments for construction products (see  paragraph 5 ).

4

4.1

Provision under  paragraph 3 (a)  (designated standards) may include
provision—

4.1.a

for the designation by the Secretary of State of standards prepared in
accordance with the regulations or the 2011 Regulation;

4.1.b

for the designation by the Secretary of State of EU harmonised standards or
international standards;

4.1.c

for EU harmonised standards or international standards to be designated
standards.

4.2

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1) (a)  may include provision as to—

4.2.a

the persons by whom standards may be proposed;

4.2.b

the procedure by which and persons by whom standards are to be prepared;

4.2.c

the matters to be covered by a standard.

5

5.1

Provision under  paragraph 3 (b)  (technical assessments) may include
provision as to the procedure by which and persons by whom technical
assessments are to be issued.

5.2

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1)  may include provision for assessment
bodies to issue technical assessments on the basis of assessment documents
developed or adopted by them, and in particular provision—

5.2.a

for the designation of assessment bodies by the Secretary of State;

5.2.b

as to the functions, operation and funding of assessment bodies;

5.2.c

as to the contents of assessment documents and the procedure by which they are
developed or adopted.

6

Construction products regulations may—

6.a

impose requirements on persons carrying out activities in relation to
construction products for which there are designated standards or technical
assessments under the regulations (see  paragraph 7 );

6.b

confer powers on relevant authorities to impose requirements on such persons
(see  paragraph 8 ).

7

7.1

Provision under  paragraph 6 (a)  (imposition of requirements) may include
provision for the imposition of requirements relating to—

7.1.a

declarations of performance in respect of products which are or are to be
marketed;

7.1.b

the making of other statements or claims in relation to the performance of
products which are or are to be marketed;

7.1.c

the marking or packaging of products;

7.1.d

the provision of information, including information about risk, to persons to
whom products are supplied;

7.1.e

the monitoring, assessment and verification of product performance, including
sample testing;

7.1.f

the storage and transportation of products;

7.1.g

the taking of corrective action, including withdrawal of products from the
market and recall of products from persons to whom they have been supplied;

7.1.h

recording and investigating complaints;

7.1.i

the production and retention of documentation or samples;

7.1.j

the notification of risks to relevant authorities;

7.1.k

information which must or may be provided to relevant authorities;

7.1.l

co-operation with relevant authorities;

7.1.m

the appointment of authorised representatives by persons carrying out
activities in relation to construction products.

7.2

Provision about declarations of performance under  sub-paragraph (1) (a)  may
include provision as to—

7.2.a

the technical documentation to be prepared in relation to a declaration of
performance;

7.2.b

the content of a declaration of performance;

7.2.c

the form of a declaration of performance;

7.2.d

how a declaration of performance is to be supplied or made available.

7.3

Provision about the marking of products under  sub-paragraph (1) (c)  may
include provision as to—

7.3.a

the form and content of any marking;

7.3.b

circumstances in which products must or must not be marked.

7.4

Provision about the monitoring, assessment and verification of product
performance under  sub-paragraph (1) (e)  may include provision as to—

7.4.a

the carrying out of testing and other tasks by approved bodies;

7.4.b

when and how a body may become or cease to be an approved body;

7.4.c

the assessment and monitoring of approved bodies.

7.5

Requirements which may be imposed on persons carrying out activities in
relation to construction products under  paragraph 6 (a)  may also be imposed
on the authorised representatives of such persons.

8

8.1

Provision under  paragraph 6 (b)  (conferral of powers) may include provision
conferring powers on a relevant authority to impose requirements on persons
carrying out activities in relation to construction products in circumstances
where—

8.1.a

there has been no failure to comply with requirements imposed under  paragraph
6 (a) , but

8.1.b

in the view of the relevant authority the products nevertheless risk causing
death or serious injury to any person.

8.2

The powers referred to in  sub-paragraph (1)  may include powers by notice to—

8.2.a

require a person to warn others of the risks attaching to a product;

8.2.b

require the marking of a product in respect of the risks attaching to it;

8.2.c

suspend for a specified period or prohibit the marketing or supply of a
product (or suspend or prohibit the marketing and supply of the product
without the consent of a specified person);

8.2.d

require the withdrawal of a product from the market;

8.2.e

require the recall of a product from persons to whom it has been supplied.

8.3

Provision under  sub-paragraph (2)  may include provision for appeals against
a notice.

9

Construction products regulations may include any provision—

9.a

which is made in the 2011 Regulation or the 2019 or 2020 Regulations
immediately after IP completion day, or

9.b

which relates to any matter in respect of which provision is made in that
Regulation or those Regulations immediately after that time.

##### Safety-critical products

10

10.1

For the purposes of  this Schedule , “ safety-critical products ” means
construction products which are included in a list contained in construction
products regulations.

10.2

A construction product may only be included in a list under  sub-paragraph (1)
if—

10.2.a

in the view of the Secretary of State any failure of the product would risk
causing death or serious injury to any person, and

10.2.b

the product is not one for which there are—

10.2.b.i

designated standards under  paragraph 3 (a) , or

10.2.b.ii

standards which are designated standards for the purposes of the 2011
Regulation.

10.3

Before including a construction product in the list, or amending the list, the
Secretary of State must consult such persons as the Secretary of State
considers appropriate.

11

11.1

Construction products regulations may make provision for and in relation to
standards for safety-critical products (“safety-critical standards”).

11.2

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1)  may include provision as to—

11.2.a

the persons by whom safety-critical standards may be proposed;

11.2.b

the procedure by which and persons by whom safety-critical standards are to be
prepared;

11.2.c

the matters to be covered by a safety-critical standard.

12

Construction products regulations may—

12.a

impose requirements on persons carrying out activities in relation to safety-
critical products for which there are safety-critical standards under the
regulations (see  paragraph 13 );

12.b

confer powers on relevant authorities to impose requirements on such persons
(see  paragraph 14 ).

13

Provision under  paragraph 12 (a)  (imposition of requirements) may include
any provision referred to in  paragraph 7 .

14

14.1

Provision under  paragraph 12 (b)  (conferral of powers) may include provision
conferring powers on a relevant authority to impose requirements on persons
carrying out activities in relation to construction products in circumstances
where—

14.1.a

there has been no failure to comply with requirements imposed under  paragraph
12 (a) , but

14.1.b

in the view of the relevant authority the products nevertheless risk causing
death or serious injury to any person.

14.2

The powers referred to in  sub-paragraph (1)  include powers by notice to—

14.2.a

require a person to warn others of the risks attaching to a product;

14.2.b

require the marking of a product in respect of the risks attaching to it;

14.2.c

suspend for a specified period or prohibit the marketing or supply of a
product (or suspend or prohibit the marketing and supply of the product
without the consent of a specified person);

14.2.d

require the withdrawal of a product from the market;

14.2.e

require the recall of a product from persons to whom it has been supplied.

14.3

Provision under sub-paragraph (2) may include provision for appeals against a
notice.

##### Enforcement

15

15.1

Construction products regulations may make provision for and in relation to—

15.1.a

monitoring compliance with construction product requirements and investigating
suspected non-compliance;

15.1.b

securing compliance with construction product requirements;

15.1.c

sanctions for—

15.1.c.i

non-compliance or suspected non-compliance with construction product
requirements;

15.1.c.ii

obstruction of, failure to assist or co-operate with, or provision of false or
misleading information to, persons carrying out construction product
functions.

15.2

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1) (a)  may include—

15.2.a

provision for relevant authorities to carry out, or secure the carrying out
of, market surveillance and test purchases;

15.2.b

provision for relevant authorities to enter, inspect and search premises and
to seize and retain products or evidence of non-compliance with construction
product requirements (including provision for the payment of compensation);

15.2.c

provision requiring the retention and provision of information (including
provision for relevant authorities to require the provision of information to
them).

15.3

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1) (b)  may include provision conferring
powers on a relevant authority by notice to—

15.3.a

require a person to warn others of the risks attaching to a product;

15.3.b

require the marking of a product in respect of the risks attaching to it;

15.3.c

suspend for a specified period or prohibit the marketing or supply of a
product (or suspend or prohibit the marketing and supply of the product
without the consent of a specified person);

15.3.d

require the withdrawal of a product from the market;

15.3.e

require the recall of a product from persons to whom it has been supplied;

15.3.f

require a person to do or cease to do anything so as to end non-compliance or
suspected non-compliance with construction product requirements.

15.4

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1) (b)  may also include—

15.4.a

provision for—

15.4.a.i

a relevant authority to accept undertakings relating to compliance with
construction product requirements instead of taking other enforcement action;

15.4.a.ii

sanctions for non-compliance or suspected non-compliance with such
undertakings;

15.4.b

provision for the forfeiture of products by court order (or, in Scotland,
order of the sheriff).

15.5

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1) (c)  or  (4) (a) (ii)  may include—

15.5.a

provision creating criminal offences;

15.5.b

in relation to England and Wales and Northern Ireland, provision for the
prosecution by relevant authorities of criminal offences created under
paragraph (a) ;

15.5.c

provision conferring powers on relevant authorities to impose civil sanctions
(including fines).

15.6

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1) (b)  or  (c)  or (4)(a)(ii) may include
provision for appeals against anything done by a relevant authority under that
provision.

15.7

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1)  may include any provision—

15.7.a

which is made by the 2013 Regulations, or

15.7.b

which relates to any matter in respect of which provision is made by the 2013
Regulations.

##### Costs

16

16.1

Construction products regulations may make provision for a relevant authority
to impose charges on a person carrying out activities in relation to
construction products, or an authorised representative of such a person, in
respect of the exercise of the relevant authority’s construction product
functions in relation to such a person.

16.2

The regulations may include provision about—

16.2.a

who is liable to pay a charge;

16.2.b

the circumstances in which a charge is payable;

16.2.c

the amount of a charge (including how an amount is to be calculated);

16.2.d

reductions and exemptions;

16.2.e

waivers;

16.2.f

how and when a charge is to be paid;

16.2.g

the collection and recovery of payments;

16.2.h

interest payable on outstanding payments;

16.2.i

the resolution of disputes (including appeals).

16.3

Provision under  this paragraph  may confer a discretion on the relevant
authority.

##### Information

17

17.1

Construction products regulations may, in connection with the exercise by
relevant authorities of their construction product functions, make provision
for and in relation to—

17.1.a

the provision of information by relevant authorities to—

17.1.a.i

other relevant authorities, or

17.1.a.ii

persons specified, or of a description specified, in construction products
regulations;

17.1.b

the provision of information to relevant authorities by—

17.1.b.i

persons specified, or of a description specified, in construction products
regulations, or

17.1.b.ii

other persons identified by relevant authorities.

17.2

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1)  may include provision—

17.2.a

as to the circumstances in which information may or must be provided (which
may include circumstances in which the information could not otherwise have
been lawfully provided or disclosed);

17.2.b

as to how information may or must be provided;

17.2.c

as to the uses to which information provided may be put;

17.2.d

for the purpose of preventing the further disclosure of information (including
provision for the creation of criminal offences);

17.2.e

for the purpose of securing that there is (taking into account any power or
duty to provide information under the regulations) no contravention of the
data protection legislation.

18

18.1

Construction products regulations may make provision for and in relation to
the publication by relevant authorities of information held by them in
connection with their construction product functions.

18.2

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1)  may include provision as to—

18.2.a

the circumstances in which information may or must be published (which may
include circumstances in which the information could not otherwise have been
lawfully published);

18.2.b

how, where and in what form information may or must be published.

19

19.1

Construction products regulations may make provision prohibiting the
disclosure of information held by relevant authorities in connection with
their construction product functions.

19.2

Provision under  sub-paragraph (1)  may include provision for the creation of
criminal offences.

##### General and supplementary

20

20.1

Construction products regulations may make—

20.1.a

different provision for different purposes;

20.1.b

different provision for or in relation to different parts of the United
Kingdom;

20.1.c

transitional, transitory, consequential and supplementary provision or
savings.

20.2

The provision made by  paragraphs 2  to  19  does not limit the power
conferred by  paragraph 1 .

21

21.1

Construction products regulations may make provision by repealing, amending or
re-enacting—

21.1.a

  assimilated   law (and in particular the 2011 Regulation and the 2013
Regulations);

21.1.b

the 2019 and 2020 Regulations;

21.1.c

any other enactment other than an Act.

21.2

Construction products regulations may under paragraph  20 (1) (c)  make
consequential provision amending section 148 (liability relating to
construction products), which may in particular include the omission or
amendment of subsection (2)(b) and (c) of that section.

22

22.1

Where construction products regulations contain provision creating a criminal
offence, the provision must have the effect that—

22.1.a

the offence is—

22.1.a.i

triable summarily only, or

22.1.a.ii

triable summarily or on indictment,

22.1.b

the offence is punishable only—

22.1.b.i

with a fine, or

22.1.b.ii

with a term of imprisonment or a fine (or both),

22.1.c

where the offence is triable summarily only, any fine with which the offence
is punishable in Scotland or Northern Ireland does not exceed level 5 on the
standard scale,

22.1.d

where the offence is triable summarily or on indictment, any fine with which
the offence is punishable on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern
Ireland does not exceed the statutory maximum, and

22.1.e

any term of imprisonment with which the offence is punishable on summary
conviction does not exceed—

22.1.e.i

in England and Wales, the relevant period,

22.1.e.ii

in Scotland, 12 months, and

22.1.e.iii

in Northern Ireland, 6 months.

22.2

In  sub-paragraph (1) (e) (i) , the “ relevant period ” means—

22.2.a

in relation to an offence that is triable only summarily—

22.2.a.i

where the offence is committed before the coming into force of section 281 of
the Criminal Justice Act 2003, 6 months, and

22.2.a.ii

where the offence is committed after that time, 51 weeks;

22.2.b

in relation to an offence that is triable summarily or on indictment—

22.2.b.i

where the offence is committed before the coming into force of paragraph 24(2)
of Schedule 22 to the Sentencing Act 2020, 6 months, and

22.2.b.ii

where the offence is committed after that time, 12 months.

##### Procedure

23

23.1

Construction products regulations are to be made by statutory instrument.

23.2

Construction products regulations which contain provision specified in  sub-
paragraph (3)  (with or without other provision) may not be made unless a
draft of the instrument containing them has been laid before, and approved by
resolution of, each House of Parliament.

23.3

The provision referred to in  sub-paragraph (2)  is—

23.3.a

the first provision to be made under  paragraph 10 (1)  (list of safety-
critical products);

23.3.b

provision omitting a construction product from the list of safety-critical
products under paragraph  10 (1) ;

23.3.c

provision creating a criminal offence;

23.3.d

. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .

23.3.e

provision under paragraph 21 (2)  (consequential provision relating to
liability for construction products).

23.4

A statutory instrument containing construction products regulations to which
the requirements specified in  sub-paragraph (2)  do not apply is subject to
annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

##### Interpretation

24

In  this Schedule —

“ the 2011 Regulation ” means  Regulation (EU) No. 305/2011  (regulation
laying down harmonised conditions for the marketing of construction products);
“ the 2013 Regulations ” means the Construction Products Regulations 2013 (
S.I. 2013/1387 ); “ the 2019 Regulations ” means the Construction Products
(Amendment etc.) (EU Exit) Regulations 2019 ( S.I. 2019/465 ); “ the 2020
Regulations ” means the Construction Products (Amendment etc.) (EU Exit)
Regulations 2020 ( S.I. 2020/1359 ); “ authorised representative ” means a
person of a description specified in the regulations who is authorised to act
on behalf of a person carrying out an activity in relation to construction
products; “ construction product ” has the meaning specified in construction
products regulations; “ construction product functions ”, in relation to a
relevant authority, means— the authority’s functions under construction
products regulations, the 2011 Regulation or the 2019 or 2020 Regulations
(including functions relating to the provision or receipt of information), and
any other functions of the authority relating to construction product
requirements; “ construction product requirements ” means requirements imposed
by or under construction products regulations, the 2011 Regulation or the 2019
or 2020 Regulations; “ construction products regulations ” has the meaning
given in  paragraph 1 (2) ; “ data protection legislation ” has the same
meaning as in the Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act); “ EU
harmonised standard ” means a harmonised standard adopted at any time by a
standardisation body of the European Union; “ international standard ” means a
standard adopted by an international standardising body (which for these
purposes has the same meaning as it has for the purposes of the Agreement on
Technical Barriers to Trade, part of Annex 1A to the agreement establishing
the World Trade Organisation signed at Marrakesh on 16 April 1994, as modified
from time to time); “ local authority ” means— a county or district council in
England, a London borough council, the Common Council of the City of London,
the Council of the Isles of Scilly, a county or county borough council in
Wales, a council constituted under section 2 of the Local Government etc
(Scotland) Act 1994, and a district council in Northern Ireland; references to
the “ marketing ” of products are to making them available on the market in
the United Kingdom; “ persons carrying out activities in relation to
construction products ” include (without limitation)— a manufacturer of
construction products, a person who markets or supplies construction products
to others, and a person who imports construction products into the United
Kingdom for use, marketing or supply; “ relevant authority ” means— the
Secretary of State or other Minister of the Crown, and a local authority
(including, in England, Wales and Scotland, a local authority in its capacity
as a local weights and measures authority); “ requirement ” includes a
prohibition or restriction; “ safety-critical products ” has the meaning given
in  paragraph 10 ; “ technical assessment ” means a documented assessment of
the performance of a construction product.
